The diagnostic message links to design.md § `#[non_exhaustive]` for Evolvable Public Types so a first-time reader sees the rationale. **New `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackageLiteral`** in `src/typechecker.rs`; mapped to `E0241` in `src/cli.rs`'s typechecker error-code table (the slot following `ConflictingImpl: E0240`). **Test surface (6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice4_*`)**: `cross_package_literal_rejected` (the headline negative — stdlib-origin `#[non_exhaustive] pub struct Config` constructed via literal in user code fires the slice-4 diagnostic, with the symbolic code, the struct name, and the `Config.new(...)` constructor fix-it all surfaced in the message), `same_package_literal_accepted` (positive pin — both decl and call user-origin → no diagnostic), `non_exhaustive_off_no_diagnostic` (rejection keys on the attribute, not the cross-package boundary alone — a stdlib-origin `pub struct` without `#[non_exhaustive]` is fine), `stdlib_internal_use_accepted` (defining-package internal use — both decl and constructor are stdlib-origin → no diagnostic; the defining package keeps exhaustive literal access), `struct_info_carries_flag` (plumbing pin — `StructInfo.is_non_exhaustive` and `defining_stdlib_origin` round-trip from the AST through env-building; pins both flags on two distinct structs in one Program), `cross_package_error_code_is_e0241` (pins the `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackageLiteral` discriminant is produced under the rule conditions — `cli.rs`'s match exhaustiveness check guarantees the `E0241` code surfaces in JSON output). **Test helper `typecheck_with_stdlib_origin_on_structs`**: flips `stdlib_origin = true` on every `StructDef` after parse, leaving `Function`s user-origin, mirroring the baked-stdlib + user-code mix the actual stdlib path produces. The same shape `src/prelude.rs::baked_item_for` uses; the test helper keeps the construction inline so each test reads top-to-bottom. **Pattern half (shipped 2026-05-17).** Enabling change: `PatternKind::Struct` gains a `has_rest: bool` field at `src/ast/patterns.rs`, populated by the parser when `..` appears in the field list. New parser helper `parse_struct_pattern_fields` in `src/parser/patterns.rs` walks the field list, accepting `..` once at any position (preferred: last) and emitting `E_REST_PATTERN_DUPLICATE` on a second occurrence and `E_REST_PATTERN_NOT_LAST` on a field-after-rest. Both struct-pattern parse sites (single-segment `Name { ... }` and qualified `Path.Name { ... }`) route through the helper; the third site (parameter-pattern grammar in `src/parser/items.rs`) keeps `has_rest: false` since params are irrefutable and `..` is meaningless there. **Cross-package pattern check** in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs`: BOTH `check_pattern_against` (match-arm route) AND `bind_pattern_types` (let-binding route) emit `error[E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_PATTERN]` (new `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackagePattern`, mapped to `E0243` in `src/cli.rs`) when `is_non_exhaustive && defining_stdlib_origin && !current_fn_stdlib_origin && !has_rest`. Both routes are exercised — `let Config { x } = c;` and `match c { Config { x } => ... }` both fire the rule, mirroring the slice-4 literal half's invariant that the cross-package check fires wherever exhaustive-shape destructuring happens. **Formatter / lowering** (`src/formatter/patterns.rs`, `src/exhaustive.rs`, `src/interpreter/pattern_match.rs`, `src/resolver/resolve_refs.rs`): all sites that destructure `PatternKind::Struct` updated to thread `has_rest` through. Formatter round-trips the `..` marker so `karac fmt` preserves rest-patterns. Exhaustiveness lowering already treated missing-field shorthand as `Pat::Wildcard`, so `..` produces an identical lowering — no semantic change to the existing Maranget machinery. Interpreter pattern-matcher never required all fields to be enumerated, so the runtime check is `has_rest`-independent. **Test surface (7 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::rest_pattern_struct_*` + 6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice4_pattern_*`).** Parser: bare `{ .. }`, field + rest, field + rest + trailing comma, no-rest sets flag false, field-after-rest rejected with `E_REST_PATTERN_NOT_LAST`, duplicate-rest rejected, qualified-path struct pattern with `..`. Typechecker: cross-package without `..` rejected (let-binding route), cross-package with `..` accepted, same-package without `..` accepted, no-attribute + cross-package accepted, match-arm route also rejected (pins both check sites fire), stdlib-internal use accepted. **Cross-package today.** The only inter-package boundary the compiler currently tracks is stdlib-vs-user (`stdlib_origin`); the slice-4 check leverages this as the v1 cross-package proxy. When richer per-package boundaries land (cross-user-package isolation), the comparison at `infer_struct_literal` widens to `defining_package_id != current_package_id` without re-flowing through `StructInfo` or the fn-context plumbing. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Blocks slice 5** (enum exhaustiveness — same fn-stdlib-origin context will be consulted on the match scrutinee's type) **[Resolved by slice 5 below — shipped 2026-05-17.]** **and slice 6** (stdlib hygiene lint — once the lint registry lands, the lint reads `is_non_exhaustive` to flag stdlib `pub enum` lacking the attribute).

  - [x] **Slice 5 — cross-package enum exhaustiveness wildcard rule shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Exhaustiveness checker — when matching on a value whose enum type is `#[non_exhaustive]` and defined in a different package, the wildcard requirement is unconditional regardless of which variants are covered; emit the existing non-exhaustive-match diagnostic with a fix-it inserting `_ => todo!(\"handle new variant\")`. The check is package-relative: same-package matches are checked normally."* Builds directly on slice 4's `current_fn_stdlib_origin` plumbing — the `EnumInfo` side of the same plumbing replicates the `StructInfo` extension. **`EnumInfo` extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs`: `is_non_exhaustive: bool` + `defining_stdlib_origin: bool`, mirroring the `StructInfo` shape from slice 4. Populated in both `EnumInfo` construction sites in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs`: the prelude-bake pre-pass and `env_add_enum`. **Check site** in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::check_exhaustiveness`: before invoking the existing `check_match_exhaustive`, if the scrutinee is a `Type::Named` of a `#[non_exhaustive]` enum from another package AND the user is in a non-stdlib fn AND the arms contain no catch-all, emit `error[E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_MATCH]` naming the enum and surfacing the `_ => todo!("handle new variant")` fix-it. The check fires BEFORE the strict-rule `check_match_exhaustive` so a missing wildcard surfaces as the slice-5 diagnostic, not as a generic "missing variant Vn" tail (which would mislead the author into adding the listed variant rather than `_`). `return` after the slice-5 emission to skip the strict rule for the same match (the cross-package rule subsumes it). **Catch-all detection** via two new free functions at the bottom of `patterns.rs`: `arms_contain_catchall(arms, &variant_names)` walks each arm's pattern under the no-guard predicate and dispatches to `pattern_is_catchall`. **Variant-aware catch-all classification**: `PatternKind::Binding(name)` is the surface for BOTH a fresh binding (`other => ...`, a catch-all) AND a unit-variant constructor (`Read => ...`, NOT a catch-all — the parser can't distinguish at parse time). The helper threads the scrutinee enum's variant-name set so `Binding(name)` counts as catch-all iff `name` is NOT a known variant. `Or` patterns and `AtBinding` chains recurse. Guarded arms (`x if cond =>`) are never catch-alls because the guard can fail. **New `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackageMatch`** mapped to `E0242` in `src/cli.rs` (the slot following `NonExhaustiveCrossPackageLiteral: E0241`). **Test surface (8 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice5_*`)**: `cross_package_match_without_wildcard_rejected` (headline negative — every variant listed but no `_` arm fires `E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_MATCH` with the symbolic code, the enum name, the `_ =>` fix-it, AND the `todo!(...)` placeholder), `cross_package_match_with_wildcard_accepted` (positive twin — same match with `_ => 0` added typechecks cleanly), `same_package_match_uses_strict_rule` (covers all variants without `_` → fine, the strict rule doesn't fire because all variants are listed), `same_package_strict_rule_fires_on_missing_variant` (missing variant + no wildcard → the EXISTING `NonExhaustiveMatch` fires, NOT the new cross-package rule — local code catches "you added a variant and forgot to handle it"), `cross_package_match_without_attribute_uses_strict_rule` (plain `pub enum` without `#[non_exhaustive]` continues to use the strict rule even when defining-package and use-site differ), `stdlib_internal_match_accepted` (the defining package retains exhaustive-match access — both enum and fn `stdlib_origin = true`), `bare_binding_arm_counts_as_catchall` (the variant-aware classification — `other => ...` is a catch-all because `other` is not a variant), `enum_info_carries_flag` (plumbing pin — both flags round-trip from AST through env-building on two distinct enums). **Test helper `typecheck_with_stdlib_origin_on_enums`** mirrors the slice-4 struct helper: flips `EnumDef.stdlib_origin = true` after parse, leaves `Function`s user-origin. **What slice 5 does *not* do.** No `NonExhaustiveMatch` deprecation — the strict rule continues to fire same-package (the slice-5 rule is package-relative, layered on top). No support for enum pattern-position wildcard (still surfaced via the existing `_` mechanism). No machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` field — slice 7 polish covers fix-it text rendering. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks** the broader same-fn-stdlib-origin design — slices 4 and 5 share the same `current_fn_stdlib_origin` context, validating the design for slice 4's deferred pattern half.

  - [x] **Slice 6 — stdlib hygiene lint `missing_non_exhaustive` shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Stdlib hygiene lint (new) — `missing_non_exhaustive` warning that fires on a stdlib `pub enum` whose name ends in `Error` or whose declared role is 'stdlib error enum' and which lacks `#[non_exhaustive]`; the lint is `deny`-by-default for stdlib crates and `allow` for user code."* The "declared role" half is reviewer judgement (not a hard rule baked into the compiler, per the spec); the lint heuristic is the name suffix. **Lint registry entry** in `src/lints.rs`: `missing_non_exhaustive` with `default_level: LintLevel::Deny`. Registry-coverage test gets the name pinned. **New `TypeErrorKind::MissingNonExhaustive`** in `src/typechecker.rs`; mapped to `W0246` in both `src/cli.rs` code tables (the W prefix reflects the underlying lint carrier; the deny-by-default level surfaces it as an error under `severity: "error"` by way of the error-loop emit path, mirroring how `Deprecated` is routed). **Emission pre-pass** in `src/typechecker.rs::emit_missing_non_exhaustive_warnings`: walks `program.items`, for each `Item::EnumDef(e)` where `e.stdlib_origin && e.is_pub && e.name.ends_with("Error") && !e.is_non_exhaustive` pushes the enum's `lint_overrides` as the innermost cascade frame and emits via `type_lint_warning` so `#[allow(missing_non_exhaustive)]` on the enum self-suppresses (same pattern as `emit_unknown_lint_warnings` from slice 4b follow-up, where the warning's natural span sits outside the item's body and a span-based cascade walker would otherwise miss it). Wired into `check()` immediately after `emit_unknown_lint_warnings()`. **Spec-correct "allow for user code"** comes free from the check site's `stdlib_origin` gate: the rule does not examine user enums at all, so no build-wide CLI default is needed (CLI build-wide defaults `-A` / `-W` / `-D NAME` land in slice 4b polish). **Test surface (8 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice6_*`)**: `stdlib_error_enum_without_attr_fires` (headline negative — stdlib `pub enum FooError` without the attribute fires `MissingNonExhaustive` with symbolic code, enum name, and attribute mention), `stdlib_error_enum_with_attr_silent` (positive twin), `user_error_enum_silent` (the "allow for user code" surface — user-package `FooError` is not examined), `stdlib_non_error_name_silent` (the name-suffix heuristic — `BarConfig` is silent), `private_enum_silent` (non-pub gating — meaningless without a cross-package boundary), `allow_suppresses_at_enum` (`#[allow(missing_non_exhaustive)]` on the enum routes through the slice-4b cascade and self-suppresses), `warn_demotes_to_warning` (`#[warn(missing_non_exhaustive)]` overrides the deny default and routes to `warnings` instead of `errors`, pinning that the lint goes through `type_lint_warning` rather than `type_error` directly), `lint_is_registered` (registry pin — adding the lint without wiring the check, or vice versa, breaks loudly). **What slice 6 does *not* do.** No `Display` / `Debug` exemption — the rule applies uniformly across all stdlib `Error`-suffixed enums. No build-wide CLI default (slice 4b polish). No fix-it `replacement` text (slice 7 polish). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 7 — machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` text for pattern + match diagnostics shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"diagnostic polish (slice 7 — machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` text for the literal/pattern/match diagnostics)"*. **New `FixIt { span: Span, replacement: String }`** in `src/typechecker.rs` — minimal one-edit surface (a zero-`length` span represents an insertion). **`TypeError` gains `fix_it: Option<FixIt>`** wired through every existing construction site (`type_error` / warning-loop `TypeError {...}` blocks → `None`; new `type_error_with_fix_it` helper threads the edit when the emitter knows one). **CLI JSON wiring** in `src/cli.rs::DiagnosticJson::add`: `DiagEntry` carries `fix_it: Option<&FixIt>`, surfaced as a nested `"fix_it":{"span":{...,"offset":N,"length":N},"replacement":"..."}` object so IDE / formatter consumers can apply the edit without re-parsing the message text. The byte-level `offset` + `length` are included alongside line/column (the existing span shape) so consumers can distinguish insertion (length=0) from replacement uniformly. **Pattern fix-it** in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::non_exhaustive_pattern_fix_it` (free helper at the bottom of the file, alongside `arms_contain_catchall` from slice 5): empty field list → insert `..` at `pattern.span.end - 1` (position of `}`); non-empty → insert `, ..` at `last_field.span.end` (chains onto the existing last field whether or not the source carried a trailing comma). Wired into both pattern emission sites — `check_pattern_against` (match-arm route) and `bind_pattern_types` (let-binding route) — so every cross-package pattern diagnostic carries the fix-it. **Match fix-it** in `non_exhaustive_match_fix_it`: empty arms → insert `_ => panic("handle new variant")` at `match.span.end - 1`; non-empty → insert `, _ => panic("handle new variant")` at `last_arm.span.end`. Wired into the slice-5 emission site in `check_exhaustiveness`. **Kāra-valid placeholder.** The spec's `todo!(...)` rendering (Rust syntax) is replaced by `panic("handle new variant")` — Kāra has no `todo!()` macro, so a machine-applicable fix-it must use the actual stdlib panic-emitter. The slice-5 message text and its pinning test are updated to match; the spec's intent ("placeholder the user fills in with the real handler") is preserved. **Test surface (7 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice7_*`)**: `pattern_fix_it_present_with_fields` (headline pin — non-empty pattern → replacement = `, ..`, zero-length span), `pattern_fix_it_empty_field_list_emits_dot_dot` (empty `Foo {}` → `..`), `pattern_fix_it_anchors_after_last_field` (round-trip — splicing the fix-it in produces a parser-valid program containing `, ..`), `match_fix_it_inserts_wildcard_arm` (replacement contains `_ => panic("handle new variant")`), `match_fix_it_anchors_after_last_arm` (round-trip — splicing into a non-empty match produces a parser-valid program), `unrelated_diagnostics_carry_no_fix_it` (channel hygiene — non-slice-7 diagnostics have `fix_it: None`), `fix_it_type_is_public` (compile-time pin on `karac::typechecker::FixIt` accessibility for IDE consumers). **What slice 7 does *not* do — literal-half fix-it.** The literal site (`E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_LITERAL`) keeps its descriptive message but emits no machine-applicable fix-it: rewriting `Foo { a: 1, b: 2 }` to `Foo.new(a: 1, b: 2)` requires either source-text access (which the typechecker doesn't have) or a multi-edit shape with per-brace spans (which `StructLiteral` AST doesn't carry — only the whole-literal span and per-field spans are available). When richer multi-edit fix-its land (or `StructLiteral` gains `lbrace_span` / `rbrace_span`), the literal-half lands as a two-edit `FixIt` rewriting `{` → `.new(` and `}` → `)`; the surface is forward-compatible (`fix_it` becomes `fix_its: Vec<FixIt>` without touching existing producers). The descriptive message at the literal site still steers to `<Name>.new(...)`. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Closes the `#[non_exhaustive]` epic** — the parent `[~]` flips to `[x]`.

- [x] **`#[deprecated]` attribute + `deprecated` lint shipped 2026-05-17.** Parser surface + AST `Deprecation` payload on all attribute-bearing item kinds + resolver placement-rejection for `impl` blocks and struct fields (slices 1+2+3a) + resolver symbol-table flag-recording (slice 3b) + typechecker use-site warning emission with cascade integration (slice 4) shipped 2026-05-16 / 2026-05-17. Infrastructure is structurally complete — adding `#[deprecated]` to a future stdlib item is a one-attribute drop-in that the slice-4 use-site emission picks up automatically.

  - [->] **Slice 6 — stdlib-canonical-deprecations.** Content slice (apply the attribute to specific stdlib items scheduled for removal). **Reason for deferral.** The stdlib has no items with an identified successor (no migration in flight, no API marked as legacy in `runtime/stdlib/*.kara`); shipping today would be a synthetic annotation, not a real-deprecation pin. **Reopen condition.** First concrete stdlib API scheduled for replacement (canonical pair `<old> → <new>` identified, replacement landed and tested). At that point this sub-bullet flips to `[x]` recording the pair + ship date.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2+3a — parser, AST payload, resolver placement-rejection shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Attribute parser — recognise `#[deprecated]`, the `#[deprecated = \"note\"]` shorthand, and the long form `#[deprecated(note: \"...\", since: \"...\")]`. Both fields optional; `since` is a free string (advisory; not validated against `kara.toml`). Reject unknown keys with `error[E_DEPRECATED_UNKNOWN_FIELD]` enumerating the accepted set."* + *"AST — new `Deprecation { since: Option<String>, note: Option<String>, span: Span }` payload attached to function / struct / enum / ... item nodes; reject the attribute on `impl` blocks (`error[E_DEPRECATED_ON_IMPL]`) and on individual struct fields (`error[E_DEPRECATED_ON_FIELD]` — field-level deprecation is post-v1)."* **AST payload** in `src/ast/items.rs`: new `Deprecation { span, since: Option<String>, note: Option<String> }` struct. New `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>` field on every attribute-bearing item kind: `Function`, `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, `TraitAliasDef`, `MarkerTraitDef`, `DistinctTypeDef`. Defaulted to `None` at every construction site (parser sets from attribute presence; `prelude.rs`'s stubs default `None`; `typechecker/items.rs`'s synthesized trait-method stub defaults `None`; `effectchecker.rs` and `effectchecker/bounds.rs` synthesized trait-method stubs default `None`). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `scan_deprecated_attr(&attributes) -> Option<Deprecation>` helper recognises all three forms — bare `#[deprecated]` (both fields `None`), shorthand `#[deprecated = "note"]` (populates `note`), and long form `#[deprecated(since: "...", note: "...")]` (populates either or both fields per their named-arg presence). Both `name: value` and `name = value` arg-shapes accepted because the underlying attribute parser already produces uniform `AttrArg { name, value }` records. Helper called from every item constructor: `parse_function`, `parse_struct_def`, `parse_enum_def`, `parse_trait_or_alias` (the trait-def tail), `parse_trait_alias_tail`, `parse_marker_trait`, `parse_distinct_type`. **Four parse-time diagnostics**: `E_DEPRECATED_UNKNOWN_FIELD` (per the spec — enumerates the accepted set `since`/`note` in the message body); `E_DEPRECATED_FIELD_NOT_STRING` (non-string value on `since`/`note`); `E_DEPRECATED_POSITIONAL_ARG` (positional arg in the long form — the shorthand `= "string"` is the only legal unnamed shape); `E_DEPRECATED_DUPLICATE` (multiple `#[deprecated]` on one item — first one wins, rest skipped, matches Rust's idempotency). **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: two new helpers `reject_deprecated_on_impl(attrs)` and `reject_deprecated_on_field(attrs)`, wired into `collect_impl` (block-level) and the `for field in &s.fields` loop inside `collect_struct`. Each emits one diagnostic per offending attribute occurrence. **New `ResolveErrorKind::DeprecatedOnImpl` and `DeprecatedOnField`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0241` and `E0242` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map — both must stay in sync). **Test surface (19 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: positive form coverage — `deprecated_slice1_bare_form_on_function`, `..._shorthand_populates_note`, `..._long_form_with_since_only`, `..._long_form_with_note_only`, `..._long_form_with_both_fields`, `..._long_form_with_equals_separator` (`name = value` shape); per-item-kind coverage — `..._struct_captures_payload`, `..._enum_captures_payload`, `..._trait_captures_payload`, `..._marker_trait_captures_payload`, `..._trait_alias_captures_payload`, `..._distinct_type_captures_payload`; regression pin — `..._without_attribute_leaves_field_none`; negative form coverage — `..._rejects_unknown_field`, `..._rejects_non_string_value`, `..._rejects_positional_arg`, `..._rejects_duplicate_attribute`, `..._first_attribute_wins_when_duplicate`, `..._set_on_impl_block_parser_does_not_reject` (parser captures uniformly; the resolver does placement validation). **Test surface (4 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `deprecated_slice3_accepted_on_function` (positive pin); `deprecated_slice3_rejected_on_impl_block` (the spec's E_DEPRECATED_ON_IMPL); `deprecated_slice3_rejected_on_struct_field` (the spec's E_DEPRECATED_ON_FIELD); `deprecated_slice3_accepted_on_struct_enum_trait` (negative pin — none of these legal placements produce DeprecatedOnImpl/Field diagnostics). **What slices 1+2+3a do *not* do.** No symbol-table flag recording (slice 3b — the resolver doesn't yet thread `Deprecation` into the per-symbol metadata, so use-site lookup can't read it cross-module). **[Resolved by slice 3b below — shipped 2026-05-17.]** No use-site warning emission (slice 4 — blocked on lint registry at line 383: the lint must be registered, suppressible, and dispatchable per the cascade rule); no stdlib annotations (slice 6). The payload is structurally complete at every parsed item; slice 4 will read it back through the resolver's symbol-table extension. **Sub-opens.** Per the spec, `#[deprecated]` is also legal on **enum variants**, **trait methods**, **associated functions** (impl methods, already covered by `Function`), **type aliases**, and **module-level consts**. The first three need attribute support added to `Variant` and `TraitMethod` AST nodes (no `attributes` field today); `TypeAliasDef` and `ConstDecl` need attribute support added too. These are the same enabling change flagged by the `#[track_caller]` slice 1 sub-open (line 389) — adding `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` and `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>` to those four AST nodes unblocks both features simultaneously. Tracked as a follow-up because it touches every existing pass that walks `Variant` / `TraitMethod` / `TypeAliasDef` / `ConstDecl` (resolver, typechecker, formatter, span_visitor) — a single enabling commit lets the parser side fan out cleanly. The slice 1 surface here is structurally complete for the seven item kinds it covers. (4) Typechecker / use-site check — at every reference resolution that lands on a deprecated item (call, type name, variant constructor, pattern, trait-bound, method dispatch), emit the `deprecated` lint (warning level by default) with the focused diagnostic shape from the spec — note string surfaced if present, `deprecated since: "..."` line if present, `help: suppress with #[allow(deprecated)]` always present, defining-package note when the deprecated item is `pub`. The lint name is `deprecated`, registered in the central lint registry from the lint-level-attributes entry below. (5) Non-transitivity — deprecating a function does not mark its callers, deprecating a struct does not mark its methods unless each method also carries the attribute. Test coverage: bare `#[deprecated]` produces default-message warning; shorthand `#[deprecated = "use X"]` surfaces the note; long form with both fields includes the `since:` line; defining-package internal use produces the same warning (and `#[allow(deprecated)]` at module level suppresses it); reference at every kind of use site (call, type-name, variant constructor, pattern, method dispatch, trait bound) fires the warning; `#[deprecated]` on `impl` rejected; on struct field rejected; unknown field rejected. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: lint-level-attributes entry below for the `#[allow(deprecated)]` / `#[expect(deprecated)]` suppression machinery.

  - [x] **Slice 3b — resolver symbol-table flag-recording shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the slice-1+2+3a sub-open: the resolver now threads each parser-captured `Deprecation` payload into the symbol table so slice-4's use-site lookup pass (once the lint emission infrastructure lands at line 419 slice 4) can read it without re-walking the AST. **Sidecar HashMap** in `src/resolver.rs::SymbolTable`: new `pub deprecations: HashMap<SymbolId, Deprecation>`, keyed by the defined-symbol's id. Mirrors the existing `generic_param_bounds` shape — sidecar is preferred over a field on `Symbol` because most symbols are not deprecated (space-efficient + cheaper match arms). **Two helpers** on `SymbolTable`: `record_deprecation(id, dep)` (insertion site) and `deprecation_for(id) -> Option<&Deprecation>` (lookup site for slice 4). **Per-collect-site wiring** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: each of the eight `collect_*` helpers that registers a top-level symbol with an attribute-bearing item kind now switches from `if let Err(e) = ...` to a `match` on the `define` result, calling `self.record_deprecation_if_present(id, &item.deprecation)` on the Ok arm. Sites wired: `collect_function` (free fns), `collect_struct`, `collect_enum` (top-level + per-variant payload recording for variant-level `#[deprecated]`), `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_distinct_type`, `collect_const`, `collect_type_alias`. **Impl-method special case** in `collect_impl`: methods bypass `table.define` (they live in `type_methods`, not the global scope) and are pushed directly onto `table.symbols`; slice 3b records the per-method payload via `record_deprecation_if_present(method_id, &method.deprecation)` after the push. **New private helper** `Resolver::record_deprecation_if_present(id, &Option<Deprecation>)` centralises the dispatch so each call-site stays one line. **Trait-method `#[deprecated]` carry-forward.** Trait method declarations carry the `deprecation` payload at the AST level (per the line-431 enabling change), but v1 does not register trait methods as top-level symbols (they're looked up via the trait's method-names list). Slice 3b therefore records the per-trait-method payload only at the impl-block side (where each impl-method gets its own SymbolId); the trait-decl side stays AST-only until slice 4's use-site lookup pass decides whether to consult the trait's method-names list or the impl table. The carry-forward is one-line comment in `collect_trait`. **Test surface (8 new tests in `tests/resolver.rs::deprecated_slice3b_*`)**: `records_payload_on_function` (basic — bare `#[deprecated]` produces a recorded payload with both fields `None`); `preserves_since_and_note` (long-form `#[deprecated(since, note)]` round-trips both fields verbatim); `shorthand_populates_note` (`#[deprecated = "..."]` shorthand populates `note` only); `undecorated_symbol_has_no_entry` (regression — a plain `fn` does not appear in the sidecar); `per_item_kind_coverage` (one entry per legal target kind — fn / struct / enum / trait / marker_trait / pub const / type alias — each with a distinct note string so a misrouting would surface as a mismatched assertion); `records_on_enum_variant` (variant-level `#[deprecated]` records against the variant's own SymbolId, not the parent enum's; pins that the parent enum and an undecorated sibling variant both lack entries); `records_on_impl_method` (the bypass-define impl-method path records correctly; pins the sibling-undecorated-method-absent invariant via a `type_methods["S"]` walk); `lookup_returns_distinct_payloads_for_two_items` (two deprecated fns hold distinct payloads — pins that the sidecar is keyed by id, not by name). Helper `lookup_deprecation(result, name)` factored at the top of the new test block to keep the per-test assertions concise. **What slice 3b does *not* do.** No use-site emission (slice 4 — that's where the lookup helper becomes load-bearing). No cross-module visibility filter (use-sites in a different package querying a deprecated `pub` item see the recorded payload identically to defining-package use-sites — visibility filtering is a slice-4 concern when the lint cascade reads the override). No trait-method-decl payload recording into a top-level symbol (the v1 surface only records trait methods at impl-block instantiation; if slice 4 needs trait-decl-side metadata it can extend the helper). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 4 — typechecker use-site warning emission shipped 2026-05-17.** Unblocked by lint-level slice 4b core (the cascade walker landed earlier the same day). Spec sentence honoured: *"Typechecker / use-site check — at every reference resolution that lands on a deprecated item (call, type name, variant constructor, pattern, trait-bound, method dispatch), emit the `deprecated` lint (warning level by default) with the focused diagnostic shape from the spec — note string surfaced if present, `deprecated since: "..."` line if present, `help: suppress with #[allow(deprecated)]` always present."* **New `TypeErrorKind::Deprecated`** in `src/typechecker.rs`; mapped to `E0245` (errors path under `#[deny(deprecated)]`) / `W0245` (warnings path) in `src/cli.rs` (slot `E0244`/`W0244` is the `unknown_lint` follow-up landed on top of slice 4b core). **`check_deprecated_use_at(span, display_name)` helper** at `src/typechecker.rs:~1062`: queries the resolver's per-span `resolutions` map first; falls back to a global-scope name lookup so call sites where the typechecker resolves via its own env (rather than threading the SpanKey) still surface the warning. Reads `SymbolTable.deprecation_for(sym_id)` (slice-3b plumbing); if `Some(dep)`, builds a message like `"warning[deprecated]: use of deprecated item `name`: <note> (since X) — suppress with `#[allow(deprecated)]` on the enclosing item"`, omitting the `note` / `since` clauses when the payload's optional fields are absent. Emits via `type_lint_warning("deprecated", ...)`, routing through the cascade so `#[allow(deprecated)]` / `#[warn(deprecated)]` / `#[deny(deprecated)]` on the enclosing scope take effect (slice 4b core). **Wired at three reference sites** (the most common surfaces; trait-bound and pattern sites are carry-forwards): (1) `resolve_identifier_type` in `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs:~180` — emits when a bare-name reference resolves to a `Function` or `Constant` in the env. (2) `infer_struct_literal` in `src/typechecker/fields.rs` — emits when a struct literal's name resolves to a deprecated struct. (3) `lower_path_type` in `src/typechecker/lowering.rs:~349` — emits when a type-position reference (`var: OldStruct`) resolves to a known deprecated struct / enum / trait. The borrow-checker required cloning the env lookups (`functions` / `constants`) before the `&mut self` emission call; clones the small `FunctionSig` fields (`params` / `return_type`) and the const's `Type` directly. **Non-transitivity** (spec sentence: *"deprecating a function does not mark its callers"*) is a natural consequence — the warning fires at the USE site, not the definition site, so a deprecated fn calling another deprecated fn still produces a warning for the inner call. **Test surface (9 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::deprecated_slice4_*`).** Headline: `call_to_deprecated_fn_emits_warning` (positive — calling a `#[deprecated]` fn fires the warning with the expected message components: fn name, `deprecated`, suppression hint). `long_form_surfaces_note_and_since` (`#[deprecated(since, note)]` round-trips the note string and the since version into the diagnostic). Cascade integration: `allow_suppresses_at_caller` (the slice-4b cascade silences the warning when the caller is `#[allow(deprecated)]`), `deny_promotes_to_error` (`#[deny(deprecated)]` routes the entry to `errors` instead of `warnings`). Negative-space: `non_deprecated_fn_no_warning` (plain `pub fn` doesn't fire), `self_referential_use_inside_deprecated_fn_emits` (non-transitivity — deprecated → deprecated still warns at the inner call). Per-site coverage: `deprecated_const_use_emits_warning` (Constant resolution site), `type_position_use_emits_warning` (`lower_path_type` site), `struct_literal_emits_warning` (`infer_struct_literal` site). **What slice 4 does *not* do.** No emission at method-call sites — the typechecker's method-dispatch path doesn't yet thread the resolved symbol's deprecation. No emission at variant-constructor sites — variant resolution lives in `resolve_identifier_type`'s variant fallback (the helper is reachable from there but variant names hit the resolver's variant scope, not the symbol-table direct lookup). No emission at pattern reference sites (struct / variant patterns). No emission at trait-bound references in `where` clauses. No emission at impl-method dispatch (`x.old_method()`). All are concrete follow-up sites that would call the same `check_deprecated_use_at` helper at the right point in their respective resolution paths. **Defining-package note** ("when the deprecated item is `pub`") from the spec is also a follow-up — today the message doesn't distinguish; the `dep` payload doesn't carry the defining `is_pub` flag through the slice-3b sidecar (it could be added by extending `Deprecation` or by joining with the symbol's `is_pub`). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

- [x] **Lint level attributes `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]`.** Parser + AST + central lint registry (slices 1+2+3a) + `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection on the four attributes (slice 6) + broader per-item `lint_overrides` attachment beyond `Function` (slice 4a) + minimal scope cascade with `type_lint_warning` emission integration (slice 4b core) + lint-name carry-through into structured diagnostics (slice 7) + `unknown_lint` warning synthesis + spec-correct `Expect → suppress` semantics (slice 4b follow-up) + CLI build-wide defaults (`-A` / `-W` / `-D` / `-F` / `-D warnings`) + forbid-mode rejection of inner `#[allow]` (slice 4b polish) + `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking with `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` emission + `E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED` circular-guard rejection (slice 5) + cross-cutting CLI fall-through across `unsafe_lint` / `must_use_lint` / `missing_must_use_lint` / `logical_lint` / `ffi_lint` (slice 4b cross-cutting) all shipped 2026-05-17. The per-frame in-source cascade across these 5 lint modules (outer-scope `#[allow]` on an impl block propagating to method bodies emitted by these modules) is deferred — see `[->]` sub-bullet below.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2+3a — parser, AST, central registry shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured for slice 1: *"Attribute parser — recognise the four attributes uniformly; each accepts a comma-separated list of lint names (`#[allow(deprecated, rc_fallback)]`); duplicate-lint-name within a single attribute is `error[E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL]`; unknown lint names produce the `unknown_lint` warning (suppressible)"* + slice 2 AST data type + slice 3 registry. **New `src/lints.rs` module** holds three types — `LintLevel { Allow, Warn, Deny, Expect }`, `LintLevelOverride { span, level, lint }`, `LintInfo { name, default_level, description }` — plus the central `STARTER_LINTS: &[LintInfo]` array enumerating the 15 v1 lint names from the design.md spec (the 14 listed in the parent-entry plus `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` which the spec calls out separately under `#[diagnostic::*]`). `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` is intentionally absent from the registry — per the spec it is a hard rule, not a lint, and the four lint-level attributes are rejected on it (slice 6 enforcement). The `lint_by_name` lookup powers parser-side validation; three module-local tests pin (a) no duplicate registry names, (b) every spec-listed name is present, (c) `LintLevel::from_attr_name` ↔ `as_attr_name` round-trips. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `Function.lint_overrides: Vec<LintLevelOverride>`, defaulted to empty at every construction site (parser sets from attribute scan; `prelude.rs`'s stub, `typechecker/items.rs`'s synthesized trait-method stub, `effectchecker.rs` + `effectchecker/bounds.rs` synthesized trait-method stubs all default empty). Attachment beyond `Function` is deferred — the spec wants overrides on every item / expression-block / statement node that supports attributes, but most of those nodes don't yet carry an `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` field; the broader attachment is bundled with slice 4 (scope cascade) since that's the consumer that needs to walk outward through statement and block scopes. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `scan_lint_level_attrs(&attributes) -> Vec<LintLevelOverride>` helper dispatches on attribute name via `LintLevel::from_attr_name`, extracts lint identifiers from each attribute's positional args (`#[allow(deprecated)]` produces an `AttrArg { name: None, value: Some(Identifier("deprecated")) }` shape; the helper deconstructs this), and emits three parse-time diagnostics: `E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL` (the same lint name appears twice in one attribute — per-attribute scope only; cross-attribute duplicates are accepted because slice 4 will define last-writer-wins semantics), `E_LINT_LEVEL_NON_IDENT_ARG` (the arg is a string literal, key=value pair, or non-identifier expression — the spec requires bare identifiers), `E_LINT_LEVEL_NO_ARGS` (the attribute has zero lint names — `#[allow]` or `#[allow()]`). The helper is called from `parse_function` and the result threaded into the `Function` constructor. **Unknown lint names are silently accepted at this slice** — per the design.md "Naming" rule ("code with `#[allow(removed_lint)]` continues to compile (the attribute targets an unknown lint, which is itself the `unknown_lint` warning, suppressible)"), an unknown name must NOT break the build. Silencing today is the safe default; the `unknown_lint` warning emission lands with slice 4's lint emission infrastructure (parser-side warnings don't have an emission channel yet). **Test surface (3 unit tests in `src/lints.rs` + 13 parser integration tests in `tests/parser.rs`).** Unit: registry well-formedness pins. Parser: `lint_attrs_slice1_allow_single_lint_captures_override` (basic — `#[allow(deprecated)]` populates the override); `lint_attrs_slice1_all_four_attribute_names_recognized` (all four levels round-trip); `lint_attrs_slice1_comma_separated_list_produces_multiple_overrides` (`#[allow(a, b, c)]` produces three overrides); `lint_attrs_slice1_function_without_attribute_has_empty_overrides` (regression pin); `lint_attrs_slice1_unknown_lint_silently_accepted` (the spec's forward-compat pin); `lint_attrs_slice1_duplicate_lint_in_single_attribute_rejected` (E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL); `lint_attrs_slice1_duplicate_in_separate_attrs_currently_allowed` (cross-attribute duplicates accepted — pin for the scope-cascade decision); `lint_attrs_slice1_empty_arg_list_rejected` (`#[allow()]` → E_LINT_LEVEL_NO_ARGS); `lint_attrs_slice1_bare_form_with_no_args_rejected` (bare `#[allow]` same diagnostic family); `lint_attrs_slice1_string_value_rejected` (`#[allow = "..."]` → E_LINT_LEVEL_NON_IDENT_ARG); `lint_attrs_slice1_key_value_arg_rejected` (`#[allow(deprecated = "oops")]` same diagnostic); `lint_attrs_slice1_spans_point_at_lint_name` (override span localises the name, not the whole attribute); `lint_attrs_slice1_attribute_coexists_with_other_attributes` (`#[allow]` next to `#[track_caller]` + `#[deprecated]` doesn't conflict). **What slices 1+2+3a do *not* do.** (a) Attachment beyond `Function` — no `lint_overrides` on `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, statement nodes, or expression blocks (slice 4 bundles broader attachment with the cascade). (b) No `unknown_lint` warning — silently accepts unknown names (slice 4 emission infrastructure). (c) No cascade — the overrides are structurally captured but no existing warning consults them yet. (d) No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5). (e) No `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection on `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` (slice 6 — today only `#[allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` is rejected via the older one-rule guard in `parse_attribute`). **[Resolved by slice 6 below.]** (f) No lint-name field on structured diagnostics (slice 7). Slices 1+2+3a are the foundation: with the registry + AST data type + parser surface in place, slice 4 reads `lint_overrides`, walks outward through scopes, and decides effective level per emission. (4) Scope cascade — when emitting a lint, walk outward from the current scope to find the nearest `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` for the named lint; the innermost match wins. CLI flags (`-A NAME` / `-W NAME` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`) set the build-wide default that the cascade falls through to; the existing `-D warnings` flag is the canonical "treat all warnings as errors" form and works by promoting every lint's effective level to `Deny`. The `-F` (forbid) flag, like Rust's `#![forbid]`, additionally disallows inner `#[allow]` overrides — an inner `#[allow]` of a forbidden lint produces `error[E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW]`. (5) `#[expect]` semantics — track per-attribute whether the named lint fired anywhere within the attributed scope (an "expectation fulfilled" bit). At end-of-typecheck, every `#[expect]` whose bit is unset emits `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` pointing at the attribute itself. Reject `#[expect(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` with `error[E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED]` (would be circular). The `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` lint is itself suppressible with `#[allow(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]`. (6) `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` exception — this is a hard rule, not a lint; the four lint-level attributes are rejected on it (`error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]`). (7) Diagnostics — every warning emitted by the compiler must record the lint name in the structured diagnostic so `karac explain --json` consumers can route, group, and filter by lint. Test coverage: `#[allow(deprecated)]` suppresses one warning; nested `#[warn(deprecated)]` overrides outer `#[allow]` for inner code only; `#[expect(rc_fallback)]` on a fn that triggers the lint is silent; the same `#[expect]` on a fn that doesn't trigger the lint emits `unfulfilled_lint_expectation`; multiple lints in one attribute (`#[allow(rc_fallback, implicit_clone)]`) work; `#[deny(deprecated)]` promotes the lint to a build error; `-D warnings` CLI flag treats every warning as an error; `-F deprecated` rejects an inner `#[allow(deprecated)]`; unknown lint name (`#[allow(no_such_lint)]`) emits `unknown_lint` warning suppressible with `#[allow(unknown_lint)]`; `#[expect]` cannot wrap `unfulfilled_lint_expectation`; lint level attributes on `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rejected. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: design.md § Lint Level Attributes for the surface, `#[deprecated]` entry above for the canonical first user.

  - [x] **Slice 6 — `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection on all four lint-level attributes shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"`unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` exception — this is a hard rule, not a lint; the four lint-level attributes are rejected on it (`error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]`)."* **Generalised the existing one-rule guard** in `src/parser/attributes.rs::parse_attribute` (the slice-5 `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`-epic guard at lines ~142-173) from `name == "allow"` to `matches!(name.as_str(), "allow" | "warn" | "deny" | "expect")`. Same `iter().any(...)` arg-shape check (positional `IDENT` and the theoretical named `name = IDENT` form, both routed through `ExprKind::Identifier` matching). The diagnostic string now carries the symbolic `error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]:` prefix (was the bare slice-5 phrasing) and quotes the offending attribute's literal form back to the author so the source-line and the diagnostic stay grepably aligned; the redirect to `unsafe { ... }` + `// Safety:` comment is preserved verbatim from slice 5. **Why a stringy match instead of `LintLevel::from_attr_name`.** `src/parser/attributes.rs` lives at the AST-walk layer; calling into `crate::lints` from there would introduce a parser→lints dependency for one boolean. The four attribute names are a fixed v1 surface per the spec ("each accepts a comma-separated list of lint names"), and the slice-1+2+3a tests already pin the round-trip with the registry — a string-list mismatch would surface there first. **Per-arg scope.** If `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` appears anywhere inside one of the four attribute's args (alone or in a multi-name list like `#[warn(undocumented_unsafe, unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]`), the whole attribute is rejected via `iter().any()`. **No other lint name is touched** — `#[warn(deprecated)]` / `#[deny(rc_fallback)]` / `#[expect(implicit_clone)]` continue to parse cleanly; the slice-4 cascade reads them. **Test surface (4 new + 2 retitled + 1 amended in `tests/parser.rs`).** New tests covering the three previously-accepted attribute names: `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_warn`, `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_deny` (replaces the prior `test_deny_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_still_accepted` regression pin, which deliberately pinned the slice-5 scoping decision that slice 6 now flips), `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_expect`, `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_warn_in_multi_lint_list` (iter-any branch on the new attribute names). Positive pin: `test_lint_level_attrs_with_other_lint_names_still_accepted` ensures the rejection is scoped to `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` only — `#[warn(deprecated)]` + `#[deny(rc_fallback)]` + `#[expect(implicit_clone)]` on the same fn parse cleanly. The existing `test_allow_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_rejected_with_focused_diagnostic` is amended to assert the `E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE` symbolic code in the diagnostic body and to spell "hard rule" instead of "hard error" (the latter wording was specific to the slice-5 framing). The slice-5 section header in `tests/parser.rs` is retitled to point at slice 6 of the lint-level-attributes entry, since the rejection is now centrally owned by lint-level slice 6 rather than the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` epic. **What slice 6 does *not* do.** No cascade integration (slice 4) — slice 6 fires at parse time, before any scope cascade exists; the cascade can't suppress a parse-time error in any case (the rule is hard, not a lint). No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5) — the `#[expect(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` rejection here predates the fulfilment machinery; when slice 5 lands, the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` name will already have been rejected at parse, so the fulfilment pass never sees it. No lint-name field on the structured diagnostic (slice 7) — the diagnostic is a parser error, not a lint emission; slice 7 covers lints. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 4a — broader `lint_overrides` attachment beyond `Function` shipped 2026-05-17.** The slice-1+2+3a ship note flagged attachment as "deferred — most nodes don't yet carry an `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` field; the broader attachment is bundled with slice 4". The AST-enabling changes at line 437 / 439 (`Variant` + `TraitMethod` + `ConstDecl` + `TypeAliasDef`) closed the field-existence gap; this slice ships the broader `lint_overrides: Vec<LintLevelOverride>` attachment that the cascade (slice 4b) will read. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, `TraitAliasDef`, `MarkerTraitDef`, `DistinctTypeDef`, `ConstDecl`, `TypeAliasDef`, `ImplBlock` all gain a `lint_overrides: Vec<LintLevelOverride>` field, mirroring the `Function` shape. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs` + `src/parser/items_trait.rs`: every `parse_*` site that constructs one of the nine extended item kinds calls `self.scan_lint_level_attrs(&attributes)` and threads the result into the constructor. `scan_lint_level_attrs` is the existing helper from slice 1; same diagnostic surface (`E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL` / `E_LINT_LEVEL_NON_IDENT_ARG` / `E_LINT_LEVEL_NO_ARGS`) carried forward unchanged — slice 4a is structurally a field addition, not a parser-behaviour change. **Prelude stubs** in `src/prelude.rs::stub_struct` / `stub_trait` default to `lint_overrides: Vec::new()` (synthetic stubs never carry user-authored attributes; the field is structurally present so the AST shape is uniform). **No semantic effect today.** The cascade reader is slice 4b; without it, the attached overrides are inert (the existing emission sites in `must_use_lint`, `unsafe_lint`, etc. don't yet consult `lint_overrides` from the surrounding scope chain). Slice 4a is the foundation that lets slice 4b walk outward from a diagnostic-emit site through `Function → ImplBlock → containing TraitDef/EnumDef/StructDef → module-level CLI flags` and pick the innermost matching `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]`. **Test surface (11 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::lint_attrs_slice4a_*`).** One round-trip pin per attachment site: struct (`#[allow(deprecated)]` captures), struct-without-attribute (regression pin — empty), enum, trait, trait alias, marker trait, distinct type, module const, type alias, impl block. Multi-lint-list pin (`#[allow(deprecated, rc_fallback, implicit_clone)]` on a struct captures three overrides — exercises the `scan_lint_level_attrs` iteration on the new item kinds). The diagnostic surface (duplicates, non-ident args, empty lists) is already pinned by slice 1's tests on `Function`; slice 4a relies on the helper's centrality to skip re-testing each negative form per-item-kind. **What slice 4a does *not* do.** No cascade — emission sites still don't consult `lint_overrides`. No `unknown_lint` emission. No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking. No CLI flag (`-A` / `-W` / `-D` / `-F`). All of those bundle into slice 4b alongside the actual cascade walker. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks slice 4b** (the cascade reader has fields to read), **slice 5** (`#[expect]` fulfilment will key off the same data), and **slice 7** (per-lint diagnostic routing reads from the same overrides). **[Slice 7 — see below — shipped on the same date.]**

  - [x] **Slice 7 — lint-name carry-through into structured diagnostics shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"every warning emitted by the compiler must record the lint name in the structured diagnostic so `karac explain --json` consumers can route, group, and filter by lint."* **`TypeError` extension** in `src/typechecker.rs`: new `lint_name: Option<String>` field on the unified error/warning carrier (the same struct is reused for `errors` and `warnings` vectors). Defaulted to `None` at every existing construction site; populated only at lint-style emission points. **New helper `type_lint_warning(msg, span, kind, lint_name: &'static str)`** in `src/typechecker.rs` replaces `type_warning` for any lint-routed warning. The original `type_warning` (lint-name-less) has been removed — the spec mandates every warning carry a lint name, so a name-less helper is a footgun; future warning emitters call `type_lint_warning` directly. **Wiring at the existing emission site** (`src/typechecker/patterns.rs::check_exhaustiveness`): the `UnreachableArm` warning now routes through `type_lint_warning` with `"unreachable_arm"` as the lint name. **Registry extension** in `src/lints.rs`: `STARTER_LINTS` gains an `unreachable_arm` entry with `default_level: LintLevel::Warn` so the slice-4b cascade reader can look up the default. The spec-list completeness pin (`starter_set_covers_spec_listed_lints`) is unaffected — `unreachable_arm` isn't on the spec's original 15-name v1 starter list, and the pin's `required` array stays a strict subset. **JSON output extension** in `src/cli.rs`: `DiagEntry` gains a `lint_name: Option<&str>` field that serializes as `"lint_name":"..."` in the JSON output (positioned between `hints` and `extra_json` in the entry shape so existing field-position assumptions stay stable). All 10 `DiagEntry` construction sites updated — 9 set `lint_name: None` (hard errors and warnings that haven't migrated to a registered lint yet), one passes through `warn.lint_name.as_deref()` for the typechecker warning channel. **Test surface (4 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice7_*`).** `unreachable_arm_warning_carries_lint_name` (headline — the `UnreachableArm` warning's `lint_name` field is `Some("unreachable_arm")`); `clean_match_has_no_warnings_with_lint_name` (regression — clean code emits no warnings; lint_name only populates on fire); `unreachable_arm_lint_is_registered` (pins the registry contains the name so the cascade reader's `lint_by_name` lookup will succeed); `error_kinds_have_lint_name_none` (pin that hard errors stay `lint_name: None` — a future drift that auto-populates would silence the slice-7 surface). **What slice 7 does *not* do.** No cascade integration — the field is populated, but `#[allow(unreachable_arm)]` doesn't yet suppress the warning (slice 4b reads `lint_overrides` + the cascade walker to decide). No JSON pre-existing-warning migration — lint-module warnings (`unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, etc.) currently render to stderr only, not through `DiagEntry`'s JSON channel; routing them through is a separate plumbing step. No CLI text-format change — the rustc-style `warning[name]:` prefix on stderr renders unchanged today. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks the slice-4b cascade** which now has a `lint_name`-aware warning channel to consult; slice 4b walks outward from the warning's span, finds the innermost matching `lint_overrides` entry for the named lint, and either suppresses / promotes / records expectation fulfilment. **[Slice 4b core — see below — shipped on the same date.]**

  - [x] **Slice 4b core — minimal scope cascade with emission integration shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the slice-7 carry-forward — `lint_overrides` are now consulted at emission time, not just structurally captured. Spec sentence honoured: *"Scope cascade — when emitting a lint, walk outward from the current scope to find the nearest `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` for the named lint; the innermost match wins."* CLI flags (`-A NAME` / `-W NAME` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`), forbid-mode rejection of inner `#[allow]`, and `unknown_lint` warning emission are slice-4b polish that lands when there's a use case (today no warning-channel consumer routes through the cascade besides `type_lint_warning`). **`lint_override_stack: Vec<Vec<LintLevelOverride>>`** on `TypeChecker` — pushed at every item-walk entry, popped on exit. Wired at `check_function` (line 800 — after `current_fn_stdlib_origin` save/restore), `check_impl_block` (line ~980 — after `enclosing_bounds` save), and `check_trait_def` (line 91 — after `enclosing_trait` save). Push/pop pairs are symmetric with the existing `current_return_type` / `enclosing_bounds` save/restore patterns; the stack invariant is "innermost frame at the top, popped on item exit". **`effective_lint_level(&self, lint_name: &str) -> LintLevel`** at `src/typechecker.rs:~1010` — walks `lint_override_stack` innermost-first (outer Vec, then innermost-to-outermost within the frame), returns the first matching `LintLevelOverride.level`. Falls through to `crate::lints::lint_by_name(lint_name).default_level` on miss; unknown lint names fall through to `LintLevel::Warn` (matches the design.md "Naming" rule of "unknown lint names continue to compile"). **`type_lint_warning` integration** at `src/typechecker.rs:~975` — consults `effective_lint_level` before deciding where to push the entry: `Allow` → suppressed silently; `Warn` / `Expect` → pushed to `warnings`; `Deny` → pushed to `errors` (the message is reused unchanged — the cascade only changes the severity). `Expect` behaves like `Warn` today; slice 5's fulfilment tracking will record whether the expected lint actually fired. **Test surface (7 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice4b_*`).** `allow_suppresses_unreachable_arm_warning` (headline — `#[allow(unreachable_arm)]` on a fn silences the warning); `deny_promotes_unreachable_arm_to_error` (`#[deny]` routes to errors, not warnings — pins the asymmetry); `warn_explicit_keeps_warning_behavior` (no-op `#[warn]` on default-warn-level lint still emits); `unrelated_allow_does_not_suppress` (cascade matches on lint name — `#[allow(deprecated)]` doesn't silence `unreachable_arm`); `default_behavior_unchanged_without_override` (regression — un-annotated code keeps the existing Warn behavior; the lint_name field stays populated); `impl_block_allow_propagates_to_methods` (cascade walks outward — an `#[allow]` on the impl block silences a warning fired inside a method body; pins push/pop on `check_impl_block`); `inner_warn_overrides_outer_allow` (the cascade rule — innermost wins; inner `#[warn]` re-enables a warning that outer `#[allow]` would have silenced). **What slice 4b core does *not* do.** No CLI build-wide flags. No forbid-mode rejection of inner `#[allow]` (slice 4b polish). No `unknown_lint` warning emission (would need a separate emission site walking each captured override). No integration with `unsafe_lint` / `must_use_lint` / `missing_must_use_lint` / `logical_lint` — those modules emit through their own `LintDiagnostic` channels and don't yet consult the cascade. Migration is per-module (each lint walks its own AST and would push frames the same way `check_function` does); deferred until a concrete need arises. No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5). No module-level / file-level `#![allow(...)]` (Kāra has no current equivalent to Rust's inner attributes). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks** lint-style suppression on every existing typechecker warning that migrates to `type_lint_warning`, and the slice-5 fulfilment tracking which keys off the same `effective_lint_level` channel.

  - [x] **Slice 4b follow-up — `unknown_lint` synthesis + `Expect` suppression shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes two of slice 4b core's deferred items in a single focused commit on top of the slice 4b core push/pop cascade. **`unknown_lint` synthesis** (`src/typechecker.rs::emit_unknown_lint_warnings`): a pre-pass in `TypeChecker::check()` (invoked between `check_signature_visibility` and `check_items`, so the cascade-aware emission path is wired before any per-item walk runs) collects every item's `lint_overrides` and, for each override whose `lint` name is not in `crate::lints::STARTER_LINTS`, pushes the item's frame (and the surrounding impl-block frame for impl methods) onto `lint_override_stack`, then emits an `unknown_lint` warning via `type_lint_warning`. Cascade self-suppression works because the item's own overrides are the innermost frame at emission time — `#[allow(unknown_lint, removed_lint)]` resolves to `Allow` and drops the warning. The synthesizer walks every item kind that carries `lint_overrides` post-slice-4a (`Function`, `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, `TraitAlias`, `MarkerTrait`, `ImplBlock`, `ConstDecl`, `TypeAlias`, `DistinctType`); impl-block methods get their own frame on top of the impl block's. The free helper `has_unknown_lint(&[LintLevelOverride])` short-circuits the per-item work when no unregistered name appears. **`TypeErrorKind::UnknownLint`** new variant, mapped to `W0244` in both the error-loop and warning-loop code tables in `src/cli.rs` (so a `#[deny(unknown_lint)]` Deny-promotion surfaces with the same symbolic code on the error side). The error-loop `DiagEntry` construction in `cli.rs` now propagates `err.lint_name.as_deref()` instead of `None` so consumers see *which lint* drove a warning-promoted-to-error through the JSON output. **`Expect → suppress` semantics** (`src/typechecker.rs::type_lint_warning`): the slice 4b core's `LintLevel::Warn | LintLevel::Expect → push to warnings` arm split into `Warn → push` and `Expect → suppress`. Per design.md § Lint Level Attributes, *"`#[expect(NAME)]` on a fn that triggers the lint is silent"* — the user has acknowledged the lint by writing `#[expect]` and the firing is silent. Slice 5 will additionally track fulfilment and emit `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` when the named lint did NOT fire in the attributed scope (the un-fired case). **Test surface (5 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice4b_*` on top of slice 4b core's 7).** `expect_suppresses_like_allow` (headline — `#[expect(unreachable_arm)]` on a fn whose match has an unreachable arm produces no warning); `inner_allow_overrides_outer_deny` (cascade rule mirror — innermost `#[allow]` overrides an outer `#[deny]`, so the warning is suppressed not promoted; pins the cascade walks past the impl-block frame); `unknown_lint_emits_warning` (synthesis pin — `#[allow(no_such_lint)]` fires an `UnknownLint` warning with `lint_name = Some("unknown_lint")`); `unknown_lint_is_suppressible` (self-suppression — `#[allow(unknown_lint, no_such_lint)]` silences itself); `multiple_lints_in_one_attribute` (`#[allow(deprecated, unreachable_arm)]` exercises the per-name lookup on a multi-arg attribute). All 7 slice 4b core tests + the slice 7 lint-name carry-through tests + the 1000+ pre-existing typechecker tests continue to pass. **What the follow-up does *not* do.** No CLI build-wide flags (`-A` / `-W` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`) — slice 4b polish. No `-F`-driven inner-`#[allow]` rejection (`E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW`) — slice 4b polish. No statement / expression-block level overrides — those AST nodes don't carry `lint_overrides`. No migration of other-phase warning emitters (`unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, `ffi_lint`, `logical_lint`) into the cascade — each module would need to push frames the way `check_function` does, or route through `type_lint_warning`; that is the slice 4b cross-cutting work which lands per-module as concrete use cases appear. No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5). Phase target: 5.2. **[Slice 4b polish — see below — shipped 2026-05-17 closing both CLI-flag items.]**

  - [x] **Slice 4b polish — CLI build-wide defaults (`-A` / `-W` / `-D` / `-F` / `-D warnings`) + forbid-mode rejection of inner `#[allow]` shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes both of slice 4b core's deferred CLI items in a single focused commit. Spec sentence honoured: *"CLI flags (`-A NAME` / `-W NAME` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`) set the build-wide default that the cascade falls through to; the existing `-D warnings` flag is the canonical 'treat all warnings as errors' form and works by promoting every lint's effective level to `Deny`. The `-F` (forbid) flag, like Rust's `#![forbid]`, additionally disallows inner `#[allow]` overrides — an inner `#[allow]` of a forbidden lint produces `error[E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW]`."* **New `CliLintOverrides` type** in `src/lints.rs`: `levels: HashMap<String, LintLevel>` (per-name CLI overrides; `-F` writes `Deny` here), `forbidden: HashSet<String>` (names marked `-F`; drives the inner-`#[allow]` rejection), `deny_warnings: bool` (the `-D warnings` catch-all). `level_for(lint, registry_default)` resolves per-name first, then `deny_warnings` (only promotes default-`Warn` lints), then `None` (caller falls through to the registry default). `is_forbidden(lint)` checks the set. Three ergonomic constructors — `with_level(name, level)`, `with_forbid(name)`, `with_deny_warnings()` — let tests construct without the `let mut o = Default::default(); o.field = ...;` pattern that clippy's `field_reassign_with_default` flags. **Cascade fall-through extended** in `src/typechecker.rs::effective_lint_level`: after the per-item `lint_override_stack` misses (innermost-first walk unchanged), `cli_lint_overrides.level_for(lint, registry_default)` is consulted before falling through to the registry default. This pins the precedence the spec implies: source `#[allow(NAME)]` always wins over CLI `-D NAME` (the inner scope is the most specific authority); a per-name CLI flag wins over `-D warnings` (per-name beats catch-all); `-D warnings` only promotes default-`Warn` lints, leaving default-`Deny` lints (like `missing_non_exhaustive`) alone. **Builder method** `TypeChecker::with_cli_lint_overrides(overrides)` mirrors the existing `with_tree` shape so the typechecker stays a single chain. **Forbid pre-pass** `TypeChecker::emit_forbidden_lint_allow_errors` (invoked between `emit_unknown_lint_warnings` and `emit_missing_non_exhaustive_warnings` in `check()`): walks every item's `lint_overrides` (via the existing `item_own_lint_overrides` helper) plus impl-block methods explicitly (their `lint_overrides` live one level inside the impl, same shape as `emit_unknown_lint_warnings`), and emits `error[E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW]` at every `Allow` override whose `lint` is in `cli.forbidden`. The free helper `collect_forbidden_allows(overrides, cli, out)` captures `(span, name)` by value so the caller can drain into `type_error` without holding a borrow of the program AST. **Hard error, not a lint.** The forbid rejection is a `type_error` (not routed through `type_lint_warning`) because forbid mode is the CLI author's load-bearing guarantee — a forbidden lint cannot be silenced anywhere in the build, and routing the rejection through the cascade would let `#[allow(forbidden_lint_allow)]` defeat its own purpose. **`TypeErrorKind::ForbiddenLintAllow`** new variant, mapped to `E0247` in `src/cli.rs` (only the errors path; never a warning by construction). Fast-path `if cli.forbidden.is_empty() { return; }` keeps the pre-pass free when no `-F` flag is set. **CLI arg parsing** in `src/cli/args.rs::try_consume_lint_flag`: recognises both forms — `-A NAME` (bare flag + next-arg) and `-A=NAME` (joined). `-D warnings` and `-D=warnings` set `deny_warnings = true` and skip the per-name entry (so a later `-A NAME` re-suppresses the catch-all promotion). Repeated flags for the same name are last-write-wins (`HashMap::insert` overwrites). Unknown lint names are accepted silently (matches the source side's `#[allow(no_such_lint)]` forward-compat behavior; the emission sites simply don't fire for unknown names, so the override is inert). `-F NAME` for an unknown name is still load-bearing because inner `#[allow]` rejection is name-based, not registry-gated. The helper is wired into `parse_check_command`, `parse_build_command`, `parse_file_args_optional` (covers `run` / bare-file paths), and `parse_run_example_command`. Bad invocations (`-D` with no NAME, `-D=` with empty NAME) exit with a focused error message that quotes the canonical form including `-D warnings`. **Threading** `Command::Run` / `Command::RunExample` / `Command::Check` / `Command::Build` gain a `lint_overrides: CliLintOverrides` field; the cmd_* functions take an extra param; `Pipeline.lint_overrides` is set via the new `Pipeline::with_lint_overrides(overrides)` builder; `Pipeline::typecheck()` routes through `crate::typecheck_with_lint_overrides(program, resolved, overrides.clone())`, a new lib.rs surface that wraps `TypeChecker::new(...).with_cli_lint_overrides(...)`. The `cmd_check_profiles` multi-profile driver clones the overrides per profile so each pass sees the same configuration. **`cmd_build` falls back** to `cmd_check(filename, output, None, concurrency_report, lint_overrides)` on the non-llvm cfg so the CLI surface stays uniform whether or not codegen is built. **Test surface (5 lints unit tests + 11 typechecker integration tests + 7 CLI subprocess tests).** Unit (`src/lints.rs`): `cli_overrides_per_name_wins_over_registry_default`, `cli_overrides_deny_warnings_promotes_default_warn` (and leaves default-`Deny` alone), `cli_overrides_per_name_wins_over_deny_warnings` (precedence pin), `cli_overrides_empty_falls_through` (regression — empty overrides return `None`), `cli_overrides_forbidden_flag_is_separate_from_levels`. Typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice4b_polish_*`): `cli_deny_promotes_default_warn_to_error` + `cli_allow_suppresses_default_warn` + `cli_deny_warnings_promotes_all_warn_to_error` (basic `-D`/`-A`/`-D warnings` round-trips); `source_allow_beats_cli_deny` (cascade precedence — inner `#[allow]` wins over CLI `-D`); `per_name_cli_beats_deny_warnings` (CLI precedence — `-A NAME` wins over `-D warnings`); `deny_warnings_does_not_affect_default_deny` (catch-all scope pin); `forbid_rejects_inner_allow` (headline — `-F NAME` + `#[allow(NAME)]` emits `E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW`); `forbid_accepts_inner_warn_deny_expect` (narrow scope — only `#[allow]` is rejected); `forbid_on_impl_method_inner_allow_rejected` (impl-method walk pin); `forbid_no_inner_allow_no_error` (regression — forbid mode is not a positive duty); `empty_overrides_keeps_default_cascade` (baseline regression). CLI subprocess (`tests/cli.rs::test_lint_cli_*`): `deny_promotes_unreachable_arm_to_error`, `allow_suppresses_unreachable_arm`, `deny_warnings_catch_all_promotes_unreachable`, `joined_form_deny_equals_name` (`-D=NAME` parses), `forbid_rejects_inner_allow` (the symbolic code surfaces in stderr), `missing_arg_fails` (bare `-D` errors with a helpful message), `allow_via_build_subcommand` (the `build` subcommand threads overrides too). **What slice 4b polish does *not* do.** No broader lint-module integration with the cascade (slice 4b cross-cutting — `unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, `missing_must_use_lint`, `logical_lint`, `ffi_lint` still emit through their own channels and don't consult `lint_override_stack` or `cli_lint_overrides`; migration is per-module as concrete use cases appear). No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5 — `Expect` still suppresses silently per slice 4b follow-up; the un-fired case stays open). No `-F warnings` shorthand (the catch-all + forbid combination would semantically mean "promote every Warn AND reject every inner `#[allow]` of any Warn lint" — a complex semantic deferred until a concrete need; today `-F warnings` is silently accepted as a literal lint name with no emission site, so it's inert). No long-form flags (`--allow`, `--deny`, etc. — the spec sentence is `-A NAME` etc., and Rust's long forms are syntactic sugar; can be added when a use case appears). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks** lint-module cascade integration (slice 4b cross-cutting can now consult either source overrides or CLI overrides via the same `effective_lint_level` channel). **[Slice 5 — see below — shipped on the same date.]**

  - [x] **Slice 5 — `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking + `E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED` circular guard shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the last remaining `[~]` item on the lint-level epic *except* the cross-cutting per-module migration. Spec sentence honoured: *"`#[expect]` semantics — track per-attribute whether the named lint fired anywhere within the attributed scope (an 'expectation fulfilled' bit). At end-of-typecheck, every `#[expect]` whose bit is unset emits `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` pointing at the attribute itself. Reject `#[expect(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` with `error[E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED]` (would be circular). The `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` lint is itself suppressible with `#[allow(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]`."* **Fulfilment bookkeeping** in `src/typechecker.rs`: new `fulfilled_expectations: HashSet<(usize, String)>` on `TypeChecker`, keyed by `(span.offset, lint_name)` of the originating `LintLevelOverride`. Byte-offset alone is unique-enough as a key — each lint-name token has a distinct offset within a single source file (and the typechecker runs per file). **Wiring at `type_lint_warning`'s `Expect` arm**: the slice 4b follow-up's silent-suppress arm now also records fulfilment via a new `find_innermost_matching_override(lint_name)` helper that walks `lint_override_stack` innermost-first; the override the cascade selected is the one whose expectation got fulfilled. **Cascade semantics pinned by `inner_allow_does_not_fulfill_outer_expect`**: when outer `#[expect]` + inner `#[allow]` shadow each other on the same lint, the cascade returns `Allow` (innermost wins), `find_innermost_matching_override` is never consulted, and the outer expect stays unfulfilled — matching Rust's documented behaviour that an `#[expect]` is fulfilled only when the cascade actually resolves to `Expect` for some firing. Nested `#[expect]` overrides on the same lint: only the innermost gets marked fulfilled per firing; outer matching `Expect`s remain unfulfilled and surface as a redundancy signal to the user. **`TypeErrorKind::ExpectOnUnfulfilled`** new variant, mapped to `E0248` in `src/cli.rs`. **`TypeErrorKind::UnfulfilledLintExpectation`** new variant, mapped to `E0249` (errors path) / `W0249` (warnings path) — `#[deny(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` routes the sweep emission to errors instead of warnings, pinned by `unfulfilled_promotes_under_deny`. **Pre-pass `emit_expect_on_unfulfilled_errors`** in `src/typechecker.rs` (invoked between `emit_forbidden_lint_allow_errors` and `emit_missing_non_exhaustive_warnings` in `check()`): walks every item's `lint_overrides` (via `item_own_lint_overrides`) plus impl-block methods explicitly, emits hard `type_error(E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED)` for any `Expect` override naming `unfulfilled_lint_expectation`. Same item-walking shape as `emit_forbidden_lint_allow_errors`; the helper `collect_expect_on_unfulfilled(overrides, out)` captures the offending spans by value so the caller can drain into `type_error` without holding a borrow of the program AST. Hard error (not routed through the cascade) so the circular guard cannot itself be suppressed. **End-of-typecheck sweep `emit_unfulfilled_lint_expectations`** invoked from `check()` after `finalize_pattern_binding_inner_types`: walks the same item-level surface and emits `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` via `type_lint_warning` for every `Expect` override whose `(offset, lint_name)` key is absent from `fulfilled_expectations` AND whose `lint` is not `"unfulfilled_lint_expectation"` (the pre-pass already rejected that name, so re-flagging would double-fire). The originating item's own `lint_overrides` are pushed as the innermost cascade frame at emission time (matching `emit_unknown_lint_warnings`'s shape) so `#[allow(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` on the same item suppresses; impl-method emissions also push the impl-block's frame so a block-level `#[allow]` cascades onto methods. The free helper `collect_unfulfilled_expects(overrides, fulfilled, outer_frame, inner_frame, out)` captures both cascade frames alongside each emission so the caller pushes them in the right order. **Test surface (9 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice5_*`).** Headline: `expect_unfulfilled_emits_warning` (the un-fired-expect case — the sweep emits with `lint_name = Some("unfulfilled_lint_expectation")`). `expect_fulfilled_silent` (positive baseline — the lint silently fulfils the expect, no warnings). `unfulfilled_suppressible_via_allow` (cascade integration — `#[allow(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` on the same item silences the sweep). `expect_on_unfulfilled_rejected` (the circular-guard pre-pass — `#[expect(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` produces `E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED`). `multiple_expects_track_independently` (`(offset, name)` keying — `#[expect(unreachable_arm, deprecated)]` on a fn whose body fulfils only `unreachable_arm` emits exactly one unfulfilled warning for `deprecated`). `expect_at_impl_block_fulfilled_by_method_body` (cascade — impl-block `#[expect]` fulfilled by lint firing inside a method body; the impl-block's frame on the cascade stack lets the method-body emission resolve to Expect at the impl level). `expect_at_impl_block_unfulfilled_emits` (mirror — same shape with no firing, the sweep walks impl-block `lint_overrides` and emits). `inner_allow_does_not_fulfill_outer_expect` (Rust-style cascade — inner `#[allow]` shadows outer `#[expect]`, outer stays unfulfilled). `unfulfilled_promotes_under_deny` (`#[deny(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` routes the sweep emission to errors). **What slice 5 does *not* do.** No statement / expression-block level overrides (those AST nodes still don't carry `lint_overrides`; out of scope for v1). No fulfilment tracking for warnings emitted by other-phase lint modules (`unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, etc. — they don't route through `type_lint_warning`, so their firings can't be recorded against the fulfilment set; this is bundled with the slice 4b cross-cutting migration). No diagnostic for the redundancy case where nested `#[expect]` overrides on the same lint shadow each other (the outer is flagged as unfulfilled per the cascade rule, which is signal enough). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **[Slice 4b cross-cutting — see below — shipped on the same date.]**

  - [x] **Slice 4b cross-cutting — CLI fall-through across `unsafe_lint` / `must_use_lint` / `missing_must_use_lint` / `logical_lint` / `ffi_lint` shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the visible portion of the spec's "lint-module integration with the cascade" item. Each of the 5 per-module lint walkers now consults CLI build-wide overrides (`-A NAME` / `-W NAME` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME` / `-D warnings`) via a shared cascade helper so `karac check -A undocumented_unsafe`, `karac check -D ffi_float_eq`, etc. work uniformly. The per-frame in-source cascade (outer-scope `#[allow]` on an impl block propagating onto lint emissions inside method bodies) is deferred — see the `[->]` sub-bullet below for the reason and reopen condition. **Lint-registry additions** in `src/lints.rs`: 4 new entries — `must_use`, `missing_must_use`, `ambiguous_not_comparison`, `ffi_float_eq` — all `Warn`-by-default.
