Registering the names makes the cascade walker treat them like any other registered lint (no spurious `unknown_lint` warning on source `#[allow(must_use)]` etc.). **Shared helper** `crate::lints::effective_level_for_module_lint(source_allow, source_deny, source_expect, cli, lint_name) -> ModuleLintSeverity`: returns `Suppress` / `Warn` / `Deny` after applying the precedence rule — source `#[allow]` / `#[expect]` wins (suppress), then source `#[deny]` (Deny), then CLI overrides (`level_for`), then registry default. Source-Expect maps to Suppress without recording fulfilment (see the `[->]` sub-bullet for the gap). 8 unit tests in `src/lints.rs::tests::effective_level_for_module_lint_*` pin every precedence path. **Per-module migration shape.** Each `check_*` entry point gains a `cli_lint_overrides: &CliLintOverrides` parameter. At the top of the pass: compute the post-cascade severity for the module's lint name; `Suppress` short-circuits with `Vec::new()`; otherwise the resolved `Warning` / `Error` severity is threaded through the AST walker and stamped onto each emitted `LintDiagnostic`. All 5 modules' `LintLevel` enums gained `Copy` so the threading is friction-free. **`logical_lint` and `must_use_lint`** had no in-source attribute walking; the migration is purely "compute once at top, propagate the level". **`ffi_lint`** gained a new `LintLevel { Warning, Error }` enum + `level` field on `FfiFloatEqDiagnostic` so the CLI `-D` promotion has somewhere to land; previously the lint had no severity field (always Warning). The cli.rs render now reads the level and emits `error[ffi_float_eq]` vs `warning[ffi_float_eq]` accordingly. **`missing_must_use_lint`** kept its existing per-function `#[allow]` early-skip but rewired through the shared helper so `#[deny(missing_must_use)]` and `#[expect(missing_must_use)]` are also recognised. New `has_lint_level_attr(attrs, level_kind, rule_name)` generalises the existing `has_lint_allow_attr`. **`unsafe_lint::check_undocumented_unsafe`** had the most existing attribute logic (extern-block + fn + impl-method); each level fed through the shared helper. The previous "outer-deny OR method-deny" cascade was replaced with the proper innermost-wins rule (method-level severity computed via the helper, falling back to outer when no method override matches). **Threading from CLI** — each call site in `src/cli.rs`'s render loop now passes `&pipeline.lint_overrides` to the corresponding `check_*` fn; `Pipeline` already carries the field (slice 4b polish). **Test surface (per-module integration tests, 8 new tests across `tests/logical_lint.rs`, `tests/unsafe_lint.rs`, `tests/must_use_lint.rs`, `tests/missing_must_use_lint.rs`, `tests/ffi_lint.rs`).** Each module exercises the same three pins: CLI Allow suppresses (`-A NAME` → empty diags); CLI Deny promotes (`-D NAME` → every emitted diag carries Error severity); for modules with in-source `#[allow]` (unsafe_lint, missing_must_use_lint), source-allow-beats-cli-deny is pinned to lock the cascade precedence. **What slice 4b cross-cutting does *not* do.** No per-frame cascade walking inside the lint modules — `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)]` on an outer impl block does not propagate to `unsafe { }` blocks inside method bodies via these modules (the module's existing single-level per-function attribute check is the only in-source layer). No fulfilment-tracking side channel — `#[expect(must_use)]` suppresses the emission but the slice-5 sweep still surfaces `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` because the lint module can't record fulfilment back into the typechecker's `fulfilled_expectations` set. Both are bundled into the `[->]` deferred sub-bullet below. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Closes the parent lint-level epic** — the `[~]` flips to `[x]`. The per-frame cascade migration is now an opt-in follow-up rather than a blocker.

  - [->] **Per-frame in-source cascade across the 5 lint modules (deferred).** What's *not* shipped by slice 4b cross-cutting: outer-scope `#[allow(NAME)]` (or `#[deny]` / `#[expect]`) on an impl block / containing struct / module-level node does not propagate to lint emissions produced inside nested scopes by `unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, `missing_must_use_lint`, `logical_lint`, or `ffi_lint`. The typechecker's slice 4b core gets this for its own warnings via `lint_override_stack` push/pop at item entry/exit. Each per-module lint walker would need an analogous stack (or a borrowed cascade reader) threaded through its walker functions, and `#[expect(NAME)]` would need a fulfilment side-channel back to the typechecker's `fulfilled_expectations` set (today the lint modules can't record fulfilment, so `#[expect(must_use)]` silently suppresses the lint but the slice-5 unfulfilled sweep still fires at end-of-typecheck). **Reason for deferral.** No concrete report of an outer-scope override failing to cascade — each of the 5 modules already does single-level per-function `#[allow]` / `#[deny]` recognition (extended to `#[expect]` by slice 4b cross-cutting), which covers the 95% case authors actually write. The cross-cutting work would touch 5 walker chains for marginal user benefit. **Reopen condition.** First user report of an outer-scope `#[allow(NAME)]` (e.g., `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)] impl S { fn f() { unsafe { ... } } }`) failing to silence a lint inside a method body OR an `#[expect(must_use)]` firing an `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` despite the lint actually firing. At that point, pick the one module and migrate it (push/pop `lint_override_stack` at every item boundary the walker enters; fulfilment side-channel back into the typechecker via a new `TypeCheckResult` field that the lint module populates and the unfulfilled sweep consumes). Other modules follow as similar reports arrive. **Cross-reference:** the spec sentence (line 433 parent) deliberately scopes this as "migration is per-module ... deferred until a concrete need arises" — this `[->]` records the deferral rather than the absence.

- [x] **`#[diagnostic::*]` attribute namespace — `on_unimplemented` and `do_not_recommend`.** Spec at `design.md § Diagnostic Namespace Attributes` (v60 item 36). Slice 1 (lexer/parser + AST migration) shipped 2026-05-17; slice 2 (namespace dispatch + `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` on unknown bare names) shipped 2026-05-17; slice 3 (`on_unimplemented` recognition + `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` shape/placeholder validation) shipped 2026-05-17; slice 4 (`do_not_recommend` recognition + impl-block-only off-target/duplicate/arg-shape checks) shipped 2026-05-18; slice 6 (placeholder substitution at the failed-bound diagnostic emit site + env-side plumbing of `do_not_recommend` onto `ImplInfo`) shipped 2026-05-18; slice 6 follow-up ("trait `X` is implemented by …" candidate-listing note that consumes the env-side `do_not_recommend` flag) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullets below. Slice 5 (lint registry) is subsumed by slices 3+4. Slice 7 (testing strategy) is a documentation slice that the per-slice test surfaces already discharge. Entry **closed** — every spec slice with code work shipped; the only remaining `do_not_recommend` consumer-site (the candidate-listing note) is wired and tested. Slices: (1) Lexer / parser — extend the attribute path grammar to accept `IDENT { "::" IDENT }` per syntax.md §8 (a single-segment path is the existing case; multi-segment paths are new). AST: `Attribute { path: Vec<String>, ... }` replaces the existing single-name field; downstream consumers that look up the name now read `path[-1]` with namespace context. (2) Namespace dispatch — central `KnownAttributeNamespace` registry in the attribute checker recognises `diagnostic::*` (and, eventually, the tool namespaces from item 37) as **silent-on-unknown** namespaces. The default behavior for an unrecognized bare-name attribute is `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]`; the default for an unrecognized member of a silent-on-unknown namespace is **accept silently, no warning**. Malformed members (recognized name, wrong shape) emit the `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` lint (warn-by-default). (3) `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` — recognise on `trait` declarations only; off-target produces the malformed-diagnostic warning. Argument shape is three optional named fields: `message: STRING_LITERAL`, `label: STRING_LITERAL`, `note: STRING_LITERAL`. Template placeholders `{Self}`, `{T0}`, `{T1}`, ... are recognised and substituted at diagnostic emit time using the failed-bound's solved metavariable map; unknown placeholders render literally and emit a build-time warning at the trait declaration site. (4) `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` — recognise on `impl` blocks only (inherent and trait); off-target produces the malformed-diagnostic warning. Captured as a flag on the impl's symbol-table entry; consulted by the failed-bound diagnostic builder when iterating candidate impls for the "trait is implemented by ..." note (skip flagged impls). Has no effect on coherence, lookup, or trait resolution — purely diagnostic. (5) Lint registry — register `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` in the central lint registry from item 35's lint-level-attributes entry (warn-by-default; suppressible with `#[allow(malformed_diagnostic_attribute)]`). (6) Integration with the existing failed-bound diagnostic — when typechecker emits `error[E_UNSATISFIED_BOUND]` for a `T: SomeTrait` failure, consult the trait's `on_unimplemented` payload (if any), substitute placeholders against the resolved metavariable map, and use the result as the diagnostic's headline / span label / note in place of the default phrasing. Identical behavior whether the trait is local or imported. (7) Testing strategy — covers both the namespace machinery and the two adopted members. Test coverage: positive — `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(message: "...")]` on a trait surfaces the custom message at a failed-bound site; `{Self}` placeholder substitutes the failing type; multiple fields all surface in the right slots; unknown member `#[diagnostic::polish_my_error_pretty]` is silently accepted with no warning at the use site; `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on a blanket impl removes that impl from the "implemented by" note while still allowing the impl to satisfy bounds. Negative — `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` on a function emits `malformed_diagnostic_attribute`; misspelled field name (`#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(messsage: "...")]`) emits the same lint; multiple `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` on one trait emits warning and uses the first; unknown placeholder `{NotAParam}` emits build-time warning at the trait decl and renders literally; `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on a function or struct emits the malformed lint and is ignored; an unknown bare-name attribute `#[no_such_thing]` is still `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` (silent-on-unknown applies only to namespaced paths). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: design.md § Diagnostic Namespace Attributes; implementation_checklist/ item 35 lint-level-attributes entry (for the lint registry the new `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` lint plugs into); item 37's tool-namespaced attributes share the same path-form lexer/parser change.

  - [x] **Slice 6 — failed-bound diagnostic integration + env-side `do_not_recommend` plumbing shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Integration with the existing failed-bound diagnostic — when typechecker emits `error[E_UNSATISFIED_BOUND]` for a `T: SomeTrait` failure, consult the trait's `on_unimplemented` payload (if any), substitute placeholders against the resolved metavariable map, and use the result as the diagnostic's headline / span label / note in place of the default phrasing. Identical behavior whether the trait is local or imported."* **TraitInfo extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs`: two new fields — `generic_param_names: Vec<String>` (the trait's declaration-order generic param names; index N selects the substitution slot for `{T<N>}`) and `on_unimplemented: Option<OnUnimplemented>` (the slice-3 parser payload, forwarded into the env so the typechecker can consult it without re-walking the program). Both populate in `env_add_trait`: `generic_param_names` from `t.generic_params.params`; `on_unimplemented` from `t.on_unimplemented.clone()`. `env_add_marker_trait` defaults both fields (markers have no generics and no on_unimplemented surface). **ImplInfo extension** — new `do_not_recommend: bool` field, populated from `imp.do_not_recommend` in `env_add_impl` and defaulted to `false` in `register_builtin_impl`. The flag is the forward-looking data plumbing for the "trait is implemented by …" candidate-listing note (see the `[->]` sub-bullet below) — the spec is explicit that it has *no* effect on coherence, lookup, or trait resolution, only on diagnostic candidate iteration; slice 6 lands the storage so the consumer slice can wire it in surgically. **Placeholder substitution helper** `pub fn substitute_placeholders(template, self_render, generic_arg_renders) -> String` in `src/diagnostic_attrs_lint.rs`. Recognises `{Self}` (always substituted from `self_render`) and `{T<i>}` (substituted from `generic_arg_renders[i]` when present; `None` slots and unknown names render literally). Unbalanced braces tolerated. Lives in the same module as the slice-3 `validate_placeholders` walker so the placeholder grammar (recognised names + render rules) is defined in one place — an author who writes `{Self}` cannot trigger a mismatch where the validator accepts it but the substituter ignores it. 7 unit tests in `tests/`-style mod tests in the same file pin every recognised path. **Discharge-site integration** in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs::discharge_type_bounds` (the workhorse for `T: SomeTrait` bound failures at call sites — every `fn f[T: Trait](...)` site flows through here, with both inline and where-clause bounds normalised into the same predicate stream via `normalize_bounds_into_where_clause`). The previous inline `format!` is replaced by a new `render_unsatisfied_bound_message(type_name, trait_name, concrete_ty, bound)` helper that: (a) builds the default phrasing `trait bound `T: Trait` is not satisfied; `X` does not implement `Trait`` (regression-pinned by a fallback test); (b) looks up the trait in `env.traits` and returns the default if no `on_unimplemented` is present; (c) when present, renders `{Self}` from `type_display(concrete_ty)` and `{T<i>}` from each `bound.generic_args[i]` via the existing `parser::render_type_for_diagnostic` AST-render helper. Const generic args don't have a concise rendering and aren't part of the documented placeholder surface — those slots stay `None` and render literally. The substituted message (when present) replaces the headline entirely; `label` appends as `; label: …` and `note` appends as `; note: …`. The choice to use a single-line concatenated message rather than a multi-line message body matches the typechecker convention of `;`-separated clauses (cf. `tests/typechecker.rs:228` for the closure-refutable-pattern hint shape). **Test surface (8 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::on_unimpl_slice6_*`).** *Default-fallback regression (1):* a trait without `on_unimplemented` reproduces the pre-slice-6 default phrasing verbatim. *Custom-message (3):* a payload's `message` replaces the default headline entirely; `{Self}` substitutes to the failing concrete type name; `{T0}` / `{T1}` substitute from the bound's generic args (here `[i64, bool]`). *Label / note (3):* `label` and `note` append after the message in the `; label: … ; note: …` shape; a partial payload with only `label` still appends to the default headline; `{Self}` substitutes inside both `label` and `note`. *AST plumbing (1):* a `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` impl still satisfies bounds at call sites — pins the "purely diagnostic" rule from the spec so the env-side flag never accidentally influences resolution. **Substitution helper unit tests (7 in the lib mod tests)** — `{Self}` alone, `{Self}` plus generics, missing slot renders literal, unknown name renders literal, unbalanced brace renders literal, repeated `{Self}` substitutes every occurrence, empty template. **What slice 6 does *not* do.** No "trait `X` is implemented by: Foo, Bar, …" candidate-listing note — Kāra's failed-bound diagnostic doesn't carry that note today, and adding it is a meaningful new user-facing feature surface independent of the `on_unimplemented` substitution. The `ImplInfo.do_not_recommend` plumbing is in place so the note can consult it without further AST/env work, but the note itself is the `[->]` sub-bullet below. No substitution at the secondary unsatisfied-bound emission sites (`expr_call.rs:368`, `stdlib_map.rs`, `stdlib_seq.rs`, `mono.rs`, `expr_ops.rs`) — those carry their own specialised phrasing (stdlib collection bounds like `Map[K, V]` use baked diagnostics tailored to the collection, not user-trait `on_unimplemented`). Extending substitution into those sites is straightforward (call the same `render_unsatisfied_bound_message` helper) but the user-facing payoff is concentrated in `discharge_type_bounds` since that's where user-defined `T: SomeTrait` failures fire. No imported-trait round-trip test — the spec calls out "identical behavior whether the trait is local or imported", but `parse` + `resolve` + `typecheck` already share the same code path for trait registration so the import case is structurally covered by the local-trait tests. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **"Trait `X` is implemented by: …" candidate-listing note shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes the `do_not_recommend` consumer surface — the env-side flag plumbed by slice 6 is now read at the failed-bound emit site. **Helper** in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs`: new `impl_candidates_for_trait(trait_name) -> Vec<String>` looks up `env.impls_by_trait[trait_name]`, dereferences each index, filters impls flagged `do_not_recommend` (the spec's headline use case), renders the target as `target_type` for generic-on-name impls or `target_type[arg1, arg2, …]` for specialized impls, dedupes by rendered string (so a specialized + generic-on-name pair that render identically collapses into one entry), then `sort().dedup()`s for a stable alphabetical order independent of registration sequence (snapshot-friendly across env-construction reorderings). **Render integration** — `render_unsatisfied_bound_message` was lightly restructured so the on_unimplemented `payload` lookup no longer short-circuits the function on `None`; instead the headline / label / note rendering is gated per-clause, and the candidate-note runs unconditionally at the end. When `impl_candidates_for_trait` returns non-empty, the message appends `; trait `<NAME>` is implemented by: A, B, C`. The clause's position after `; note: …` follows the convention of compiler-generated help following author-authored text. **Empty-list suppression** — the note is omitted when (a) the trait has no env entries (built-in traits like `Eq` / `Ord` / `Hash` are implicit and don't surface in `env.impls`) or (b) every registered impl is `do_not_recommend`, leaving zero candidates after filtering. Both behaviours are pinned. **Design choices fixed by this slice (resolving the four sub-questions from the prior `[->]` deferral).** *Sort order:* alphabetical, so registration order never leaks into user-visible diagnostics and tests stay stable across env-construction changes. *Truncation:* none at v1 — most user traits have a small handful of impls and the message length is bounded by `env.impls_by_trait` size; truncation can be added later if a real-world report surfaces a problem. *Suppression signals:* only `do_not_recommend`; broader suppression heuristics (e.g., visibility filtering, private-impl hiding) are not in scope and are a separate follow-up if a need arises. *Generic-impl render:* `target_type[arg1, arg2]` for specialized impls, bare `target_type` for generic-on-name impls — matches how `env_add_impl` already classifies them and the conventional Kāra type-syntax shape. **Test surface (6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::impl_candidates_note_*`).** *Single impl listed* — `impl Custom for Yes` produces `... is implemented by: Yes`. *Multiple alphabetical* — `Cherry`, `Apple`, `Banana` impls in source order render as `Apple, Banana, Cherry` after sort. *Skips do_not_recommend* — `LegacyShim` flagged is filtered out; `Public` remains. *Absent when no impls* — pure-declaration trait with zero impls suppresses the note (would otherwise render `implemented by: ` with nothing). *Absent when all do_not_recommend* — every impl flagged means zero candidates means no note (a hard suppression of the entire clause, not just a trailing empty list). *Appended after on_unimplemented payload* — the candidate-note is complementary to `on_unimplemented`, not alternative; pin asserts the candidate-note string appears positionally after the `; note: ...` clause from the author's payload.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` recognition + impl-block-only off-target/duplicate/arg-shape checks shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"`#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` — recognise on `impl` blocks only (inherent and trait); off-target produces the malformed-diagnostic warning. Captured as a flag on the impl's symbol-table entry; consulted by the failed-bound diagnostic builder when iterating candidate impls for the 'trait is implemented by …' note (skip flagged impls). Has no effect on coherence, lookup, or trait resolution — purely diagnostic."* Failed-bound consumption is slice 6; slice 4 lands the recognition + lint surface. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: new `do_not_recommend: bool` field on `ImplBlock`, defaulted to `false` at every construction site (`tests/missing_must_use_lint.rs` impl-block helpers + the parser path are the only carriers; no synthesized impl-block stubs exist elsewhere). Pure boolean rather than `Option<DoNotRecommend>` because the attribute carries no payload — argument-less per spec. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `pub(crate) fn scan_do_not_recommend_attr(attrs) -> bool` returns `true` when *any* `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` is present on the impl block — even an argument-bearing malformed-shape occurrence flips the flag, on the principle that the spec's "purely diagnostic" framing means erring on the side of suppression is safer than letting a typo'd attribute silently leak the impl into the candidate list. The shape warning fires independently from the lint pass. `src/parser/items_trait.rs::parse_impl_block` calls the scan and stores the result on the constructed `ImplBlock`. **Lint emission** in `src/diagnostic_attrs_lint.rs`: extended the existing `walk_item` so impl blocks dispatch a new `check_impl_do_not_recommend` helper (first-occurrence-wins on duplicates → one warning per extra; argument-bearing form → "takes no arguments" warning). The off-target helper was generalised from per-attribute to multi-attribute: `emit_off_target_for(attrs, target_kind, legal_here: &[&str], …)` walks every `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` or `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on `attrs` and emits an off-target warning when the member name is not in `legal_here`. Traits pass `&["on_unimplemented"]`, impl blocks pass `&["do_not_recommend"]`, everything else passes `&[]`. The two legal-target shape walkers (`check_trait_on_unimplemented`, `check_impl_do_not_recommend`) then handle duplicates/argument-shape independently — the structure mirrors how the on_unimplemented and do_not_recommend surfaces stay decoupled even when they live in the same lint pass. **Test surface (15 lint tests in `tests/diagnostic_attrs_lint.rs::do_not_recommend_lint_*`).** *Positive (2):* `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on an inherent impl and on a trait impl both emit zero diagnostics. *Off-target (6):* function, struct, trait, enum, impl method, trait method each emit exactly one warning naming the target kind and pinning that the message mentions "only valid on `impl` blocks" (the trait-target test additionally pins that the message names `do_not_recommend` so the diagnostic-namespace neighbour isn't confused with on_unimplemented in error output). *Duplicate (1):* two `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on the same impl → one warning. *Arg-shape (2):* `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend(reason: "x")]` and `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend = "x"]` both warn with "takes no arguments". *AST plumbing (2):* the parser's bool flag is true on a legal-target impl when the attribute is present and false when it's absent (regression pin for slice 6's consumer). *CLI cascade (2):* `-A malformed_diagnostic_attribute` suppresses; `-D malformed_diagnostic_attribute` promotes to error — reuses the same cascade infrastructure slice 3 exercised, but pins it independently on the do_not_recommend surface to catch regressions if either attribute's emission path diverges. **What slice 4 does *not* do.** No failed-bound diagnostic integration — the bool flag is structurally captured but the candidate-impl iterator does not yet consult it (slice 6 — same dependency as slice 3's `OnUnimplemented` payload). No per-method `do_not_recommend` semantics — the spec scopes the attribute to impl *blocks* (the whole impl is suppressed or not); methods inside an impl block fall under off-target. **Slice 5 subsumed** — the lint registry entry was already in `STARTER_LINTS` (item 35 slice 1); slice 3 lit up the first emitter, and slice 4 adds the second within the same module. The `[~]` parent flips to "slice 5 subsumed; slices 6-7 remain" because no separate registration step survives. Phase target: 5.2. **Unblocks** slice 6 — the failed-bound diagnostic builder now has both `TraitDef.on_unimplemented` (slice 3) and `ImplBlock.do_not_recommend` (slice 4) to consume.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` recognition + `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` shape/placeholder validation shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"`#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` — recognise on `trait` declarations only; off-target produces the malformed-diagnostic warning. Argument shape is three optional named fields: `message: STRING_LITERAL`, `label: STRING_LITERAL`, `note: STRING_LITERAL`. Template placeholders `{Self}`, `{T0}`, `{T1}`, ... are recognised and substituted at diagnostic emit time using the failed-bound's solved metavariable map; unknown placeholders render literally and emit a build-time warning at the trait declaration site."* Substitution at emit time remains slice 6 — slice 3 lands the recognition / payload / build-time validation surface. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: new `OnUnimplemented { span, message: Option<String>, label: Option<String>, note: Option<String> }` struct + `on_unimplemented: Option<OnUnimplemented>` field on `TraitDef`. All three payload fields are optional; absent fields fall back to the default failed-bound diagnostic phrasing at emit time. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `pub(crate) fn scan_on_unimplemented_attr(attrs) -> Option<OnUnimplemented>` does best-effort extraction — first-occurrence-wins on duplicates; positional args, unknown fields, non-string-literal values, and the `= "..."` shorthand are silently dropped so legal sibling fields still flow through. `src/parser/items_trait.rs::parse_trait_def_tail` calls it and stores the result on the constructed `TraitDef`. `src/prelude.rs::stub_trait` gets the new field defaulted to `None` since synthesized stubs never carry user attributes. **Validation lives in a new lint pass** `src/diagnostic_attrs_lint.rs` (not the parser) — the spec's malformed signal is a `warn`-by-default lint, not an `E_*` parse error, so emission flows through `crate::lints::effective_level_for_module_lint` for CLI cascade plumbing (`-A` suppresses, `-D` / `-D warnings` promotes to error). The pass walks every item kind that carries attributes and emits `warning[malformed_diagnostic_attribute]` for four shapes: (a) **off-target** — the attribute on any non-trait item (function, struct + field, enum + variant, impl block + method, trait alias, marker trait, trait method, const, type alias, distinct type, extern fn, extern block + items, layout block; the message names the target kind so the author knows where to remove it). (b) **duplicate** — multiple `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` on the same trait; the parser scan's first-wins is paired with one warning per extra attribute. (c) **bad arg shape** — positional argument, unknown field name (anything other than `message` / `label` / `note`), non-string-literal value, repeated field within one attribute, and the `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented = "..."]` shorthand (the long form's three distinct fields make a single string ambiguous). (d) **unknown placeholder** — a `{NAME}` placeholder in any of the three string fields that is neither `{Self}` nor `{T0}` / `{T1}` / ... within the trait's generic-arity. The check fires at the trait declaration site so the author sees it once rather than at every use site; unbalanced braces are silently tolerated (the emit-time formatter will handle them when slice 6 lands). **CLI wiring** in `src/cli.rs`: new render block after `ambiguous_not_comparison` calls `crate::diagnostic_attrs_lint::check_diagnostic_attributes(&pipeline.parsed.program, &pipeline.lint_overrides)` and stringifies with the same `warning[malformed_diagnostic_attribute]: file:line:col: …` shape the other module-style lints use. **Lint-registry status** — the `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` entry was already in `STARTER_LINTS` (item 35 slice 1 reserved the name); slice 3 is the first emitter that actually calls into it. Slice 5 (lint registry — name claim) is therefore subsumed: the registration was already done; slice 3 closes the gap between the name and an active emitter. **Test surface (6 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::on_unimpl_slice3_*`).** `full_payload_captured` (positive — all three fields populated); `partial_payload_captured` (only `message`); `trait_without_attribute_has_none` (regression pin — `on_unimplemented` is `None` when absent); `first_wins_on_duplicate` (the parser keeps the first occurrence; the lint warning is the duplicate's surface, not a parse error); `malformed_fields_silently_dropped_at_parse` (the parser scan tolerates unknown fields / non-string values; the lint pass produces the warnings); `non_trait_carrier_still_in_attribute_list` (the attribute on a function lives in the function's `attributes` vec but produces no function-side payload — only `TraitDef` carries the field). **Test surface (27 lint tests in `tests/diagnostic_attrs_lint.rs`).** *Positive (4):* trait with full / partial payload / `{Self}` placeholder / multi-generic `{T0}…{T2}` placeholders all emit zero diagnostics. *Off-target (8):* function, struct, enum, impl block, module const, type alias, trait method, impl method each emit exactly one warning naming the target kind. *Duplicate (2):* two occurrences → one warning; three occurrences → two warnings (one per extra). *Bad arg shape (6):* unknown field, typo field (`messsage` close-spell), non-string value, shorthand `= "..."`, positional arg, and repeated field within one attribute each emit one warning with a focused message. *Unknown placeholders (4):* `{NotAParam}` in `message`; `{T1}` on a single-generic trait (arity 1); `{T0}` on a non-generic trait (arity 0); placeholders across all three fields each surface. *CLI cascade (3):* `-A malformed_diagnostic_attribute` suppresses; `-D malformed_diagnostic_attribute` promotes to error; `-D warnings` promotes to error. **What slice 3 does *not* do.** No substitution at emit time — `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(message: "{Self} is not Foo")]` parses, stores, and validates the placeholder set, but the failed-bound diagnostic builder does not yet read the payload (slice 6). No `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` recognition (slice 4 — parallel surface on `ImplBlock`). No per-frame source-level `#[allow(malformed_diagnostic_attribute)]` cascade beyond CLI overrides (deferred to the per-frame cascade `[->]` sub-bullet of slice 4b cross-cutting at line 453, alongside the other lint-module deferrals). Phase target: 5.2. **Unblocks** slice 4 (parallel `do_not_recommend` payload + lint emission on impls reuses the `check_diagnostic_attributes` walker and the `LintDiagnostic` shape) and slice 6 (the failed-bound diagnostic builder now has a populated `TraitDef.on_unimplemented` to consume).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — namespace dispatch + `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` on unknown bare names shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Namespace dispatch — central `KnownAttributeNamespace` registry in the attribute checker recognises `diagnostic::*` (and, eventually, the tool namespaces from item 37) as silent-on-unknown namespaces. The default behavior for an unrecognized bare-name attribute is `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]`; the default for an unrecognized member of a silent-on-unknown namespace is accept silently, no warning."* **New module** `src/attribute_validator.rs` houses three pieces: (a) `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES` — the closed v1 list of bare-name attributes the compiler accepts, sourced from the existing `is_bare("...")` lookup sites plus the spec-listed forward-compat entries from `docs/book/src/appendix-d-attributes.md` (`repr`, `thread_local`, `interrupt`, `max_stack`, `gpu`, `cyclic`, `property`, `snapshot`, `rc_budget`) so v1-spec'd code that hasn't yet been wired through the consumer phases still parses without spurious `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE`. The list is exported via `is_recognized_bare_attribute(name) -> bool` for external callers that need to mirror the recognition rule. (b) `KnownAttributeNamespace` enum — at v1 a single arm (`Diagnostic`) with `from_first_segment(&str) -> Option<Self>`. Sets up the registry shape slices 3, 4, and item 37 will extend (per-member validation + tool-namespace catch-all). (c) `validate_program_attributes(program) -> Vec<ResolveError>` — walks every attribute-bearing AST node (function, struct + per-field, enum + per-variant, trait + per-method, trait alias, marker trait, impl + per-method, const, type alias, distinct type, extern fn, extern block + per-item, layout) once and emits `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` on each bare-name attribute whose name is not in the recognised set. Multi-segment paths with a known compiler-reserved first segment (`diagnostic`) are silently accepted (per-member validation lives with slices 3, 4); multi-segment paths in other namespaces (tool-namespaced attributes from item 37) are also silently accepted because the walker only inspects bare-name paths. **Resolver wiring** in `src/resolver.rs`: new `ResolveErrorKind::UnknownAttribute` discriminant; the `Resolver::resolve` pipeline calls `validate_program_attributes(self.program)` at pass 1.6 (between layout validation and body resolution) and extends `self.errors`. **CLI mapping** in `src/cli.rs`: `UnknownAttribute` maps to `E0243` in both error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map — both must stay in sync, mirroring slice 1's plumbing). **Diagnostic shape** — the message names the offending attribute and offers two recovery hints: `#[diagnostic::NAME]` (when the user meant a diagnostic hint, which is silently accepted) and `#[your_tool::NAME]` (when the user meant a tool-namespaced attribute, also silently accepted). **Test surface (13 tests in `tests/resolver.rs::attr_slice2_*`).** Negative: `#[no_such_thing]` on a function rejected (`unknown_bare_attribute_on_function_rejected`); `#[polish_my_error_pretty(level: 9)]` on a function rejected — the argument shape is irrelevant (`unknown_bare_attribute_with_args_rejected`); `#[invent_a_layout]` on a struct, struct field, enum variant, trait method, and impl method all rejected (five separate tests so individual regressions surface cleanly). Positive: `#[allow(deprecated)]` / `#[deprecated]` / `#[derive(Eq)]` / `#[must_use]` / `#[non_exhaustive]` / `#[track_caller]` / `#[kara_name = "..."]` all accepted without `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` (`recognised_bare_attributes_accepted` — spot-check across families); `#[diagnostic::polish_my_error_pretty]` on a trait silently accepted — the headline rule (`diagnostic_namespaced_unknown_member_accepted_silently`); `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(message: "...")]` on a trait and `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on an impl both silently accepted at slice 2 — slices 3, 4 will add the shape validation (`diagnostic_namespaced_known_member_accepted_silently`); `#[karafmt::skip]` and `#[acmecorp_security::audit_required(level: "...")]` silently accepted — pins the tool-namespace surface so item 37 doesn't regress (`tool_namespaced_attribute_accepted_silently`). Discriminant + symbolic-code pin: `unknown_attribute_has_dedicated_error_kind_and_e0243` asserts the `UnknownAttribute` kind plus the `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` prefix; `unknown_attribute_message_suggests_namespaced_form` pins the two recovery hints so future message tweaks keep them. **What slice 2 does *not* do.** No semantic handling of `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` / `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` (slices 3, 4 — for now both are silently accepted alongside any unknown member). No `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` lint registration (slice 5 — the lint name is already in `STARTER_LINTS` from item 35's slice 1, but no emitter calls into it; slices 3, 4 + 5 wire the actual malformed-shape detection). No failed-bound diagnostic integration (slice 6). No `karac query attributes` / tool-namespace catch-all formalisation (item 37 — but the silent-accept behaviour for tool namespaces is already in place because slice 2 only validates bare names). Phase target: 5.2. **Unblocks** slices 3, 4 (they can now assume bare-name validation is upstream — their job is to add the per-member shape checks against the `KnownAttributeNamespace::Diagnostic` arm) and item 37 (the tool-namespace silent-accept surface is in place; item 37 adds the read-side `karac query attributes` machinery).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — lexer + AST + parser path migration shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Lexer / parser — extend the attribute path grammar to accept `IDENT { "::" IDENT }` per syntax.md §8 (a single-segment path is the existing case; multi-segment paths are new). AST: `Attribute { path: Vec<String>, ... }` replaces the existing single-name field; downstream consumers that look up the name now read `path[-1]` with namespace context."* **`Token::ColonColon`** new lexer token in `src/token.rs` + greedy two-char lookahead in `src/lexer.rs` (`:` followed by `:` emits `ColonColon`; lone `:` stays `Token::Colon` for named args and type ascription). Kāra uses `.` for the general path separator (use / import / type paths in `parse_path_segments`), so `::` is dedicated to attribute paths per syntax.md §8 — no collision with existing language surface. **AST migration** in `src/ast/types.rs`: `Attribute.name: String` → `Attribute.path: Vec<String>`. New inherent method `Attribute::is_bare(&str) -> bool` returns `true` iff `path.len() == 1 && path[0] == name`; this is the canonical helper for downstream consumers that match a specific bare attribute (`attr.is_bare("derive")` does NOT match `#[diagnostic::derive]`). **Parser extension** in `src/parser/attributes.rs`: `parse_attribute` now consumes `IDENT (ColonColon IDENT)*` into `path` (previously just `expect_identifier()` into `name`); `parse_at_attribute` (the `@name` shorthand) and `parse_unsafe_wrapped_attribute` (the `#[unsafe(no_mangle)]` form) both wrap their single identifier in a one-element `path` vec since neither surface form carries a namespace by design. The bare `#[no_mangle]` / `#[link_section(...)]` rejection and the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection (slice 6 of lint-level-attributes) are now scoped to `path.len() == 1` so a multi-segment path like `#[diagnostic::no_mangle]` or `#[diagnostic::allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` is accepted at the parse layer (namespace dispatch in slice 2 will validate based on the namespace registry; parsing does not). **Migration surface** spanned 37 sites across 18 files: `src/{cli,ownership,interpreter,prelude,typechecker,unsafe_lint,missing_must_use_lint,codegen/functions,formatter/items,effectchecker/extern_ffi,resolver/collect,parser/items,parser/items_extern,typechecker/env_build,ownership/closure_escape,ownership/par_helpers}.rs`. Almost every site is a one-line conversion of `attr.name == "X"` to `attr.is_bare("X")` — `is_bare` reads as the right contract everywhere existing code looked up a specific bare attribute. Two sites needed structural changes: `src/parser/items.rs::scan_lint_level_attrs` got an early `if attr.path.len() != 1 { continue; }` so lint-level attributes (`#[allow]`, `#[warn]`, `#[deny]`, `#[expect]`) only match single-segment paths; the existing `attr.name` reads inside the loop became `&attr.path[0]` (the early skip guarantees length is 1). `src/formatter/items.rs::format_attributes` now writes multi-segment paths back out with `::` between segments for round-trip idempotence (`#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` formats unchanged); the linker-attr `#[unsafe(...)]` wrap-detection got an explicit `path.len() == 1` guard since `no_mangle` / `link_section` are bare-name only by design. `src/codegen/functions.rs::apply_linker_attrs` got the same `path.len() == 1` guard so codegen never inspects multi-segment paths (namespaced attributes have no codegen meaning at v1). **Test migration**: 32 sites across `tests/{parser,must_use_lint,missing_must_use_lint}.rs` converted from `.name` field reads to `.path[0]` reads (or `is_bare` calls in `find`/`any`/`all` predicates). The two `Attribute` constructors in `tests/missing_must_use_lint.rs` (`must_use_attr` + `allow_missing_must_use_attr`) updated to populate `path: vec!["X".to_string()]`. **Test surface (6 new tests in `tests/parser.rs::attr_path_slice1_*`).** `bare_name_parses_as_single_segment` (positive — `#[derive(Eq)]` produces `path == vec!["derive"]` and `is_bare("derive")` returns true). `two_segment_namespaced_parses` (`#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` on a trait produces `path == vec!["diagnostic", "on_unimplemented"]`; `is_bare("on_unimplemented")` returns false since the path is multi-segment). `three_segment_path_parses` (`#[a::b::c]` produces a three-element path). `namespaced_with_args_round_trips` (`#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(message: "x", label: "y")]` parses the path and the named args independently). `namespaced_path_does_not_trigger_bare_name_guards` (regression — `#[diagnostic::allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` is accepted at parse layer because the hard-rule rejection is bare-name-scoped; also pins that multi-segment paths do not populate `lint_overrides`). `at_attribute_stays_single_segment` (the `@name` shorthand never produces a multi-segment path). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No `KnownAttributeNamespace` dispatcher (slice 2). No `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` emission for unknown bare-name attributes (slice 2 — unknown bare names are currently still accepted silently, matching pre-slice-1 behavior). No `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` lint registration (slice 5). No `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` / `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` semantics (slices 3, 4). No integration with failed-bound diagnostics (slice 6). Phase target: 5.2. **Unblocks** slices 2-7 of item 36 (the parser/AST surface they consume is in place) AND the item-37 tool-namespace work (which reuses the same path-form lexer/parser change).

- [~] **Tool-namespaced attributes `#[TOOL::NAME(...)]`.** Spec at `design.md § Tool-Namespaced Attributes` (v60 item 37). Slice 1 (silent-accept discriminator) was incidentally landed by item 36 slice 2's namespace dispatcher (multi-segment paths in non-compiler-reserved namespaces flow through `attribute_validator::visit_attrs` unchallenged) and is now pinned by the slice 1+3 test surface; slice 2 (AST representation) is documentary — the existing `Attribute { path: Vec<String>, args, span }` from item 36 slice 1 already covers tool-namespaced attributes; slice 3 (`karac query attributes [--tool PREFIX]` subcommand + JSON output) shipped 2026-05-18; slice 5 (v1-reserved name-claim documentation in design.md + book appendix) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullets below. Slice 4 (LSP integration) is blocked on the LSP infrastructure itself (no in-tree language server today). Slice 6 (no `#[register_tool]`) is an explicit post-v1 deferral per the spec.

  - [x] **Slices 1+3 — silent-accept discriminator pinned + `karac query attributes [--tool PREFIX]` subcommand shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Attribute checker discriminator — extend the namespace dispatch from item 36 (`KnownAttributeNamespace`) to recognize the first segment of every multi-segment attribute path: if the segment matches a compiler-reserved namespace (currently only `diagnostic`), validate per the corresponding spec (item 36); otherwise treat as a tool namespace and accept silently."* and *"`karac query attributes [--tool PREFIX]` subcommand — new query command emitting a JSON list of every multi-segment attribute on every item, filtered by tool-name prefix when `--tool` is provided."* **Slice 1 (discriminator).** No code change needed in `attribute_validator.rs` — slice 2 of item 36 already passes multi-segment paths through `visit_attrs` without emitting `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` (the slice-2 walker matches on `attr.path.len() == 1` for bare-name validation only). The slice-1 work is the test pin: 18 collector tests in `tests/query_attributes.rs` exercise the rule — `#[karafmt::skip]`, `#[acmecorp::audit(...)]`, `#[a::b::c]` all flow through with zero diagnostics; bare-name unknowns still error at `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` (already pinned in `tests/resolver.rs::attr_slice2_*`). **Slice 3 (`karac query attributes`).** New collector module `src/query_attributes.rs` houses the data shapes (`AttributeQueryRecord`, `AttributeQueryArg`, `AttributeQueryValue`, `AttributeQueryFilter`) and the entry function `pub fn collect_attributes(program, filter) -> Vec<AttributeQueryRecord>`. The walker visits every attribute-bearing item kind (function, struct + field, enum + variant, trait + method, trait alias, marker trait, impl block + method, const, type alias, distinct type, extern fn, extern block + items, layout) and emits one record per **multi-segment** attribute occurrence — bare-name attributes (`#[derive]`, `#[deprecated]`, `#[must_use]`, …) are the compiler's own surface and are excluded from this read channel by design (reporting them would conflate the compiler and tool-namespaced surfaces). Records carry `path`, `args` (each with classified value: `String` / `Int` / `Bool` / `Path` / `Other` for compound expressions), `attached_to` (human-readable item identifier: `fn parse`, `struct UserRecord.id`, `impl T for S`, `impl T for S.method`, …), and `span`. **CLI plumbing.** `QueryKind::Attributes { tool_prefix: Option<String> }` enum variant; the args parser accepts `--tool=PREFIX` (and `--tool PREFIX` long-form) before the file target; the `Attributes` arm reuses the `cost-summary` "bare file path, no `.function`" shape since it's whole-file. Dispatch in `cmd_query` calls a new `query_attributes(pipeline, tool_prefix)` that runs `collect_attributes` and renders JSON via `render_attribute_query_json`. The JSON envelope is `{"tool_prefix": <prefix-or-null>, "attributes": [...]}` with each record `{"path": [...], "args": [...], "attached_to": "...", "span": {"file": "...", "line": N, "column": N}}`. Each arg is `{"name": <name-or-null>, "value": <classified-value-or-null>, "span": {...}}`; the classified value is `{"kind": "string"|"int"|"bool"|"path", "value": ...}` or `{"kind": "expr"}` for compound expressions. The render flows through the existing `json_string` / `span_to_json` helpers so the encoder behaves like every other `karac` JSON surface. Pipeline phases: only `resolve()` runs (which gates fatal parse/resolve errors); the query intentionally does not require typecheck / ownership / effectcheck — tool-namespaced attributes have no semantic effect on later phases, so we emit a usable result even when those phases would have flagged unrelated problems. The spec-listed positive cases — `#[karafmt::skip]` on a function, `#[arbitrary_tool::custom_thing(arg1: 1, arg2: "x")]` with full named-arg shape, attributes on every item kind — all flow through; the spec-listed negative cases (`E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` on bare unknowns; `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` on `#[diagnostic::*]` shape errors) continue to fire from the existing slice 2 / slice 3 / slice 4 emitters because the query is purely additive. **Help text** in `src/cli/help.rs::query`: added the `attributes` kind entry + the `--tool=PREFIX` option; updated the usage line to `karac query <kind> [flags] <target>` and the target-form note to include attributes. **Test surface (18 collector tests in `tests/query_attributes.rs`).** *Multi-segment surface (4):* simple `#[karafmt::skip]` on a function; `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(...)]` on a trait (compiler-reserved namespaces flow through the same channel — `--tool` is how a consumer focuses); bare-name attrs (`#[derive]` etc.) are excluded; three-segment path `#[a::b::c]` flows through. *`--tool` filter (3):* first-segment match keeps only matching prefix; `--tool karafmt` does not include `#[diagnostic::*]` (exact first-segment match); unknown prefix returns empty. *Arg classification (2):* string / int / bool / path / positional-ident all classified; compound expressions (`level: 1 + 2`) classified as `Other`. *`attached_to` surface (6):* struct field walks (`struct S.x`); enum variant walks (`enum E.Empty`); trait method walks (`trait T.m`); inherent impl + method (`impl S` + `impl S.m`); trait impl (`impl T for S`); const + type-alias + distinct-type (`const MAX_K`, `type Alias`, `distinct MyId`). *Empty / no-op (3):* empty program; bare-attribute-only program; source-order preservation across items and sub-items. **What slices 1+3 do *not* do.** No LSP integration (slice 4 — Phase 5.x LSP work). No design.md / book-side documentation of the `karafmt::*` / `karalint::*` / `karadoc::*` reserved names (slice 5 — documentation slice). No `#[register_tool(name)]` mechanism (slice 6 — explicit post-v1 deferral per the spec). No statement / block-level tool attributes (the spec's "attribute attached to a stmt/block" sub-bullet is exotic and the AST today doesn't carry attributes on individual statements; the documented surface for tool attributes is item-level, which the collector covers). Phase target: 5.2. Slices: (1) Attribute checker discriminator — extend the namespace dispatch from item 36 (`KnownAttributeNamespace`) to recognize the *first segment* of every multi-segment attribute path: if the segment matches a compiler-reserved namespace (currently only `diagnostic`), validate per the corresponding spec (item 36); otherwise treat as a tool namespace and accept silently. A bare-name attribute (single-segment path) that doesn't match a known compiler attribute remains `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` — the silent-on-unknown rule applies *only* to multi-segment paths, never to bare names. (2) AST representation — the existing `Attribute { path: Vec<String>, args: Vec<AttrArg>, span: Span }` shape from item 36 already covers tool-namespaced attributes; no new variant needed. The arguments are stored verbatim (parsed, not validated). Tools are responsible for their own argument-shape validation. (3) `karac query attributes [--tool PREFIX]` subcommand — new query command emitting a JSON list of every multi-segment attribute on every item, filtered by tool-name prefix when `--tool` is provided. Output shape: one record per attribute with `path` (the full path), `args` (the parsed arg list as JSON), `attached_to` (item kind + qualified name), `span` (file/line/col). The `--tool` filter is a first-segment match (`--tool karafmt` returns every `#[karafmt::*]`); without `--tool`, returns every multi-segment attribute. (4) Language-server integration — the existing LSP surfaces item-level attributes through workspace-symbol responses; extend it to include tool attributes when the LSP client requests them by namespace prefix. The compile-as-library API exposes the same `Attribute` structure. (5) v1-reserved name-claim — document `karafmt::*`, `karalint::*`, `karadoc::*` as reserved for the canonical first-party tools that will ship post-v1; user attributes against these names parse and store like any other tool attribute, but the names cannot be claimed by other tools. The reservation is documentary (in design.md and the attribute reference book appendix) — there is no compiler-side enforcement that another tool cannot collide with these names; the social authority is "first reserved, first served." (6) No `#[register_tool(name)]` mechanism at v1 — open namespace rule applies; per-project tool registration is a deferred feature (post-v1 quality-of-life addition for typo detection). Test coverage: positive — `#[karafmt::skip]` on a function parses, stores, emits no diagnostic, appears in `karac query attributes --tool karafmt` output; `#[arbitrary_tool::custom_thing(arg1: 1, arg2: "x")]` likewise — fully open namespace; multi-arg tool attributes parse with full `IDENT ":" EXPR` arg shape; tool attribute on every item kind (function, struct, enum, trait, impl, module-const) accepted; attribute attached to a stmt/block accepted with no diagnostic but documented as exotic. Negative — bare-name unknown attribute `#[no_such_thing]` still rejected with `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` (silent-on-unknown applies only to multi-segment paths); compiler-reserved namespace member with malformed args still emits `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` warn (item 36 rule, not subsumed by tool-namespace silence). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: design.md § Tool-Namespaced Attributes; item 36 attribute-namespace dispatch (shares the same `KnownAttributeNamespace` machinery — item 36 lands the `diagnostic::*` arm, this entry lands the catch-all tool-namespace arm); `karac query attributes` command lands together with this entry as the tool-facing read surface.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — v1-reserved name-claim documentation shipped 2026-05-18.** Two doc surfaces updated: `design.md § Tool-Namespaced Attributes` already enumerated the three reserved namespaces (`karafmt::*`, `karalint::*`, `karadoc::*`) with their initial members and the "first reserved, first served" social-authority framing — that side was already in place from the design.md write-up. The new work is in `docs/book/src/appendix-d-attributes.md`: added a `## Tool-namespaced attributes` section before `## Post-v1 / reserved` covering the v1 mechanism (open-namespace rule, structural discriminator vs `#[diagnostic::*]`, no-per-project-registration rationale), the three v1-reserved first-party tool namespaces with their initial members (`karafmt::skip`, `karalint::{allow,warn,deny,expect}(NAME)`, `karadoc::hidden`), the third-party-tool convention (namespace matching package or organisation name), and the three read paths (`karac query attributes`, LSP post-v1, direct AST access). The reservation is documentary — no compiler-side enforcement, no test code; user attributes against the reserved names continue to parse and store like any other tool attribute (the open-namespace rule from slices 1+3 is unchanged).

  - [ ] **Slice 4 — LSP integration (blocked).** Surface item-level tool attributes through the language server's workspace-symbol responses, filterable by namespace prefix; expose the same `Attribute` structure through the compile-as-library API. **Blocked on** the LSP infrastructure itself — karac does not yet have an in-tree language server. Reopen condition: LSP work begins in earnest (Phase 5.x), at which point this slice's collector reuses `crate::query_attributes::collect_attributes` with a prefix filter mirroring `karac query attributes --tool=PREFIX`. The compile-as-library API surface (`pub fn parse` → `Program` → `program.items[i].attributes`) is already in place; LSP just needs to call into it.

  - [->] **Slice 6 — `#[register_tool(name)]` mechanism (post-v1 deferred).** Explicit post-v1 deferral per the spec — the open-namespace rule applies at v1 (any first segment that isn't a compiler-reserved namespace is accepted as a tool attribute, no registration required). Per-project tool registration is a post-v1 quality-of-life addition for typo detection (e.g. flagging `#[karaftm::skip]` as a likely typo of `karafmt`). Reopen condition: first user report of a confusing silent-accept where a typo'd tool name escaped notice.

- [~] **`#[track_caller]` for stdlib panic-emitters — caller-location redirection.** Parser flag + resolver placement validation (slice 1) shipped 2026-05-16; slice 1 trait-method extension (sub-open closure) shipped 2026-05-18; `missing_track_caller` lint (slice 7) shipped 2026-05-18. Resolver/typechecker pass-through (slice 3) is a no-op the slice 1 wiring already preserves. Codegen call-lowering with hidden caller-location parameter (slice 4, phase-7), panic runtime integration (slice 5, phase-6/7), and stdlib annotations (slice 6, blocked on slices 4+5) remain. Implement the spec in `design.md § Error Handling > Stdlib panic-emitters report the caller's source location` and the cross-reference at `design.md § Crash Report Format > Panic site`.

  - [x] **Slice 1 — parser flag + resolver placement validation shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Attribute parser — recognize `#[track_caller]` as a function-level attribute; reject on items that aren't `fn` declarations ...; reject arguments — the attribute takes none"* and *"AST — capture as a boolean `is_track_caller: bool` field on the existing `Function` node."* Bundles spec slices 1 + 2 because (per the `#[non_exhaustive]` precedent shipped earlier this session) the AST field is the parser's storage shape — splitting them lands an unused field for one commit. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `Function.is_track_caller: bool`, defaulted to `false` at every construction site (parser sets the flag from attribute presence; `prelude.rs`'s `stub_function`, `typechecker/items.rs`'s trait-method synthesized stub, `effectchecker.rs`'s trait-method synthesized stub, `effectchecker/bounds.rs`'s trait-method scan stub all default `false` — none of those synthesized stubs represent a user-authored function so the flag is structurally `false`). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: `parse_function` calls a new `scan_track_caller_attr(&attributes)` helper that returns the flag and emits `E_TRACK_CALLER_ARGS_NOT_PERMITTED` for any occurrence carrying args (`#[track_caller(extra)]`) or a string value (`#[track_caller = "..."]`); the diagnostic is anchored at the attribute's own span. Duplicates are accepted silently — bare `#[track_caller]` is idempotent, and a "duplicate attribute" lint belongs to the lint registry (line 383) once it lands. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: new `reject_track_caller_attr(attrs, target_kind)` helper emits one `E_TRACK_CALLER_INVALID_TARGET` diagnostic per occurrence on a disallowed item, naming the target kind in the message (`"struct"`, `"enum"`, `"trait"`, `"marker trait"`, `"trait alias"`, `"impl block"`, `"struct field"`). Wired into every non-`fn` `collect_*` site: `collect_struct` (block + each field), `collect_enum`, `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_impl` (block only — impl methods are `fn`s and skip the helper). `collect_function` and impl-method walks don't call the helper because the attribute is legal there. **New `ResolveErrorKind::TrackCallerInvalidTarget`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0240` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path at line 706 and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map at line 2711 — both must stay in sync). **Test surface (7 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: `track_caller_slice1_sets_flag_on_function` (basic — attribute presence sets flag); `track_caller_slice1_function_without_attribute_has_flag_false` (regression pin); `track_caller_slice1_coexists_with_other_attributes` (the flag is set when the attribute appears alongside others like `#[must_use = "..."]`); `track_caller_slice1_rejects_paren_args` (negative pin — `#[track_caller(extra)]` produces `E_TRACK_CALLER_ARGS_NOT_PERMITTED`); `track_caller_slice1_rejects_string_value` (negative pin — `#[track_caller = "oops"]` same diagnostic); `track_caller_slice1_duplicate_attribute_is_idempotent` (two bare copies are silently idempotent at parse — pin for the no-duplicate-lint posture); `track_caller_slice1_set_on_non_fn_item_parser_does_not_reject` (the parser captures the attribute on a struct without diagnostic; placement rejection is the resolver's job). **Test surface (10 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `track_caller_slice1_accepted_on_function` / `..._on_impl_method` (positive pins — no diagnostic on the legal `fn` and impl-method placements); `track_caller_slice1_rejected_on_struct` / `..._enum` / `..._trait` / `..._marker_trait` / `..._trait_alias` / `..._impl_block` / `..._struct_field` (rejection at each disallowed site, asserting the kind name appears in the diagnostic so the role is unambiguous); `track_caller_slice1_rejection_uses_dedicated_error_kind` (pin that the new `ResolveErrorKind::TrackCallerInvalidTarget` discriminant is used rather than overloading existing kinds, AND that the message carries the symbolic `E_TRACK_CALLER_INVALID_TARGET` prefix for CLI/IDE consumers). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No call-site lowering — the codegen pass does not yet inject the hidden caller-location argument (slice 4); no panic runtime integration — `PanicRecord` doesn't yet read the caller-location parameter (slice 5); no stdlib annotations — `Option::unwrap` / `Result::unwrap` / `Vec::index` etc. don't yet carry the attribute (slice 6); no `missing_track_caller` lint (slice 7, blocked on lint registry at line 383). **Trait-method support** is a sub-open: the spec accepts the attribute on trait method declarations with last-writer-wins propagation to impls, but `TraitMethod` has no `attributes` field at the AST level yet — adding attribute support to trait methods is a separate enabling change that unblocks (a) `#[track_caller]` on trait method declarations, (b) `#[deprecated]` on trait method declarations once that lands (line 381), and (c) the broader `#[diagnostic::*]` / tool-namespaced attribute work (lines 385, 387). The slice-1 parser flag is structurally complete for the function and impl-method cases that cover the spec's stdlib-annotation slice 6. (3) Resolver / typechecker — pass through unchanged; the attribute does not affect types, effects, or generic instantiation. (4) Codegen / call lowering — for every call site whose callee is `#[track_caller]`, insert a hidden caller-location argument carrying the call site's `(file, line, col)`; if the **enclosing** function is itself `#[track_caller]`, forward its received caller-location parameter instead of the literal call site (transitivity rule); the parameter is ABI-stable within the language but never user-visible. (5) Panic runtime (`std.panic`) — when constructing a `PanicRecord`, read the caller-location parameter (if the panicking frame is `#[track_caller]`) and store it as the `site.file`/`site.line`/`site.col` triple of the Crash Report Format Field 1; the demangled function name and instruction pointer continue to identify the actual emitting frame. (6) Stdlib annotations — apply `#[track_caller]` to: `Option::unwrap`, `Option::expect`, `Result::unwrap`, `Result::expect`, `Result::unwrap_err`, `Result::expect_err`, `Vec::index` / `Slice::index` / `Array::index` and their `_mut` variants (the bare `[i]` operator desugars onto these), `Vec::first` / `Vec::last` (the panicking variants — the `.get()` / `.first_opt()` / `.last_opt()` Option-returning forms do not carry the attribute), the trapping arithmetic helpers (`i64::unchecked_div`, `i64::unchecked_rem`, the `embedded`-profile overflow-trapping named methods), the assertion macros once macros land (`assert!`, `assert_eq!`, `assert_ne!` — for v1 the assertion intrinsics in stdlib carry the attribute directly), and the diverging primitives `todo()` / `unreachable()` / `panic()`. (7) Stdlib hygiene lint — new `missing_track_caller` lint that fires on any `pub fn` in a `lib.kara` of the standard library whose declared or inferred effect set contains `panics` and which lacks `#[track_caller]`; lint level `deny` for stdlib crates, `allow` for user code. The lint is opt-in for user code (a regular `pub fn foo() with panics` does *not* require the attribute — only stdlib panic-emitters do). (8) Built-in operator panics (`a + b` overflow trap under `app`/`lib`, `a / b` div-by-zero trap, exhaustiveness violations the compiler did not statically rule out) already point at the operator's own source location — no attribute or codegen change is needed for them; this entry is exclusively about stdlib **function** panic-emitters. Test coverage: `vec.get(99).unwrap()` reports the user's `unwrap()` site as Field 1, not a frame inside `Option::unwrap`; same for `Result::expect("...")`, `Vec[i]` OOB, `i64::unchecked_div(0)`, `panic("msg")`, `todo()`, `unreachable()`; transitivity — a user `#[track_caller] fn must_be_pos(x: i32) -> u32 { if x >= 0 { x as u32 } else { panic!(...) } }` called from `caller_fn` reports `caller_fn`'s site, not `must_be_pos`'s; a `#[track_caller]` user fn that calls a `#[track_caller]` stdlib fn reports the *user fn's* caller; a non-`#[track_caller]` fn that calls a `#[track_caller]` stdlib fn reports the call site inside the wrapper (no transitivity); attribute on a non-`fn` item is rejected; attribute with arguments is rejected; trait-method `#[track_caller]` declaration is honoured by impls that don't explicitly drop it; `missing_track_caller` lint fires on a stdlib `pub fn` with `panics` effect that lacks the attribute; the lint does not fire on user-code `pub fn` with `panics`. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 1 trait-method extension (sub-open closure) shipped 2026-05-18.** The slice-1 entry flagged trait-method support as a sub-open *blocked on `TraitMethod` not carrying attributes at the AST level*. The "AST enabling change — attributes on `TraitMethod` + `Variant` nodes" entry unblocked it — `TraitMethod` gained `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` and `is_track_caller: bool`, and the parser wiring in `parse_trait_def_tail` / `parse_trait_method` already threads attributes through and calls `scan_track_caller_attr`. The slice-1 contract was structurally complete already; this entry adds the broader test surface to pin the trait-method side at the same depth as the function-level slice 1 tests. **Test surface (5 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::track_caller_slice1_trait_method_*`)**: `_without_attribute_has_flag_false` (regression pin — bare trait method has `is_track_caller == false`); `_coexists_with_other_attributes` (`#[track_caller]` + `#[deprecated]` on the same trait method both attach); `_rejects_paren_args` (`#[track_caller(extra)]` produces `E_TRACK_CALLER_ARGS_NOT_PERMITTED` on a trait method, same diagnostic as the function-level path); `_rejects_string_value` (`#[track_caller = "oops"]` same); `_per_method_independent` (mixed presence within a single trait — pins the flag is per-method, not per-trait). No production code changed: the wiring was already in place from the enabling-change entry; this closes the slice-1 sub-open by widening test coverage to match the function-level surface. The existing single positive pin `enabling_change_trait_method_track_caller_attaches` from the enabling-change entry continues to anchor the basic-attachment case.

  - [ ] **Slice 4 — codegen call-lowering with hidden caller-location parameter (phase-7 blocked).** For every call site whose callee is `#[track_caller]`, insert a hidden caller-location argument carrying `(file, line, col)`; if the enclosing function is itself `#[track_caller]`, forward its received caller-location parameter instead of the literal site (transitivity rule). Parameter is ABI-stable within the language but never user-visible. **Phase-7 territory** — touches codegen substrate (`src/codegen.rs`). Will read `Function.is_track_caller` and `TraitMethod.is_track_caller` (both already plumbed). Reopen condition: codegen-phase work begins on the phase-7 worktree.

  - [ ] **Slice 5 — panic runtime integration (phase-6/7 blocked).** When constructing a `PanicRecord`, read the caller-location parameter (if the panicking frame is `#[track_caller]`) and store it as the `site.file` / `site.line` / `site.col` triple of the Crash Report Format Field 1; the demangled function name and instruction pointer continue to identify the actual emitting frame. **Phase-6/7 territory** — touches the runtime crate (`runtime/src/panic.rs`-style file) and the codegen-emitted panic call sites. Cannot land before slice 4 (the parameter must exist before the runtime can read it).

  - [ ] **Slice 6 — stdlib annotations (blocked on slices 4+5).** Apply `#[track_caller]` to: `Option::unwrap`, `Option::expect`, `Result::unwrap`, `Result::expect`, `Result::unwrap_err`, `Result::expect_err`; `Vec::index` / `Slice::index` / `Array::index` and their `_mut` variants (the bare `[i]` operator desugars onto these); `Vec::first` / `Vec::last` (panicking variants); the trapping arithmetic helpers (`i64::unchecked_div`, `i64::unchecked_rem`, embedded-profile overflow-trapping named methods); the assertion intrinsics (`assert!`, `assert_eq!`, `assert_ne!` — for v1 the stdlib functions carry the attribute directly, since macros land later); the diverging primitives `todo()` / `unreachable()` / `panic()`. **Symbolic until slices 4+5 ship** — the attribute is just data otherwise. Could land as a no-op annotation pass on phase-5 once the AST surface is verified (the slice 7 lint below will fire on every unannotated panic-emitter, so slice 6 implicitly drives the lint clean).

  - [x] **Slice 7 — `missing_track_caller` lint shipped 2026-05-18.** New lint that fires on any `pub fn` in a `lib.kara` of the standard library whose declared or inferred effect set contains `panics` and which lacks `#[track_caller]`. **Lint registration** in `src/lints.rs::STARTER_LINTS`: `missing_track_caller` added with `default_level: Warn` and a description naming the stdlib-hygiene framing. The walker scopes emission to `stdlib_origin == true` items, so user code with `panics` does not fire — the registry default applies uniformly but the walker filter is what gates user-vs-stdlib (matching the spec's "deny for stdlib, allow for user code" rule). **New module** `src/missing_track_caller_lint.rs` mirrors `missing_must_use_lint`'s shape: takes `&Program`, `Option<&EffectCheckResult>`, `&CliLintOverrides`; walks every `Item::Function` and every `Item::ImplBlock`'s inherent-impl methods (`trait_name == None`); fires on `stdlib_origin && is_pub && !is_track_caller && !has_allow(missing_track_caller) && has_panics_effect`. The panics check consults declared effects (`Function.effects` matched against `EffectVerbKind::Panics`) first, then falls back to `EffectCheckResult.inferred_effects[key]` where `key` is `"name"` for free fns and `"Target.method"` for inherent methods — the same key shape `EffectChecker` uses internally. Trait-impl methods (impl blocks with `trait_name = Some(...)`) are skipped: `#[track_caller]` on a trait method declaration propagates to all impls, so linting impl methods would force every implementor to re-annotate. **Diagnostic shape** matches the other lint modules' three-piece rustc-style (primary + `= note:` + `= help:`). The primary names the function (`stdlib pub fn <name> has panics in its effect set but lacks #[track_caller]`); the note explains *why* (`panic from this function reports the stdlib frame as the panic site — callers see the implementation line, not their own call site`); the help suggests the fix (`add #[track_caller] above the function declaration so the panic-site fields (file/line/col) point at the caller`). **CLI wiring** in `src/cli.rs`: a new `render_missing_track_caller_lint_diag` mirrors `render_missing_must_use_lint_diag`; the dispatch happens immediately after the `missing_must_use` lint in the render loop and pipes `pipeline.effects.as_ref()` so the lint sees the effect-checker output. The lint runs unconditionally when the effect-check pass succeeded; when it didn't (earlier-phase fatal error short-circuited), the lint silently produces zero diagnostics rather than firing on absent data. **Test surface (14 tests in `tests/missing_track_caller_lint.rs`)**: 4 positive (fires on stdlib pub fn with inferred panics, fires on stdlib pub fn with declared panics, fires on inherent impl method, diagnostic carries note and help) + 7 negative-space (silent when `#[track_caller]` present, silent when `#[allow(missing_track_caller)]` present, silent on user-origin function, silent on private function, silent when no panics effect, silent on trait-impl method, silent when effects argument is None) + 3 CLI cascade (`-A` suppresses, `-D` promotes to error, `-D warnings` promotes to error). Tests use synthetic AST + hand-constructed `EffectCheckResult` like `missing_must_use_lint`'s test surface — the lint is purely data-consultative so end-to-end parser/resolver/effectcheck plumbing isn't needed to exercise it. **What slice 7 does *not* do.** No actual stdlib annotation pass (slice 6 — the annotations are what drive this lint clean). No baseline test against real stdlib source (the way `missing_must_use_lint` has a `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` sentinel) — adding one is a forward step once a stdlib panic-emitter inventory exists; today the synthetic-AST coverage is the regression surface. Pre-slice-4/5/6, the lint already fires correctly on candidate-set discovery; the slice-6 annotation pass will drive it clean.

- [x] **AST enabling change — attributes on `TraitMethod` + `Variant` nodes shipped 2026-05-17.** Resolves the trait-method-support sub-open flagged in the `#[track_caller]` slice 1 entry (line 391) and the variant/trait-method sub-open flagged in the `#[deprecated]` slices 1+2+3a entry (line 381). Two AST surface extensions in `src/ast/items.rs`: (1) `Variant` gains `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` (defaulted to empty in any synthesized construction) and `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>` — the spec's variant-level `#[deprecated]` target now has a place to attach. (2) `TraitMethod` gains `attributes: Vec<Attribute>`, `doc_comment: Option<String>`, `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>`, and `is_track_caller: bool` — covering the spec's last-writer-wins propagation rule (the impl-level `Function.is_track_caller` overrides this when set; the codegen slice consults both). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs` (`parse_variant` now calls `parse_attributes` after collecting doc comments and threads them through; `scan_deprecated_attr` produces the payload) and `src/parser/items_trait.rs` (`parse_trait_def_tail` now collects per-item attributes before dispatching to `parse_trait_method`; `parse_trait_method` takes `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` as an arg and calls both `scan_track_caller_attr` + `scan_deprecated_attr`). **Visibility change**: `Parser::scan_track_caller_attr` was promoted from `fn` to `pub(crate) fn` so the trait-method parser in the sibling impl block can call it. **Attributes on associated-type declarations** are rejected with the new `E_ATTR_ON_ASSOC_TYPE_DECL` diagnostic — `AssocTypeDecl` has no `attributes` field today and the v1 surface explicitly doesn't include them; silently dropping attributes attached to `type Item;` inside a trait body would mask user intent. **Resolver placement-rejection extensions** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: `collect_enum` now walks `e.variants` and rejects `#[track_caller]` and `#[non_exhaustive]` at each variant (both type-level-only per spec). `collect_trait` walks `t.items` and rejects `#[non_exhaustive]` on each `TraitItem::Method`; `#[track_caller]` and `#[deprecated]` are accepted on trait methods (both legal targets per spec). **Test surface (9 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: `enabling_change_variant_captures_attributes` (basic positive — `#[deprecated]` on a variant attaches and populates the payload); `enabling_change_variant_bare_deprecated_attaches`; `enabling_change_trait_method_captures_attributes`; `enabling_change_trait_method_track_caller_attaches` (the headline — `#[track_caller]` on a trait method declaration now sets `is_track_caller = true`); `enabling_change_trait_method_doc_comment_captured` (regression pin — doc comments before a trait method now attach); `enabling_change_attr_on_assoc_type_decl_rejected` (E_ATTR_ON_ASSOC_TYPE_DECL negative pin); `enabling_change_unsafe_fn_in_trait_with_attribute` (the `unsafe fn` dispatch in the trait body must thread attributes through, not lose them); `enabling_change_attr_on_tuple_variant` / `..._struct_variant` (the attribute attaches to every variant kind, not just unit variants). **Test surface (6 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `enabling_change_track_caller_on_enum_variant_rejected`; `enabling_change_non_exhaustive_on_enum_variant_rejected`; `enabling_change_non_exhaustive_on_trait_method_rejected`; `enabling_change_track_caller_on_trait_method_accepted` (the spec's "trait method declarations are accepted" positive pin); `enabling_change_deprecated_on_enum_variant_accepted` (the spec's variant-level deprecation positive pin); `enabling_change_deprecated_on_trait_method_accepted`. **What this entry does *not* do.** No codegen — the `is_track_caller` flag on `TraitMethod` is structurally captured but the codegen pass doesn't yet propagate it to impl methods at synthesis time (that's slice 4 of the `#[track_caller]` entry at line 391). No use-site warning for `#[deprecated]` on variants/trait methods (slice 4 of line 381, blocked on lint registry at line 383). **Still-pending sub-opens** flagged in those parent entries: attribute support on `TypeAliasDef`, `ConstDecl` (no `attributes` field today either) — both items the spec lists as legal `#[deprecated]` targets. Those AST nodes are smaller surface than `Variant`/`TraitMethod` (no nested items to walk) but still touch every existing pass that walks them; tracked as a follow-up.

- [x] **AST enabling change — attributes on `ConstDecl` + `TypeAliasDef` nodes shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the remaining sub-open flagged in the `TraitMethod`/`Variant` enabling change above — `TypeAliasDef` and `ConstDecl` were both spec-listed `#[deprecated]` targets but had no `attributes` field. Two AST surface extensions in `src/ast/items.rs`: `ConstDecl` gains `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` and `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>`; `TypeAliasDef` gains the same two fields. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: `parse_const_decl` and `parse_type_alias` both take `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` as a new first argument (threaded from the `parse_item` dispatcher's per-item attribute collection — the dispatcher was already collecting attributes; the two `Token::Const` and `Token::Type` arms now pass them through instead of dropping them).
