Both functions call `scan_deprecated_attr` and store the payload on the AST node. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: `collect_const` and `collect_type_alias` both call `reject_non_exhaustive_attr(attrs, "module const" / "type alias")` and `reject_track_caller_attr(attrs, ...)` — neither attribute is legal on these item kinds (`#[non_exhaustive]` is type-level only on `pub struct` / `pub enum`; `#[track_caller]` is fn-only). `#[deprecated]` is accepted on both (spec-listed targets); no rejection helper is called for it. **Test surface (5 parser tests + 6 resolver tests)** covering positive payload capture, regression pins (no attribute → empty field), the long-form deprecation shape, and the four cross-product rejection sites. **What this entry does *not* do.** No use-site `#[deprecated]` warning emission on consts / type aliases (still blocked on lint emission infrastructure — slice 4 of the lint-level-attributes entry at line 385). No `lint_overrides` field on `ConstDecl`/`TypeAliasDef` (slice 4 of lint-level entry will add it across all attribute-bearing nodes alongside the cascade). The parser-captured `deprecation` field is structurally complete; the warning emission will read it once the cascade infrastructure lands.

- [x] **Identifier case-class enforcement.** Enforce the case-class rule specified in `design.md § Identifiers and Naming`. Lexer classifies each `Ident` token as Type / Const / Value by its character pattern (see `syntax.md §1.5`). Parser checks the class at every declaration site — `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `type` / `distinct` / generic param / const generic param / associated type / `effect resource` require Type-class; `fn` / function-body `let` / param / field / `mod` / `layout` / effect group / effect verb require Value-class; `const` requires Const-class. Mismatch emits a structured diagnostic with position-aware wording and a suggested rename. `#[kara_name = "..."]` attribute on `extern` items provides the FFI escape hatch (CN-7). Non-ASCII identifiers remain a parse error (Unicode deferred). No-op for existing codebase — all current Kāra source already follows the convention. Test coverage for every site in `tests/parser.rs` (snake_case struct/enum/variant/trait/type-alias rejected, PascalCase fn/param/field/extern-fn rejected, snake_case const-generic/assoc-type/generic-param rejected, PascalCase layout name rejected, single-upper Type-class accepted, leading-underscore Value-class accepted, `#[kara_name]` skip-check accepted, let-binding deferred to resolver).

- [~] **`#[profile(P1, P2, ...)]` attribute.** Function/module attribute asserting compatibility with a specific set of project profiles. Compile error if the function's transitive effect set isn't compatible with the *intersection* of the listed profiles' constraints (function must satisfy the strictest constraint from any listed profile). Slices 1+2 (parser + AST + resolver validation) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullet below. Slice 3 (effect-checker integration) shipped 2026-05-18 — see sub-bullet below. The spec also references `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary; the current manifest carries a singular `[package].profile = "..."` field — see the `[->]` sub-bullet below for the deferral. Stdlib `core` layer is the first major user; portability marking becomes structural rather than convention-based. The attribute name `profile` is chosen over `profile_compatible` for consistency with `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2 — parser + AST + resolver validation shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Parser: recognize `#[profile(...)]` with comma-separated profile name list."* and *"Resolver: validate names against profiles defined in `kara.toml`; unknown names are a parse-level diagnostic."* **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `Function.profile_compat: Vec<String>`, defaulted to `Vec::new()` at every construction site (parser sets the list from attribute presence; the synthesized stubs in `prelude.rs::stub_function`, `typechecker/items.rs`, `effectchecker.rs`, `effectchecker/bounds.rs` all default empty — none represent user-authored functions). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `pub(crate) fn scan_profile_attr(attrs) -> Vec<String>` reads bare positional identifiers across all `#[profile(...)]` occurrences on the function and accumulates into a single list (slice 3 dedupes at intersection-compute time). Reject everything else with focused parse diagnostics: `E_PROFILE_NO_PROFILES` (empty arg list / bare `#[profile]`), `E_PROFILE_STRING_VALUE` (`#[profile = "..."]` shorthand or `#[profile("embedded")]` string positional), `E_PROFILE_NAMED_ARG` (`#[profile(name: embedded)]` / `#[profile(name = embedded)]`), `E_PROFILE_NON_IDENT_ARG` (any other expression — integer, bool, struct literal, …). Duplicates within one attribute (`#[profile(a, a)]`) tolerated at parse — slice 3 dedupes. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: new `reject_profile_attr(attrs, target_kind)` mirrors `reject_track_caller_attr` and is wired into every non-fn `collect_*` site (`collect_struct` block + field, `collect_enum` block + variant, `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_impl`, `collect_const`, `collect_type_alias`); produces `error[E_PROFILE_INVALID_TARGET]` naming the target kind. New `validate_profile_names(f)` walks `f.profile_compat` against the closed v1 set (`default` / `embedded` / `kernel`, mirroring `CompileProfile` from `src/manifest.rs`) and emits `error[E_UNKNOWN_PROFILE]` on each unknown name; the diagnostic lists the valid set and anchors at the function's span (per-arg span tracking is a future refinement once the scan helper threads it through). **New `ResolveErrorKind::ProfileInvalidTarget` + `UnknownProfile`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0244` / `E0245` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map — both stay in sync per the established pattern). **Test surface (10 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::profile_slice1_*`)**: `single_profile_captured` (basic — one profile in the list); `multi_profile_captured` (`#[profile(embedded, kernel)]` → both names); `absent_attribute_leaves_empty` (regression pin); `multiple_attributes_accumulate` (two `#[profile]` attributes append into one list); `rejects_empty_arg_list` / `rejects_string_shorthand` / `rejects_string_positional` / `rejects_named_arg` / `rejects_integer_arg` (one per malformed shape, each pinning the specific symbolic-code emission); `set_on_non_fn_item_parser_does_not_reject` (parser captures uniformly; placement rejection is the resolver's job). **Test surface (13 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs::profile_slice12_*`)**: `accepted_on_function_with_known_profile` / `accepted_on_function_with_all_three_known` (positive pins for each known profile and all-three combination); `rejects_unknown_profile_name` (basic unknown — names the offending profile and emits the symbolic code); `unknown_diagnostic_lists_valid_profiles` (the diagnostic enumerates `default` / `embedded` / `kernel` so the user can self-correct); `rejects_one_unknown_among_known` (per-name checking; one bad name doesn't suppress good ones); `rejected_on_struct` / `..._enum` / `..._trait` / `..._impl_block` / `..._module_const` / `..._type_alias` / `..._struct_field` (rejection at each disallowed site, asserting the kind name appears in the message); `rejection_uses_dedicated_error_kinds` (pin that both new discriminants round-trip). **What slices 1+2 do *not* do.** No effect-checker integration — the `profile_compat` list is structurally captured but no per-call constraint check fires (slice 3). No module-level placement — `#[profile]` on a module is part of the spec but blocked on the module-attribute AST surface (separate enabling change). No `kara.toml`-driven validation — the resolver validates against the closed `CompileProfile` enum since the manifest carries a singular `profile` field today (see `[->]` below). Phase target: 5.2.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — effect-checker integration shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Effect checker: for each function with `#[profile(...)]`, intersect the listed profiles' constraint sets and check the function's transitive effect set against the intersection; emit a focused diagnostic on any forbidden effect."* **New module** `src/effectchecker/profile_compat.rs` houses `check_profile_compat(&mut self)` plus the free helper `profile_forbids_effect(CompileProfile, &Effect) -> bool`. The helper duplicates the per-profile forbidden-effect table from `extern_ffi::profile_forbids` but is keyed on an explicit `CompileProfile` argument rather than `self.profile` — the attribute names target profiles independent of the active build profile, and the two checks now have distinct surfaces (`ProfileViolation` for extern declarations under the build profile, `ProfileIncompatibleEffect` for `#[profile(...)]`-annotated functions under any listed profile). The forbidden tables agree by construction: `default` forbids nothing, `embedded` forbids `allocates(Heap)`, `kernel` forbids `allocates(*)` / `panics` / `blocks` / `suspends`. **Walker shape** mirrors the `missing_track_caller` lint: walk every `Item::Function` and every `Item::ImplBlock` inherent-or-trait-method (both are kept — the attribute is structurally valid on both, and the resolver does not distinguish). Inherent methods key as `Type.method` to match the `inferred_effects` lookup convention; free fns key as `name`. Functions with empty `profile_compat` skip; functions whose declared profile list contains an unknown name skip entirely (the resolver already emitted `E_UNKNOWN_PROFILE`, so we don't pile a stale-data effect error on top). **Dedup** is done at check time — `#[profile(embedded, embedded)]` or two `#[profile]` attrs naming the same profile collapse to one constraint contributor, so one diagnostic per offending effect is emitted regardless of duplication. **Effect-source selection.** The check reads `self.inferred_effects[key]` — by Phase A's `collect_function_info` seeding, this map contains the declared set for `Explicit` declarations *and* the inferred propagation result, so a function declaring `with allocates(Heap)` and a function inferring `allocates(Heap)` from a `Vec.new()` call both surface the same way. The check runs in Phase B after `check_with_e_unification` so the inferred set is fully settled. **New `EffectErrorKind::ProfileIncompatibleEffect`** in `src/effectchecker.rs`; mapped to `E0407` in `src/cli.rs` (the per-effect-error mapping table — the legacy duplicate path inherited the same variant via the exhaustive match, so no second site needs touching). **Diagnostic shape.** One error per offending effect, naming the function, the declared profile list, the effect (with resource in parens for resource verbs), and the profile(s) that forbid it. When only one listed profile forbids the effect the diagnostic reads `forbidden by the \`<P>\` profile`; when two or more forbid it the phrasing shifts to `forbidden by the strictest of \`P1, P2, …\` (forbidden by \`P_a\`, \`P_b\`, …)` so the user sees the tightening came from the intersection rather than a single profile. **Test surface (17 effect-checker tests in `tests/effectchecker.rs::profile_slice3_*`)**: `default_allows_all_effects_via_attribute` (default-profile baseline — `allocates(Heap)` accepted); `embedded_accepts_pure_function` (no effects, no violation); `embedded_rejects_heap_allocates` (the canonical case — message asserts symbolic code, fn name, profile name, effect rendering); `embedded_allows_non_heap_allocates` (user-defined resource `Arena` passes `embedded` since only `Heap` is forbidden); `kernel_rejects_panics` / `kernel_rejects_blocks` / `kernel_rejects_suspends` / `kernel_rejects_allocates_any_resource` (one per kernel-forbidden verb — `blocks` is triggered via an `extern "C"` call to inherit the ABI default, `suspends` via `Receiver.recv()`, `panics` via `todo()`, `allocates(Arena)` via a declared effect); `intersection_tightens_one_profile_forbids` (`#[profile(embedded, kernel)]` + `panics` — only `kernel` forbids, diagnostic names `the \`kernel\` profile` and echoes the full declared list); `intersection_tightens_multiple_profiles_forbid` (`#[profile(embedded, kernel)]` + `allocates(Heap)` — both forbid, "strictest of" phrasing kicks in); `two_offending_effects_yield_two_errors` (per-effect granularity — two diagnostics for `allocates(Heap)` + `panics` under `kernel`); `inherent_method_checked` (`Type.method` key shape — method-level violation surfaces with the type-qualified name); `inferred_effect_drives_check` (the declared list is empty but inferred carries `allocates(Heap)` from a `Vec.new()` call — confirms the post-inference map is the source of truth); `unknown_profile_skips_check` (`#[profile(yolo)]` produces no profile-compat diagnostic since the resolver already errored); `dedupe_within_attr` (duplicate profile names emit one diagnostic, not two); `diagnostic_uses_dedicated_error_kind` (kind discriminant round-trip); `absent_attribute_silent` (functions without `#[profile]` never produce profile-compat diagnostics regardless of their effect set). **What slice 3 does *not* do.** No module-level enforcement — the attribute is still function-only at the AST level, so a module-level `#[profile(...)]` is still parser-blocked. No `kara.toml`-driven validation — see the `[->]` sub-bullet below. Phase target: 5.2.

  - [ ] **Sub-open — `kara.toml` `profiles = [...]` array.** The spec entry references `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary, but the current manifest carries a singular `[package].profile = "..."` field (single profile per package, not an array). Adding a manifest-level `profiles` array is a separate enabling change; until it lands, the resolver validates against the closed `CompileProfile` enum's known set. Reopen condition: user request for multi-profile package declarations or a custom-profile mechanism beyond the three built-ins.

- [x] **C-string literals `c"..."` — lex acceptance.** Spec lives at design.md § C-String Literals (v60 item 18). Today the lexer rejects `c"..."` with a focused diagnostic that points at the spec ("specced for v1 but lex acceptance lands in Phase 5.2"); the work here is to graduate the prefix from rejected to recognized. Sub-steps: (1) `Token::CStringLiteral { bytes: Vec<u8>, source_len: i64 }` variant in `src/token.rs` — `bytes` excludes the trailing NUL (the codegen layer appends it); `source_len` records the textual length for `len()` / `as_bytes()` introspection without re-walking. (2) Lexer dispatch arm — add `b'c' if self.peek() == b'"' => self.c_string()` between the existing `f"`-arm and the reserved-prefix catch-all. (3) `c_string()` method — body parsing identical to `string()` plus the `\xHH` hex-byte escape (already implemented for byte-literals, lift the helper); `\u{...}` Unicode escapes encode to UTF-8 bytes. (4) Interior-NUL guard — any escape that produces a `0x00` byte (`\0`, `\x00`, `\u{0}`) is a lex error `error[E_INTERIOR_NUL_IN_C_STRING]` with the message from design.md, pointing at the offending escape. (5) Update the existing `test_v60_reserved_string_prefix_diagnostic` in `tests/lexer.rs` to drop the Phase-5.2-gating diagnostic and add positive lex tests for the new token shape (empty, ASCII, escape sequences, Unicode escapes producing multi-byte UTF-8). Parser handling and the stdlib `CStr` / `CString` types ship in Phase 8 (see follow-up entry below); this Phase 5.2 entry is lex-level only. (Phase 5.2 — items 3, 18, 22 land together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [x] **Field offsets `offset_of[T](field)` + `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec lives at design.md § Field Offsets (v60 item 25). The `offset_of` intrinsic shipped earlier and `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` ship on top of slice 2 of the strict-provenance work (line 511). See the two `[x]` sub-bullets below. **API-shape deviation note.** The spec's full container_of takes a field-path syntactic argument (`ptr.container_of[T, F](field_ptr, inner.y)`); v1 ships the offset form (`ptr.container_of[T, F](field_ptr, offset_of[Outer](inner.y))`) where the offset is computed by a separate `offset_of` call. The two forms are semantically identical at the lowering level; the field-path-sugar form requires new method-call turbofish parsing (the current parser doesn't accept `obj.method[T](args)` shapes) and lands as a parser-sugar follow-up. Tracked at the container_of sub-bullet below.

  - [x] **`offset_of[T](field.path)` intrinsic shipped.** Parser special-form in `src/parser/stmts.rs::parse_offset_of_special_form`, dispatched from `src/parser/exprs.rs:1130` when an identifier `offset_of` is followed by `[`. Argument grammar is `FIELD_PATH = IDENT ("." IDENT)*` parsed as a dotted identifier sequence, *not* as an expression — indexing / method calls / dereferences inside the parens are rejected at parse with `error[E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH]`. **AST** `ExprKind::OffsetOf { ty: TypeExpr, field_path: Vec<String> }` in `src/ast/exprs.rs:229`. **Typechecker** `infer_offset_of` in `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs:42` walks each path segment against `env.structs`, descending into nested struct field types; result type is `usize`. **Diagnostic family**: `E_OFFSET_OF_GENERIC_PARAM` (type-parameter target), `E_OFFSET_OF_OPAQUE_TYPE` (opaque foreign type — consulted via `env.opaque_foreign_types`), `E_OFFSET_OF_NON_STRUCT_TARGET` (primitives, enums, walk-into-non-struct on a nested segment), `E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH` (empty path or non-identifier segment forms — parser-side), `E_OFFSET_OF_UNKNOWN_FIELD` (segment doesn't name a field on the current struct; diagnostic enumerates the available field names). Private-field access from outside the defining module routes through the standard `check_cross_module_field_access` rather than a dedicated `E_OFFSET_OF_PRIVATE_FIELD` (the standard cross-module field-access diagnostic is what fires — same load-bearing surface, different symbolic code). **Const-evaluator** path: `compile_offset_of` in `src/codegen/exprs.rs:324` lowers to a literal `usize` constant via inkwell's `TargetData::offset_of_element` (chained across nested segments); no runtime arithmetic is emitted. Because the LLVM struct type the codegen consults is the post-layout-transformation type, layout-block SoA-transformed structs return the runtime (physical) offset automatically — no special-casing needed. **Test surface** (`tests/typechecker.rs::test_offset_of_*`): returns usize, first field, nested path, unknown field rejected, opaque type rejected, non-struct rejected, walk-into-non-struct rejected, indexing-form parser-rejected, call-form parser-rejected. E2E codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_offset_of_*`: first field == 0 with `#[repr(C)]`, second field, nested path. **Sub-opens** still attached to this half: (a) no `W_OFFSET_OF_UNION_FIELD` warning — depends on union support landing at line 515; (b) no explicit regression test for the SoA layout-block case — the behaviour is correct by construction (TargetData walks the lowered type) but a pinned test would catch a future layout-pipeline regression; (c) no dedicated `E_OFFSET_OF_ENUM_VARIANT` / `E_OFFSET_OF_PRIVATE_FIELD` symbolic codes — the funneling through `E_OFFSET_OF_NON_STRUCT_TARGET` / `check_cross_module_field_access` is intentional today, but if the diagnostic catalogue is curated for stable symbolic codes per kind, splitting these out is a cosmetic follow-up.

  - [x] **`ptr.container_of[T, F](field_ptr, offset)` / `ptr.container_of_mut[T, F](field_ptr, offset)` stdlib helpers shipped 2026-05-18.** Registered in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs` alongside the slice-2 `ptr.*` entries: `generic_params: ["T", "F"]`, params `[*const F, usize]` / `[*mut F, usize]`, return `*const T` / `*mut T`. `T` is the enclosing type (returned), `F` is the field type (inferred from the pointer arg). **Codegen** in `src/codegen/method_call.rs::compile_ptr_module_call`: lowers to integer subtraction (`field_ptr_i64 - offset_i64`), which is the i64-pointer-ABI collapse of the spec's `field_ptr.with_addr(field_ptr.addr() - offset)` — equivalent under the current ABI; the slice-3 docstring covers the rationale. **Unsafe enforcement** in `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `top_level_unsafe` seeded with both names; the existing OpWalker `MethodCall` arm catches the dotted `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` against the registry. **Test surface (4 typechecker + 3 unsafe-lint + 2 codegen)**: typechecker — `container_of_returns_const_ptr_to_t` / `container_of_mut_returns_mut_ptr_to_t` (positive shape pins; both use `offset_of[Outer](inner.y)` as the offset source), `container_of_with_wrong_arity_rejected` (arity check), `container_of_pointer_arg_is_required` (pointer-shape unification against `*const F`). Unsafe-lint — `ptr.container_of` and `ptr.container_of_mut` outside `unsafe { }` produce the expected diagnostic; both inside `unsafe { }` are silent. Codegen — both `container_of` and `container_of_mut` compile; the integer-subtract instruction appears in the IR for `container_of`. **API-shape deviation.** The spec's full container_of takes a *field-path* argument syntactically equivalent to the `offset_of` field-path (`ptr.container_of[T, F](field_ptr, inner.y)`). v1 takes a `usize` offset instead; the user composes via `offset_of[T](inner.y)` separately at the call site. The two forms are semantically identical — the v1 form is just a desugared version. Lifting to the spec's sugar requires extending the parser to recognize `obj.method[T](args)` shapes (method-call turbofish) and to switch the second argument's parse mode to field-path; tracked as a sugar follow-up and not a load-bearing v1 gap. **Reopen condition for the sugar:** method-call turbofish parsing + field-path-arg recognition in the `ptr.container_of` site. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; ABI-collapse codegen ships with slice 3 of the strict-provenance work at line 511.)

- [x] **Strict-provenance pointer APIs `ptr.addr` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.expose` / `ptr.from_exposed` shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec lives at design.md § Pointer Provenance (v60 item 20). Three slices: cast rejection, stdlib API surface, codegen lowering — each closed via its own sub-bullet below. Closes the line-509 blocker on `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` (the spec lowers them through `with_addr` / `addr`, which are now available).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `ptr ↔ int` cast rejection shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Cast-rejection — extend the existing `as`-cast typechecker to reject all four `ptr ↔ usize` casts."* The rule is widened to **any integer width**, not just `usize` — otherwise users could circumvent strict-provenance via an intermediate `as u32` / `as i64` cast. **Implementation** in `src/typechecker.rs::check_cast_pair`: two new arms placed immediately before the generic-fallthrough. `Type::Pointer { .. } as integer` emits `error[E_PTR_TO_INT_CAST_FORBIDDEN]` naming both `ptr.addr(p)` (the safer default) and `ptr.expose(p)` (the round-trip case) so the user can pick the right primitive without reading the spec. `integer as Type::Pointer { .. }` emits `error[E_INT_TO_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN]` naming both `ptr.with_addr(base, addr)` (reseat-existing-pointer form) and `ptr.from_exposed[T](addr)` (round-trip form) — the spec deliberately leaves the choice to the user since the compiler can't reliably guess which is in scope. Both diagnostics use `TypeErrorKind::InvalidCast` (mapped to `E0210` in `src/cli.rs`) — the symbolic code lives in the message body per the existing convention used by `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` / `E_INT_AS_CHAR` / `E_INT_AS_BOOL` / `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL`. **Test surface (8 tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::provenance_slice1_*`)**: `ptr_const_as_usize_rejected` / `ptr_mut_as_usize_rejected` (the canonical `usize` cases); `ptr_as_i64_also_rejected` (confirms the rule covers non-`usize` integer widths — the design intent that a user can't circumvent via intermediate cast); `usize_as_ptr_const_rejected` / `usize_as_ptr_mut_rejected` (reverse direction); `int_as_int_still_accepted` (regression pin — usize widening / narrowing still works); `diagnostic_names_ptr_addr_suggestion` (E_PTR_TO_INT diagnostic surfaces both `ptr.addr` and `ptr.expose`); `diagnostic_names_with_addr_and_from_exposed` (E_INT_TO_PTR diagnostic surfaces both `ptr.with_addr` and `ptr.from_exposed`). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No stdlib `ptr` API — the diagnostic messages name `ptr.addr` / `ptr.expose` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.from_exposed` but those functions are not yet callable; that surface lands in slice 2. No `&T → *_ T` reference-to-raw cast rejection — tracked under line 517 (the raw-pointer-construction entry); the spec calls that `E_REF_TO_RAW_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN` and the ergonomic story is `ptr.const(...)` / `ptr.mut(...)` which is also part of line 517. Raw-to-raw casts (`*const T as *mut T` etc.) currently funnel through the generic-fallthrough "cannot cast" diagnostic — out of scope for slice 1 (they're not in the strict-provenance forbidden set).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — stdlib `ptr` API surface shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Stdlib `ptr` module — generic functions `addr` / `with_addr` / `with_addr_mut` / `expose` / `expose_mut` / `from_exposed` (unsafe) / `from_exposed_mut` (unsafe)."* **`ptr` module registration**: `src/resolver.rs` adds `push(self, "ptr", SymbolKind::Module)` alongside the existing `env` / `process` magic modules — local bindings named `ptr` shadow the module per the standard scope rules. **Seven function signatures** in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs` (sibling to `env.var` / `process.exit`): `ptr.addr` / `ptr.expose` (`[T](p: *const T) -> usize`), `ptr.expose_mut` (`[T](p: *mut T) -> usize`), `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.with_addr_mut` (`[T](p, addr: usize) -> *const T` / `*mut T`), `ptr.from_exposed` / `ptr.from_exposed_mut` (`[T](addr: usize) -> *const T` / `*mut T`). Function names cannot syntactically contain `.`, so the entries are registered programmatically rather than as baked `.kara` source — the same pattern `env.var` / `process.exit` use. **Method-call dispatch** in `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call`: the parser produces `MethodCall { object: Ident("ptr"), method: "addr" }` for `ptr.addr(p)`, so a new `ptr` arm routes through `check_call_args_with_substitution_full` — the full generic-aware path. The simpler `env` arm uses `check_assignable` directly, which would silently accept any argument against a `*const T` slot because `(Type::TypeParam(_), _) => true` in `types_compatible`; the full-substitution path instantiates `T` to a fresh metavar so the outer `*const ?T` shape unifies properly. **Type-system substrate** in `src/typechecker/inference.rs::unify_types` and `src/typechecker/types.rs::types_compatible`: missing `Type::Pointer` arms added (mutability must match — `*const T` does not unify with `*mut T`; the strict-provenance APIs `with_addr` / `with_addr_mut` provide the explicit constness-conversion path). Without these arms `unify_types(*const ?T0, *const i64)` fell through to the wildcard-false branch, so `?T0` never bound — generic-aware ptr dispatch surfaced this gap. **Unsafe enforcement** in `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `top_level_unsafe` seeded with `"ptr.from_exposed"` and `"ptr.from_exposed_mut"`; the `OpWalker::MethodCall` arm extended to match the dotted name (`format!("{mod}.{method}")`) against the registry when the object is a bare `Identifier`, treating the leading identifier as a magic module rather than a value. The path-form callee arm (`OpWalker::Call` with `ExprKind::Path` callee) also joins segments with `.` — covers the explicit-generic-args form `ptr.from_exposed[T](addr)` if it ever lands. The diagnostic shape matches the existing `Vec.get_unchecked` precedent: lint name `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`, help text directs the user to wrap in `unsafe { ... }` with a `// Safety:` comment. **Test surface (9 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::provenance_slice2_*` + 7 unsafe-lint tests in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs::test_ptr_*`)**: typechecker — each of the seven functions accepts the correct argument shape and returns the correct type; round-trip pattern `with_addr(p, addr(p) | 1)` typechecks; wrong-argument-type rejected (regression pin against the `(TypeParam, _) => true` permissiveness bug). Unsafe-lint — `ptr.from_exposed` / `ptr.from_exposed_mut` outside `unsafe { }` produce the expected diagnostic; both inside `unsafe { }` are silent; `ptr.addr` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.expose` are safe and produce no diagnostic regardless of context. **What slice 2 does *not* do.** No codegen lowering — calls typecheck but `cargo run` won't actually execute them (slice 3 ships the LLVM `ptrtoint` / `inttoptr` lowering with provenance metadata). No explicit-generic-args path-form (`ptr.from_exposed[i64](addr)` doesn't bind T via the `[T]` syntax — T is inferred from the return-type context, which works for every realistic use site). No effect-system declaration — the seven functions have no declared effects; if a future spec entry assigns them an effect (e.g. `expose` could be argued to belong in a `reads(Provenance)` category), the seeding lives next to the env.functions registration and is a one-line change. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work.)

  - [x] **Slice 3 — codegen lowering shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec sentence honoured: *"`addr` and `with_addr` lower to LLVM `ptrtoint` / `inttoptr` … `expose` and `from_exposed` lower to the same instructions."* Dispatch lives in `src/codegen/method_call.rs::compile_method_call`, sibling to the other early-receiver arms (`unwrap`/`expect`, indexed-receiver, field-receiver). A new helper `compile_ptr_module_call` matches the seven method names and emits the appropriate cast. Skipped when a local binding shadows `ptr` — mirrors the typechecker and resolver shadow rules. **ABI note (load-bearing).** Under the current codegen ABI, raw pointer kinds (`*const T` / `*mut T`) lower to LLVM `i64` at every function-signature and binding-slot boundary (see the fallthrough in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` — there's no `TypeKind::Pointer` arm; the wildcard returns `i64`). Under that ABI, all four ptr↔int operations in the strict-provenance API are *identity at the LLVM level*: the address bits round-trip losslessly through the i64 slot. The helper therefore emits `ptrtoint` only when a receiver actually flows as `BasicValueEnum::PointerValue` (uncommon but possible for an intermediate SSA value) and falls through to pass-through otherwise. **Test surface (6 tests in `tests/codegen.rs::test_ir_ptr_*` + 1 round-trip)**: each of the seven methods compiles without falling through to the "method dispatch fell through" diagnostic; round-trip `addr` → `with_addr` → `addr` produces an equality the caller can observe. Pure-LLVM IR tests rather than execution tests because the linker-side e2e harness requires an actual heap pointer source, which is line-517 territory (`ptr.const` / `ptr.mut`) and isn't shipped yet. **What slice 3 does *not* do.** No provenance-preserving LLVM-IR metadata. The spec's preferred `!provenance.preserve` markers (and the `noalias` invalidation that would discriminate `expose` from `addr`) depend on lifting raw-pointer-typed slots from LLVM `i64` to LLVM `ptr` end-to-end — a contained refactor in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` plus propagation through every site that allocas/stores/loads a raw-pointer-typed value (parameters, returns, fields, slots, FFI shims). Until that uplift lands, the alias-analysis precision available to LLVM stays the same as it was before slice 3 — the strict-provenance *surface* is in place (compile-time discipline, focused diagnostics for forbidden casts), and the *backend optimization* benefit will land with the type-system uplift. Tracker entry: follow-up for "raw-pointer slots → LLVM `ptr` type" tracked under the broader Phase 7 codegen work; not a new line because the user-visible behaviour ships now. (Phase 5.2.)

- [x] **Opaque foreign types — `extern "C" { type Foo; }` shipped 2026-05-18.** Spec lives at design.md § Opaque Foreign Types (v60 item 24). The form lets a `unsafe extern "ABI" { ... }` block declare a C-side type whose layout is unknown — usable only behind indirection (`ref Foo` / `mut ref Foo` / `*const Foo` / `*mut Foo`) so Kāra never tries to size or move the value. Substrate ships across parser, resolver, typechecker, and codegen; the sub-bullets below break down what landed and the small set of follow-up surfaces still open.

  - [x] **Parser — `type IDENT;` extern items.** `src/parser/items_extern.rs::parse_extern_block_item_opaque_type` accepts the form alongside `fn` items in `unsafe extern "ABI" { ... }` blocks. AST node `ExternItem::OpaqueType(OpaqueTypeDecl)` in `src/ast/items.rs` carries `name`, `attributes`, `doc_comment`, `vis`, `span`. Identifier class enforced (CN-1 type-class), `#[kara_name = "..."]` rebinds a non-conforming foreign name per CN-8. Generic forms `type Foo[T];` parser-rejected with the rationale message ("C does not have generic types — declare a wrapper that carries the parameter"); body forms `type Foo { ... }` parser-rejected with a redirect to `#[repr(C)] struct`. **Test surface**: `tests/parser.rs::test_extern_block_opaque_type_*` covers the bare form, the `pub` / doc-comment / attribute combinator, and the mixed fn-and-opaque-type block.

  - [x] **Resolver — opaque type names register in module type namespace.** `src/resolver.rs` collects opaque-type names alongside other top-level item names; the `SymbolKind::OpaqueForeignType` discriminator is reserved for the cross-block warn-on-duplicate sub-bullet below. Duplicate names within the same block / module currently funnel through the standard duplicate-definition error path. **Test surface**: `tests/resolver.rs::test_extern_block_opaque_type_collected`, `test_extern_block_opaque_type_duplicate_in_same_block_rejected`. Cross-block warn-on-duplicate (the spec's `W_OPAQUE_TYPE_REDECLARED`) is the resolver-side follow-up tracked under "open follow-ups" below.

  - [x] **Typechecker — env registration + by-value rejection.** `src/typechecker/env_build.rs::env_add_opaque_foreign_type` inserts each declared name into `env.opaque_foreign_types: HashSet<String>` (`src/typechecker/env.rs:200`), called during `Item::ExternBlock` traversal. Internal type representation: opaque names flow as `Type::Named { name, args: [] }` and are gated purely by HashSet membership at every check site — a separate `Type::OpaqueExtern` variant was deferred since the HashSet-keyed checks cover every consumption point cleanly. **By-value rejection**: `src/typechecker/lowering.rs::lower_type_expr_inner` threads a `parent_is_ref: bool` flag (true only when descending through `TypeKind::Ref` / `TypeKind::MutRef`) and emits `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_REQUIRES_INDIRECTION]` when an opaque-named path is reached with `parent_is_ref == false`. Covers fn params, fn returns, let bindings, struct fields, enum payloads, tuple elements, generic args (Vec[Foo], Option[Foo], etc.). **Test surface**: `tests/typechecker.rs::test_opaque_type_by_value_*` (7 negative shapes) plus `test_opaque_type_through_ref_accepted` / `test_opaque_type_through_mut_ref_accepted` (positive controls).

  - [x] **Typechecker — focused-diagnostic rejection sites.** Each load-bearing misuse gets its own symbolic code so a programmer hitting the wall lands on the actionable hint without scanning the spec:
    - **`E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_FIELDS`** at `src/typechecker/fields.rs:46-59` rejects field access on a value of opaque-foreign type (e.g. `r.field` where `r: ref Foo`).
    - **`E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_METHODS`** shipped 2026-05-18 at `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call` (intercept placed before the generic Named-receiver lookup). Catches `r.method(args)` where the stripped receiver-name is in `env.opaque_foreign_types`. The diagnostic body steers the user toward the wrapper-type pattern (`distinct type Wrapper = *mut Foo; impl Wrapper { … }`) and the free-function alternative (calling a sibling `unsafe extern "C" { fn … }` that takes `ref Foo` / `mut ref Foo`). Tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::test_opaque_type_method_call_*` (3 tests — ref / mut ref receivers; diagnostic-body assertion for the wrapper-pattern suggestion).
    - **`E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_KNOWN_SIZE`** at `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs:127-130` rejects `size_of[Foo]()` / `align_of[Foo]()`; the layout-query intrinsic suppresses the parallel `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_REQUIRES_INDIRECTION` so the diagnostic shows the right hint instead of mis-directing the user toward `ref Foo`. Tests `test_size_of_opaque_type_rejected` / `test_align_of_opaque_type_rejected`.
    - **`E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_INHERENT_OR_TRAIT_IMPLS`** at `src/typechecker/env_build.rs::env_add_impl` rejects both `impl Foo { … }` (inherent) and `impl Bar for Foo` (trait). Tests `test_inherent_impl_on_opaque_type_rejected` / `test_trait_impl_on_opaque_type_rejected` plus message-body assertions naming the target form.
    - **`E_OFFSET_OF_OPAQUE_TYPE`** at the offset_of intrinsic path (line 511 entry above already enumerates this consumer). Test `test_offset_of_opaque_type_rejected`.

  - [x] **Codegen — opaque types lower naturally as pointees.** `src/codegen/declarations.rs::declare_extern_functions` matches `ExternItem::OpaqueType(_)` with a no-op arm (line 1075-1082): the type name is never used as a value, only as the element of `ref Foo` / `mut ref Foo` / `*const Foo` / `*mut Foo`, all of which lower as pointer-sized handles via existing reference-type machinery. No LLVM `%struct.Foo = type opaque` emission is needed because the upstream by-value rejection guarantees that no SSA value of `Foo` ever exists. The spec's preferred LLVM `opaque struct` representation would only matter if a future codegen pass needed to discriminate opaque-foreign-pointee i64s from regular i64s — until then, the cheaper pass-through covers every behavioural use case.

  - [x] **Effect integration & linker integration — no special handling.** Opaque type declarations contribute no effects (they declare no operations). Sibling `unsafe extern "C" { fn … }` declarations referencing the opaque type via pointer follow the standard FFI effect-declaration rules — the opaque type's mere presence doesn't change effect inference. Linker: opaque-type declarations emit no import symbols (only function bindings do); the type's identity is the C side's.

  - **Open follow-ups** (none load-bearing for v1 because every realistic misuse already lands on a focused diagnostic):
    - **`W_OPAQUE_TYPE_REDECLARED` cross-block warn-on-duplicate.** Today a same-block or cross-block duplicate of an opaque-type name funnels through the standard duplicate-definition *error*. The spec asks for a *warning* on cross-block / cross-file duplicates (the C side has the final word; redeclarations are noisy but not unsound). Implementation requires resolver-level discrimination of `SymbolKind::OpaqueForeignType` (the variant is reserved but unused today) and a warn-vs-error branch in the duplicate-name check.
    - **`#[derive(...)]` rejection diagnostic.** Attribute placement of `#[derive(Debug)]` on a `type Foo;` declaration currently passes the parser (attributes are collected generically) and then silently does nothing — derives never wire up because opaque types reject impls. A focused `E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_DERIVE` would be a small attribute-scan extension at typecheck-time.
    - **`#[non_exhaustive]` rejection diagnostic.** Same shape as the derive case — currently silent, would benefit from a focused diagnostic.
    - **Codegen `%struct.Foo = type opaque` emission.** If a future LLVM-IR-precision pass wants to discriminate opaque-pointee i64s from other i64s (provenance metadata, distinct alias sets, etc.), the no-op declaration site is where the emission would live. Today's behavioural surface is correct without it.
    - **E2E codegen smoke test** exercising `extern "C" { type FILE; fn fopen(...) -> *mut FILE; fn fclose(p: *mut FILE) -> i32; }` round-trip. The unit tests cover every type-system rule; an end-to-end smoke test would pin the cross-phase contract once the e2e harness has an established `libc`-shim pattern. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; lexer/parser change shipped together. Items 3, 18, 22, 24 cluster together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [~] **FFI unions — `union Foo { ... }`.** Spec lives at design.md § FFI Unions (v60 item 22). Sliced into: **Slice 1a–1d** (lex / AST+parser / resolver / typechecker decl-time validation) — shipped 2026-05-18 (this commit); **Slice 2a–2c** (use-site `unsafe { }` rules — read, borrow, literal-shape); **Slice 3a–3b** (impl-Drop rejection, focused non_exhaustive code); **Slice 4** (codegen lowering — Phase 7); **Slice 5** (effect integration — reviewed, no work). Each slice tracked as its own checkbox below. Items 3, 18, 22 cluster together as the FFI-tightening cluster.

  - [x] **Slice 1a — Lexer: `union` keyword.** `src/lexer.rs:1067` adds `"union" => Token::Union`; `src/token.rs:53` reserves the variant. The keyword is unconditional at item position but **weak in field- / method-name position**: `src/parser/exprs.rs::primary` accepts `Token::Union` as a method-name token after `.` and produces the string `"union"`. This preserves the existing `Set.union(...)` stdlib method surface (and any future user-defined union-named fields) without contextual lexing. The original tracker line predicted "no contextual-keyword treatment because every legitimate use is at item position" — the Set.union test case proved the weak-keyword treatment is needed at the parser level.

  - [x] **Slice 1b — AST + Parser: `union NAME { ... }` shape.** `src/ast/items.rs` adds `Item::UnionDef(UnionDef)` (variant), `UnionDef { span, attributes, doc_comment, is_pub, is_private, name, fields, stdlib_origin, deprecation, lint_overrides }`, and `UnionField { span, attributes, doc_comment, is_pub, name, ty }` — narrower than `StructDef` (no `is_shared`, `no_rc`, `invariants`, `is_non_exhaustive`, `generic_params`, `where_clause` — those are nonsensical for FFI unions or rejected at parse). `src/parser/items.rs::parse_union_def` (mirrored after `parse_struct_def`) plus `parse_union_fields` (rejects per-field `mut` annotation). Parse-time rejection diagnostics: `E_EMPTY_UNION` (empty body), `E_UNION_GENERICS_FORBIDDEN` (`union Foo[T]`), `E_UNION_TUPLE_FORBIDDEN` (`union Foo(...)`), `E_UNION_WHERE_FORBIDDEN` (where-clause), `E_UNION_FIELD_MUT_FORBIDDEN` (per-field `mut`). 7 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::union_*`. Sync-to-item recovery list also extended with `Token::Union` in `src/parser.rs::synchronize_to_item`.

  - [x] **Slice 1c — Resolver: type-namespace registration.** `src/resolver.rs` adds `SymbolKind::Union { field_names: Vec<String> }`; `src/resolver/collect.rs::collect_union` mirrors `collect_struct` (attribute placement rejections for `non_exhaustive` / `track_caller` / `profile` plus per-field rejections; same `deprecation` recording shape). `src/resolver/resolve_items.rs::resolve_union_def` resolves field types in the module scope without pushing a generic-params scope (unions are non-generic at v1). 2 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs::union_*`.

  - [x] **Slice 1d — Typechecker: env registration + decl-time validation.** `src/typechecker/env.rs` adds `UnionInfo { fields, is_repr_c, defining_stdlib_origin }` and `TypeEnv.unions: HashMap<String, UnionInfo>`. `src/typechecker/env_build.rs::env_add_union` lowers field types into the env, then emits three decl-time diagnostics: **`E_UNION_REQUIRES_REPR`** — fires when neither `#[repr(C)]` nor `#[repr(C, packed)]` is present (helper `has_repr_c` in `src/typechecker.rs` scans the attribute list for any `repr(...)` with a positional `C` arg, accepting `#[repr(C, packed)]` because `C` appears among the args); **`E_UNION_FIELD_NOT_COPY`** — fires per offending field, using the existing `is_type_copy` predicate from `src/typechecker/derives.rs`, naming both the union and the field so the user lands on the fix site; **`E_UNION_DERIVE_FORBIDDEN`** — fires when any `#[derive(...)]` attribute is present, lists every requested derive in the message, and steers the user toward implementing the trait by hand in an `unsafe { }` block. 6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::union_*` covering both repr-C accepting forms, repr-absent rejection, non-Copy field rejection (with `String` as the field type), derive rejection, and a diagnostic-body assertion that the repr-required message names `#[repr(C)]`.

  - [x] **Slice 2a — `E_UNION_READ_REQUIRES_UNSAFE`.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Hook: `src/typechecker/fields.rs::infer_field_access` — the union branch (which also services field-type lookup for non-error downstream typing) fires the focused diagnostic when `self.unsafe_depth == 0 && !self.assigning_lhs`. `self.unsafe_depth: usize` is incremented around `ExprKind::Unsafe(block)` in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs`; `self.assigning_lhs: bool` is set to `true` only at the topmost `infer_expr(target)` call in `StmtKind::Assign` (`src/typechecker/items.rs`) and reset to `false` on entry into `infer_field_access` so nested reads (`a.b.c = x` where `a.b` reads union `a`'s field `b`) still fire. `Type::Ref(inner)` / `Type::MutRef(inner)` are peeled when `inner` names a union so `r.field` where `r: ref Foo` is treated identically to `u.field` where `u: Foo`. `CompoundAssign` (`u.f += 1`) intentionally does NOT set `assigning_lhs` — the read half of the read-modify-write still trips the gate. `TypeCheckResult.union_info: HashMap<String, UnionInfo>` exposes the registered unions for downstream phases (codegen, future slices). 7 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::union_field_*` covering: read outside unsafe, read inside unsafe, read through `ref` borrow, field assignment passthrough, compound assignment trips, struct-field-read regression, and undefined-union-field diagnostic shape.

  - [x] **Slice 2b — `E_UNION_BORROW_REQUIRES_UNSAFE`.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Surface translation: design.md's tabular `&u.field` / `&mut u.field` examples are Rust-shaped illustrations — Kāra has no `&` / `&mut` prefix borrow operator (design.md § "No implicit coercions": "references are created implicitly at call sites by the parameter-mode rules"). The actual Kāra borrow surface for a union field is therefore **passing `u.field` as a call argument to a `ref T` parameter**, where the `T → ref T` owned-to-shared-borrow coercion at the call site materialises the borrow. Hook: `src/typechecker/exprs.rs::borrow_context_for_param` maps a callee's formal parameter type to `Some("ref")` / `Some("mut ref")` / `None`; `check_call_args_with_substitution_full` saves/sets/restores `self.borrow_context` around each arg's `check_expr` in both the non-generic path and the generic path's pass-1 inference loop (where the `Type::Ref(_)` wrapper is visible on the formal param even before metavar resolution). `src/typechecker/fields.rs::infer_field_access` takes `borrow_context` on entry to the union arm and routes to `E_UNION_BORROW_REQUIRES_UNSAFE` (with the borrow form named in the message) when set, falling back to slice 2a's `E_UNION_READ_REQUIRES_UNSAFE` otherwise. Taking the flag on entry guarantees nested non-borrow union reads inside the same arg still route through 2a, and the save/restore around each arg keeps sibling args independent. The `Type::MutRef(_)` arm of the helper is preserved for symmetry, but it has no reachable Kāra surface today — there is no expression form that produces a `mut ref T` from a place, and the owned-to-shared-ref coercion does not extend to mut-ref (design.md § "owned-to-mut-ref still needs the explicit mut call-site marker"); the diagnostic wording is therefore forward-compatible should a place-to-mut-ref form land later. 5 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::union_field_borrow_*` plus `nested_union_read_inside_borrow_arg_routes_to_read_diag` and `union_field_passed_by_value_outside_unsafe_fires_read_not_borrow`: cover ref-param outside unsafe (2b fires, 2a suppressed), inside unsafe (accepted), generic ref-param via pass-1 wiring, value-param falling back to 2a, and the temporary-through-unsafe routing carve-out.

  - [x] **Slice 2c — `E_UNION_LITERAL_REQUIRES_ONE_FIELD`.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Hook: `src/typechecker/exprs.rs`'s `ExprKind::StructLiteral` arm intercepts when `path.last()` names a key in `self.env.unions` and dispatches to `src/typechecker/fields.rs::infer_union_literal` (with the spread arg threaded through), bypassing `infer_struct_literal` entirely so the union has its own construction rules. The helper fires `E_UNION_LITERAL_REQUIRES_ONE_FIELD` for three shapes: empty body (`Foo {}` — zero fields, message reports `got 0`), multi-field (`Foo { a: x, b: y }` — message reports the actual count), and any literal carrying a spread base (`Foo { ..base }` — separate spread-rejection wording explaining that "copy remaining fields from base" is meaningless when only one field is active). Available field names are listed in the count-rule message so the recovery shape is obvious. The single-field case validates the field name (firing the standard `no field 'X' on union 'Y'` undefined-union-field diagnostic on mismatch, mirroring slice 2a's field-access shape) and typechecks the value against the declared field type via `check_expr` so check-mode coercions (literal suffixes, etc.) flow through normally. Cross-module private-field access reuses `check_cross_module_field_access` from slice 2a's plumbing. Construction itself is **safe** — no `unsafe { ... }` block required, because exactly-one-field commits the bytes to a single named interpretation (design.md § FFI Unions). The previous behaviour (a union literal falling through to `'X' is not a struct`) is replaced. Note from the original tracker still holds: field assignment (`u.field = x`) is unconditionally safe (slice 2a's `assigning_lhs` flag); `ptr.const(u.field)` / `ptr.mut(u.field)` are safe under the strict-provenance place-expression validator. 8 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::union_literal_*` cover: single-field acceptance (both field shapes), empty-body rejection (with count + available-field-list assertions), multi-field rejection, unknown-field rejection, value-type-mismatch routing through `check_expr`, spread rejection, and a struct-literal regression to confirm the dispatch only branches for unions.

  - [x] **Slice 3a — `E_UNION_DROP_FORBIDDEN`.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Hook: `src/typechecker/env_build.rs::env_add_impl` — directly after `trait_name` is extracted (and before method walking), the focused diagnostic fires and the function early-returns when `trait_name.as_deref() == Some("Drop")` *and* `type_name` keys an entry in `self.env.unions`. Trait-name extraction is `path.segments.last().cloned()`, so qualified forms (`prelude::Drop`, `std::ops::Drop`) collapse to the bare `"Drop"` check identically to direct references. Early-return ahead of method registration keeps the bogus impl out of `env.impls` so downstream phases don't trip on a half-registered entry — mirrors the opaque-foreign-type early-return pattern higher up in the same function. Non-`Drop` trait impls on unions are intentionally NOT rejected by this slice: design.md § FFI Unions explicitly points users at hand-written `impl SomeTrait for U` inside `unsafe { }` blocks when equality / hashing / etc. is needed (slice 1d's `E_UNION_DERIVE_FORBIDDEN` already steers users toward that escape hatch when they reach for `#[derive(...)]`). 3 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::union_drop_impl_rejected` / `union_inherent_impl_unaffected_by_drop_slice` / `struct_drop_impl_unaffected_by_union_arm` cover: positive rejection (diagnostic body names both the union *and* the `Drop` trait), inherent impls on unions (`impl FloatBits { fn ... }`) continuing to typecheck, and the struct-Drop regression. Tests declare `trait Drop { fn drop(mut ref self); }` inline because karac does not bake a `Drop` trait into stdlib today — the resolver rejects `impl <unknown> for ...` ahead of the typechecker, and the focused diagnostic only fires once we reach `env_add_impl`. Per-field `Copy` (slice 1d's `E_UNION_FIELD_NOT_COPY`) already guarantees the compiler never emits a destructor for union storage; this slice exists to prevent the foot-gun where a user writes a `Drop` body that the compiler then silently never runs.

  - [x] **Slice 3b — `E_UNION_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_FORBIDDEN` (focused code).** Shipped 2026-05-18. Hook: `src/resolver/collect.rs::collect_union` — the prior `self.reject_non_exhaustive_attr(&u.attributes, "union")` call is replaced with an inline attribute walk that emits a focused diagnostic carrying the new `ResolveErrorKind::UnionNonExhaustiveForbidden` kind and an FFI-specific body ("unions are an FFI boundary shape, not a versioned Kāra-owned aggregate; their field list is determined by the C side and cannot be extended in a backwards-compatible way the way `pub struct` / `pub enum` can"). The new kind variant is added in `src/resolver.rs` and mapped to the verbose CLI code `E_UNION_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_FORBIDDEN` at both `src/cli.rs` sites (the JSON-emitter mapping and the `resolve_error_code` function), matching the `QueryResolutionConflict → "E_QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT"` precedent — the verbose-code convention slice 1d's typechecker diagnostics already follow. The dedicated kind lets downstream consumers distinguish the union case from the generic one without parsing the message body. Field-level `#[non_exhaustive]` on a union field continues to route through the generic `reject_non_exhaustive_attr` helper — the focused code is type-level only, since the field-level post-v1 deferred reasoning is uniform across struct/union/enum. 3 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs::union_non_exhaustive_*`: focused-code positive (kind + message body + absence of double-firing generic kind), pub-union still rejected (the focused code is visibility-independent because the FFI reasoning doesn't care about `pub`), and the field-level regression (generic kind continues to fire for `union { #[non_exhaustive] f: T, ... }`). Tracker note from the original entry still holds: this slice is a diagnostic-quality polish, not a correctness fix — the prior generic-rejection form was already correct *behavior*, just less informative.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — codegen lowering (Phase 7 entry).** Shipped 2026-05-18. LLVM lowering for `#[repr(C)] union Foo { ... }` plus its supporting field-access / literal / layout-rejection plumbing. **Storage type construction** lives in `src/codegen/declarations.rs::declare_unions` (called from `Codegen::compile_program` right after `declare_structs`, so a union field whose type names a user struct resolves correctly when computing primary-field alignment). The algorithm matches the slice spec: each field's ABI size + alignment is computed via `TargetData::get_abi_size` / `get_abi_alignment`; the field with the largest alignment (tie-break: largest size, then earliest source position) becomes the LLVM storage struct's first member; a trailing `[k x i8]` padding tail brings the total size to `max(field_sizes)` when the primary field is smaller. The resulting struct's alignment is derived by LLVM from its first member's alignment, which by construction is `max(field_aligns)` — so `size_of[Foo]` / `align_of[Foo]` work for free through the existing intrinsic dispatch in `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs::compile_layout_query_intrinsic`. **Lookup integration**: `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs::llvm_type_for_name` checks `union_types` between the `struct_types` and `enum_layouts` arms so bindings declared as `let u: Foo` alloca the right number of bytes and parameter typing routes through the storage struct. **Literal codegen** in `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_struct_init` dispatches to a new `compile_union_init` helper when the named type is a registered union (typechecker slice 2c already enforced the exactly-one-field shape); the helper allocas the storage type, untyped-stores the field value at offset 0 (LLVM opaque pointers under v15+ — the store writes the field's natural width, leaving any padding bytes undef, matching Rust's union-literal semantics), then loads the storage back so callers receive an SSA `StructValue` ready for the let-stmt path's alloca-and-store. **Field-access codegen** (`src/codegen/expr_ops.rs`) adds `try_compile_union_field_read` and `try_compile_union_field_store` plus a shared `resolve_union_field_access` helper; the read path injects ahead of the indexed-shared-struct branch in `compile_field_access`, and the store path injects ahead of the indexed-shared-struct branch in `compile_field_store`. Both reach through `var_type_names` to identify the union (extended at the let-stmt's StructValue reverse-lookup in `src/codegen/stmts.rs` so a `let u = Foo { ... }` binding lands in the table), look up the field's LLVM type from `union_field_types`, and load/store at the storage alloca's address. Ref-bound union locals (`ref u: Foo`) are handled by mirroring `get_data_ptr`'s ref-param dereference. **Layout-block rejection** in `src/resolver/collect.rs::validate_layout` adds a third arm alongside the existing struct / enum cases — every `LayoutItem` in a union-targeting layout block emits a focused diagnostic explaining that "unions are an FFI alternation, not a struct shape with a field-set to lay out", with a per-item suggestion to remove the offending group / cold / split_by_variant entry. **Test surface**: 6 E2E codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs::codegen_tests::test_e2e_*union*` — `size_of[FloatBits]() == 4`, `align_of[FloatBits]() == 4`, two-field same-shape literal + cross-field read round-trip, `size_of` / `align_of` on the `epoll_data`-style 4-field union both reporting 8, and the assignment-then-read regression that pins the LHS-store path's persistence; 3 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs::layout_block_on_union_*` — positive rejection (message body assertions), per-item firing on a multi-group block, and a struct-layout regression to confirm the new arm doesn't shadow the well-formed case. The slice spec's "Cross-`extern "C"` use needs no special handling" clause holds via the existing extern-struct codegen path — once a union name resolves through `llvm_type_for_name`, parameter / return / nested-field uses inherit the standard ABI lowering with no per-site union branch needed. The phase-7-codegen tracker carries the upstream half of the contract.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — effect integration (reviewed, no implementation work).** Spec says union field reads contribute no effects to the inferred set — the surrounding `unsafe { }` block carries the language-level safety load. If a hardware effect is in play (volatile MMIO read interpreted as a union field), the effect is already captured by the existing `volatile_read` / `reads(Hardware)` machinery. This sub-bullet exists only to record that effect integration was reviewed and intentionally has no implementation cost. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; depends on `#[repr]` and Pod/Copy bound infrastructure being stable. Lexer change landed together.)

- [x] **Raw pointer construction `ptr.const` / `ptr.mut`.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Spec lives at design.md § Raw Pointer Construction (v60 item 19). Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1a — Lexer/Parser: `const` / `mut` as weak-keyword method names.** `src/parser/exprs.rs` (Pratt-loop `Token::Dot` arm) extends the method-name-position token set from `Token::Identifier | Token::Union` to also accept `Token::Const` and `Token::Mut`, mirroring the slice 1a precedent for `union`'s weak-keyword treatment in `Set.union(...)`. Both forms produce `ExprKind::MethodCall { method: "const" | "mut", ... }` or `ExprKind::FieldAccess { field: "const" | "mut" }` depending on the trailing `(`. 4 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::ptr_*_method_call_parses` / `*_as_field_name_parses` pin both shapes (method call + field access) for both keywords.

  - [x] **Slice 1b — Typechecker: place-form validator + 3 focused diagnostics.** Hook: `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call` — the existing `ptr.*` dispatch arm gains a head check: when `mod_name == "ptr"`, no local shadow, and `method == "const" | "mut"`, the call routes to a new `infer_ptr_construction` helper that bypasses the generic-function dispatch entirely. The helper enforces arity 1 (with a focused wrong-args message), rejects labeled args, and runs two structural checks: (a) `is_place_expression` predicate over `Identifier` / `SelfValue` / `FieldAccess` / `TupleIndex` / `Index` / `Unary(Deref, _)` chains — non-place → `error[E_PTR_CONST_REQUIRES_PLACE]` / `error[E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_PLACE]`; (b) for `.mut` only, `place_is_mut_reachable` walks the place chain and rejects when the root binding's type is `Type::Ref(_)` or a deref step passes through a `*const T` / `Type::Ref(_)` — failure → `error[E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_MUTABLE_PLACE]`. The mutability rule mirrors `place_root_is_mut_borrow`'s "structural type-driven" check used by `mut ref` call-site forwarding (binding-level `let mut` enforcement stays the ownership checker's responsibility — the typechecker has no `let mut` side-channel today). Result type is `Type::Pointer { is_mut: method == "mut", inner: T }`; when the place's type is `Type::Ref(T)` or `Type::MutRef(T)`, the inner is peeled so `let r: ref i32 = ...; ptr.const(r)` produces `*const i32` rather than `*const ref i32` (the *value* at the place is the underlying T; ref / mut-ref are borrow modes, not distinct address-space layers). 12 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::ptr_const_*` / `ptr_mut_*` cover positive cases (local binding, field access, ref-rooted place for `.const`), structural rejections (value expr, function-call expr, ref-rooted place for `.mut`), arity rejections (zero, two), return-type pinning via typed-binding annotation, and the shadow regression (when a local `ptr` exists, the special form does not fire and the call routes to ordinary method-call lookup).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `E_REF_TO_RAW_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN` + raw-to-raw passthrough.** Hook: `src/typechecker.rs::check_cast_pair` adds two new arms after the existing strict-provenance ptr↔int rejections. First arm: `Type::Ref(_) | Type::MutRef(_) → Type::Pointer { .. }` fires the focused diagnostic with a per-mutability suggested-fix (`ptr.mut(place)` when the destination is `*mut T`, `ptr.const(place)` otherwise) and an explanation that references and raw pointers have different rooting/lifetime contracts. Second arm: `Type::Pointer { .. } → Type::Pointer { .. }` returns early, *accepting* raw-to-raw casts including mutability changes (`*const T as *mut T`) and pointee changes (`*const T as *const U`) — the existing fallthrough rejected these via the generic "cannot cast" diagnostic, contradicting the spec's "remain unaffected" clause. 6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::ref_to_const_ptr_cast_rejected` / `ref_to_mut_ptr_cast_rejected` / `mut_ref_to_mut_ptr_cast_rejected` (with fix-suggestion body assertion) cover the rejection paths; `const_ptr_to_mut_ptr_cast_accepted` / `mut_ptr_to_const_ptr_cast_accepted` / `const_ptr_to_const_ptr_pointee_change_accepted` pin the new raw-to-raw acceptance arm.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Stdlib `ptr.null` / `ptr.null_mut` / `ptr.dangling` / `ptr.dangling_mut` / `ptr.is_null` + codegen lowering.** Five new generic function signatures land in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs` immediately after `ptr.container_of_mut`. Each follows the `ptr.*` precedent: registered in `env.functions`, generic in `T`, dispatched by the typechecker's existing `ptr` module arm via `check_call_args_with_substitution_full` (T inferred from arg type for `is_null`, from the expected return type for the zero-arg `null` / `dangling` family). Codegen lowering in `src/codegen/method_call.rs::compile_ptr_module_call` adds matching arms under the i64-pointer ABI: `null` / `null_mut` → `i64.const_int(0)`; `dangling` / `dangling_mut` → `i64.const_int(8)` (alignment 8 is the max alignment of any built-in primitive on a 64-bit target; correct for every T whose alignment ≤ 8, conservative for over-aligned SIMD / `#[repr(align(N))]` types — the actual deref of a dangling pointer is always UB anyway, so the only observable property is non-null + alignment, both of which hold); `is_null` → `build_int_compare(EQ, p_i64, 0)` returning i1 that flows through the standard bool-from-icmp convention. The same dispatch helper also gains arms for `const` / `mut` (the slice-1b construction form): identifier place → `get_data_ptr(name)` + `ptr_to_int`; deref of an already-pointer SSA → the operand's compile result coerced to i64. Field / index / nested-deref places fall through to the synth-identifier path when reachable, with a focused-diagnostic follow-up tracked. 5 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::ptr_null_*` / `ptr_dangling_*` / `ptr_is_null_*` pin the type signatures; 8 codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs::codegen_tests::test_ir_ptr_null_*` / `test_ir_ptr_dangling_*` / `test_ir_ptr_is_null_*` / `test_ir_ptr_const_on_local_compiles` / `test_ir_ptr_mut_on_local_compiles` pin the dispatch shape; `test_e2e_ptr_null_is_null_round_trips_to_true` / `test_e2e_ptr_dangling_is_not_null` pin the end-to-end runtime semantics (null → true, dangling → false). **Surface caveat (codegen turbofish):** `ptr.method[T](args)` parses as `Call(Index(FieldAccess(ptr, method), T), args)` rather than as a `MethodCall` with `turbofish` set — the parser only recognises `[T]` as a postfix on a *call*-position primary, not on a `.method` segment. This means the turbofish form bypasses `compile_method_call` (and hence `compile_ptr_module_call`) at the codegen layer, while the typechecker accepts it because its dispatch path operates on the AST before any of those routing distinctions matter. Tests for codegen rely on type inference from the binding annotation or argument type to pin T; routing the turbofish form through the same lowering is a parser-side follow-up.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Local-binding shadowing (reviewed, no new work).** The shadow rule (`mod_name == "ptr" && self.local_scope.lookup("ptr").is_none()` at `infer_method_call`'s ptr-arm head, mirrored at codegen by `!self.variables.contains_key("ptr")` at `compile_method_call`'s ptr-arm head) already gates BOTH the construction special form (slice 1b) and the generic `ptr.*` dispatch — a local binding named `ptr` causes the call to fall through to ordinary method-call lookup, surfacing a `NoMethodFound` diagnostic when no impl provides the method. `ptr_const_shadowed_by_local_falls_to_method_lookup` (slice 1b's regression) pins this behaviour. The "standard prelude-shadow lint (warn-by-default)" the spec mentions does not exist as a separate lint in karac today; the local-shadows-prelude warning is a future addition to the unified lints surface and is tracked as part of the broader prelude-shadow follow-up rather than this entry.

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally deferred** (not load-bearing for the v1 design contract): (a) field / index / nested-deref place support at codegen (`ptr.const(s.f)`, `ptr.mut(arr[i])`) — currently route through the synth-identifier path when their receiver shapes are recognised; an explicit place-pointer helper would close the gap uniformly. (b) Codegen support for the `ptr.method[T](args)` turbofish form — parser-side rewrite required. (c) `let x = ...; ptr.mut(x)` rejection (binding-level immutability) — needs a typechecker-side `let mut` side-channel or coordination with the ownership checker. (d) Standard prelude-shadow lint as a named lint with `#[allow]` / `#[deny]` plumbing. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker + codegen work.)

- [~] **C-string literals — parser + stdlib `CStr` / `CString` types.** Follow-up to the Phase 5.2 lex-acceptance entry above (line 507). Sliced into: **Slice 1** (parser AST + lowering) — shipped 2026-05-18; **Slice 2** (typechecker `ref CStr` assignment) — shipped 2026-05-18; **Slices 3-5** (stdlib `CStr`, stdlib `CString`, `CStr.from_raw` constructor) — deferred to Phase 8 per the entry's footer (depends on Phase 7.2 stdlib codegen substrate).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Parser: `ExprKind::CStringLit { bytes, source_len }` + parser arm.** Shipped 2026-05-18. AST: `src/ast/exprs.rs` adds the `CStringLit` variant carrying `bytes: Vec<u8>` (without trailing NUL — codegen appends it) and `source_len: usize` (textual body length, lets future `len()` / `as_bytes()` return the pre-NUL byte count without re-walking). Parser: `src/parser/exprs.rs::parse_prefix` adds a `Token::CStringLiteral { bytes, source_len }` arm parallel to the existing `Token::StringLiteral` arm, producing the new ExprKind. Exhaustiveness cascade through 16 sites covering effect inference, ownership use-checking, lints (ffi / logical / must_use / unsafe), lowering, cost summary, formatter (re-emits with `\x..` escapes for non-printable bytes), span visitor, resolver, interpreter, and yield-point walkers in `cli.rs` — all treat CStringLit as a Copy/value leaf identical to StringLit. 3 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::c_string_literal_parses_*` cover ASCII / empty body / hex-escape decoding.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Typechecker: assign `ref CStr` to c-string literals.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Hook: `src/typechecker/exprs.rs::infer_expr_inner` adds an arm for `ExprKind::CStringLit` returning `Type::Ref(Box::new(Type::Named { name: "CStr", args: vec![] }))`. The result is recorded into `TypeCheckResult.expr_types` via the standard `record_expr_type` path, exposing it for downstream phases. The spec's "with `'static` lifetime" phrasing is aspirational — Kāra v1 has no lifetime surface (no `'static` syntactic form, no `Lifetime` carrier on `Type::Ref`), so v1 commits to `ref CStr` without lifetime annotation. The `CStr` *type* itself is not yet registered in `env.structs` / `env.types` — that's Phase 8 stdlib work. The consequence: bare-let bindings (`let s = c"hi";`) typecheck cleanly because the typechecker doesn't lower a TypeExpr-from-source; the literal's surface type flows directly through the inference cache. Explicit `let s: ref CStr = c"hi"` annotations would currently route through `lower_type_expr` and fail at the resolver (no `CStr` in scope) until Phase 8 registers the type. 5 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::c_string_literal_*`: bare-let typecheck (ASCII / empty / non-NUL escapes), multi-literal sibling acceptance, and a direct `expr_types`-lookup regression that pins the assigned `Type::Ref(Type::Named { CStr })` shape so Phase 8's stdlib + codegen wiring has a stable contract to consume.

  - [ ] **Slice 3 — Stdlib `CStr` (Phase 8).** Unsized `[u8]`-shaped type with the trailing-NUL invariant; methods `as_ptr(ref self) -> *const u8`, `len(ref self) -> i64`, `is_empty(ref self) -> bool`, `as_bytes(ref self) -> Slice[u8]`, `to_string_slice(ref self) -> Result[StringSlice, Utf8Error]`, `to_string(ref self) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]`. Needs Phase 7.2 stdlib codegen substrate for global-constant lowering of c-string initializers.

  - [ ] **Slice 4 — Stdlib `CString` (Phase 8).** Owning heap-allocated counterpart; constructed via `String.to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]` and `Slice[u8].to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]`; `as_ptr` / `len` / `is_empty` / `as_bytes` mirror `CStr`.

  - [ ] **Slice 5 — `unsafe`-only constructor `CStr.from_raw(ptr: *const u8) -> ref CStr` (Phase 8).** For runtime-borrowed C strings (walks to terminating NUL at `O(N)` per the spec).

  **Test plan for slices 3-5** (Phase 8): round-trip via FFI through a stub `extern "C" fn strlen(s: *const u8) -> usize`; `to_string_slice` on UTF-8 and non-UTF-8 inputs; `to_cstring` rejection on interior-NUL `String`. (Phase 5.2 parser + typechecker landed; stdlib types remain Phase 8.)

### 5.3: Advanced Diagnostics

- [x] **`--output=jsonl` streaming mode.** Newline-delimited JSON, six event types (`build_start`, `phase_start`, `phase_complete`, `phase_skipped`, `diagnostic`, `build_complete`). Strict superset of `--output=json`. See design.md § AI-First Compiler Interface > 1b. Streaming Phase Events.

- [x] **Error return traces.** Ring buffer (depth 64) at each `?` site. `"error_return_trace"` field in JSON output. Pushed on `Err`/`None` propagation, cleared on `Ok`/`Some`. Truncation flag set when buffer is full.

- [x] **Enhanced per-SCC effect diagnostics.** Tarjan's SCC algorithm detects mutual recursion groups. `"mutual_recursion_groups"` JSON field includes full effect resolution trace — which call site resolved which effect through which callee. See [deferred.md § Per-SCC Effect Diagnostics](deferred.md#per-scc-effect-diagnostics).

- [x] **`karac query` subcommands.** `karac query effects` (inferred + declared effects), `karac query ownership` (parameter modes, RC values).

- [x] **`karac query cost-summary` (static counts).** Per-function and per-module table of every silent runtime cost the compiler emitted: RC ops (Rc/Arc), Arc-provider-wraps, borrow-flag fields, partition-guard sites, auto-clone insertions. Each category aggregates into `totals` and breaks down per-function with a `derivation` array of source locations. v1 is static counts only — runtime attribution (sampling-profiler-driven %wall-clock against a real workload) is post-v1. Closed 2026-05-01 — see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. v1 wires `rc_ops` (per-function from the ownership pass), `arc_provider_wraps` (per-function `with_provider[R]` AST sites), and `borrow_flag_fields` (totals-only over `shared struct` `mut` fields); `partition_guard_sites` and `auto_clone_insertions` ship as `0` until parameterized resources and the REPL `--auto-clone` flag respectively land — schema reserves the keys so post-v1 wiring is purely additive. Codegen-time wiring of additional cost sites (e.g. tighter Arc-provider-wrap accounting once Phase 7 lowering tracks per-call closure-boundary crossings) can refine the static counts; the surface stays the same.

- [x] **`ffi_float_eq` lint.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `src/ffi_lint.rs`: `check_ffi_float_eq(program)` collects all `extern "C"` function names that return `f32`/`f64`, then walks for `BinOp::Eq`/`NotEq` where either operand is a direct call to one of those functions. Wired into `cmd_run` in `cli.rs`. 6 tests in `tests/ffi_lint.rs`. Indirect patterns (via let-binding) not tracked — requires DFA.

- [x] **`undocumented_unsafe` lint.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `check_undocumented_unsafe(program, source)` walks the AST for `ExprKind::Unsafe` nodes; checks the line immediately before the `unsafe` keyword in the raw source text for `// Safety:` (case-insensitive). `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)]` on the enclosing function suppresses; `#[deny(undocumented_unsafe)]` escalates to error. Wired into `cmd_run` in `cli.rs` (text output mode). 8 tests in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs`. Note: `unsafe fn` not yet a syntactic form; lint only covers `unsafe { }` blocks. ~~`unsafe fn` doc-comment `# Safety` section check and one-time doc pass deferred.~~

- [x] **Empty prefix-literal diagnostic — `Vec[]` / `Array[]` / `Set[]` / `Map[]` without binding annotation.** Per `design.md § Collection Literals` (line 1462), an empty prefix-literal has no element type to infer and requires a binding annotation. Today the typechecker accepts empty literals in check mode (the binding's expected type drives recovery — see `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md § Set[T] LLVM codegen` subtask 8 for the `Set[]` case; `Vec[]` / `Array[]` / `Map[]` follow the same pattern), but synthesis-mode use (no enclosing annotation) currently surfaces a generic `Type::Error` rather than a focused message. Slices: (1) Typechecker — at the `infer_expr` arm for `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { items: [] }`, detect synthesis-mode entry (no expected type threaded from `check`) and emit `error[E_EMPTY_PREFIX_LITERAL_NEEDS_ANNOTATION]` naming the literal kind. (2) Diagnostic body — `cannot infer element type from empty 'Vec[]' literal — add a binding annotation: 'let v: Vec[T] = Vec[]'`, with per-kind annotation skeletons (`Vec[T]`, `Array[T, 0]`, `Set[T]`, `Map[K, V]`); the fix-it offers both the annotated-literal form and the corresponding constructor (`Vec.new()` / `Set.new()` / `Map.new()`) per design.md line 1470. (3) Check-mode unchanged — annotated binding, typed call argument, typed struct-field initializer continue to recover via the expected type with no diagnostic. Test coverage: bare `let x = Vec[];` / `Array[]` / `Set[]` / `Map[]` each rejected with the per-kind diagnostic; annotated forms continue to typecheck (regression — `test_set_prefix_literal_empty_with_annotation` already exists for `Set`; add `Vec` / `Array` / `Map` counterparts); typed call-arg and struct-field positions with empty literals accepted. Phase target: 5.3 (typechecker diagnostic emission only; no parser / resolver / AST changes). Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 10.

- [x] **`karac explain --format=json` — structured diagnostics.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Machine-parseable diagnostic output with a finite error-class enum, typed `expected` / `got` fields, and `fixes: [{ description, edits }]` candidate-patch arrays. The deferral condition ("class enum freezes once the diagnostic catalogue has matured ~20+ entries") is comfortably met — 87 unique `E_*` codes across the typechecker, resolver, and lints. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Mint `DiagnosticClass` enum + serialisation.** `src/diagnostic_class.rs` introduces a 22-variant enum covering type-system (TypeMismatch, UndefinedType, WrongNumberOfArgs, NoMethodFound, InvalidCast, InvalidUnaryOp, TraitBoundNotSatisfied, RefutablePattern, CannotInferTypeParam), resolver (UndefinedName, DuplicateDefinition), effects (EffectUndeclared, EffectConflict), ownership (OwnershipMoveAfterUse, OwnershipBorrowConflict, OwnershipUseOfUninitialized), FFI / unsafe / target (TargetIncompatible, UnsafeRequired, FfiViolation), layout queries (LayoutQueryInvalid), lints (LintWarning), and a catch-all `Other` for diagnostics not yet individually classified. `as_str()` produces UPPER_SNAKE wire form. Per the Specification Layers policy, enum values live in the reported-behavior tier — additive evolution within a release, rename / removal is a release-boundary change. 2 unit tests pin every variant's wire form.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Thread `class: Option<DiagnosticClass>` through `TypeError`.** Auto-derived from `kind` via the new `class_for_type_error_kind` helper that lives next to the `TypeErrorKind` enum (so kind additions force a classification decision at the same edit site). 21 kinds mapped to specific classes, 8 left `None` (unclassified → `OTHER` at the JSON-emit site as a backfill opportunity). Three `TypeError` construction helpers updated: `type_error`, `type_error_with_fix_it`, and `emit_lint_with_kind` (lint emissions set `class = Some(LintWarning)` explicitly since the lint-routed class trumps the underlying kind's class). 5 typechecker tests pin canonical kind → class wirings.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Wire `--format=json` flag on `karac explain` + emit JSON envelope.** `Command::Explain` widens from `concept: String` to `{ target: ExplainTarget, format: ExplainFormat }`. New `ExplainTarget` enum covers `Concept(String)` (existing) and `Class(String)` (new — UPPER_SNAKE wire-form lookup against the slice 1 enum). New `ExplainFormat` enum covers `Text` (existing default) and `Json` (new). The CLI parser at `src/cli/args.rs::parse_explain_command` accepts `--concept=NAME` / `--class=NAME` (mutually exclusive) and `--format=text|json`.
