The renderer emits single-line JSON records: `{kind:"diagnostic_class",class,description}` for `--class`; `{kind:"concept",concept,body}` for `--concept`. Hand-rolled JSON with an escape helper keeps the dep surface small and matches the existing emitter style. Per-class prose descriptions (single source of truth for both text and JSON) cover all 22 classes. 8 CLI tests in `tests/cli.rs` pin text + JSON for both targets, single-record-per-call JSON shape, escaping correctness, unknown-class / unknown-format / both-targets rejection diagnostics.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Typed `expected` / `got` fields on TypeMismatch JSON records.** Extends `TypeError` with `expected: Option<String>` and `got: Option<String>` carrying the display form of the types involved. A new `type_error_with_types` helper populates them from `Type` values via `type_display`. The canonical assignment-mismatch site in `check_assignable` migrates to use it; other TypeMismatch sites continue to call `type_error` (typed fields left `None`) — JSON consumers can distinguish "no shape data available" from "expected = some type, got = none". The `--output=json` / `--output=jsonl` envelope gains `class`, `expected`, `got` on every diagnostic record via the `DiagEntry` struct in `src/cli.rs`; the 9 `DiagEntry` construction sites are updated (the 2 typecheck sites populate from the TypeError fields, the 7 non-typecheck sites default to `None` for the new fields and are backfill candidates for future slices). 3 typechecker tests pin the typed-fields wiring; 2 CLI integration tests pin the JSON-output wire shape end-to-end.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — `fixes: [{ description, edits }]` array shape on diagnostic JSON.** Lifts the existing `fix_it: { span, replacement }` legacy field into the spec's preferred shape. Emission is additive: when a `FixIt` is present, both the legacy `fix_it` object and the new `fixes` array appear. Description derives from `lint_name` when available, falling back to "apply suggested edit". v1 ships one edit per fix and one fix per diagnostic; the array shapes are forward-compatible with multi-edit / multi-fix diagnostics when they land. 3 unit tests in a new `diagnostic_json_tests` module exercise the emitter directly with synthetic `DiagEntry` values.

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the JSON contract treats `OTHER` and absent typed fields as valid shapes): (a) classify the 8 `TypeErrorKind` variants currently in `Other` (NonExhaustiveMatch, UnsupportedNumericSuffix, PrivateTypeInPublicSignature, ConflictingImpl, the three NonExhaustiveCrossPackage* variants, MissingNonExhaustive). (b) Thread `class` through `ResolveError` and the per-lint `LintDiagnostic` structs (currently default to `None`). (c) Backfill `type_error_with_types` migration at the ~20 other TypeMismatch emission sites (typed fields stay `None` until each site opts in). (d) Add `code` field to the catalogue lookup so `karac explain --code=E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_MUTABLE_PLACE --format=json` returns the per-code entry alongside the per-class entry. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Structured Diagnostics and Error Class Enum](deferred.md#structured-diagnostics-and-error-class-enum-karac-explain---formatjson).

- [x] **Signature-from-call-site stub diagnostic.** Shipped 2026-05-18. Unresolved-identifier call sites inside `_test.kara` files now carry a `hints[].diff` entry proposing a stub function in the sibling production file with literal-argument inference and a `todo()` body. Activation strictly gated to test files (production-file unresolved calls keep the plain diagnostic). Implementation picked the **resolver-time best-effort** inference layer — local-only literal inference covers the high-frequency TDD opener (`add(2, 3)` → `i64, i64`) without needing to fork the typechecker. The diagnostic shape is identical to what the post-typecheck-refinement layer would emit, so a future deepen-inference slice is a contained extension. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `StubHint` scaffolding + test-file gate.** `src/resolver.rs` introduces `StubHint { callee_name, args, return_type }`, `StubArg { inferred_type: Option<String> }`, and `render_source()` — the compiling skeleton `fn name(arg0: _, arg1: _) -> _ { todo() }`. `ResolveError` grows a `stub_hint: Option<Box<StubHint>>` field; the existing 40+ construction sites default to `None`. `Resolver::with_test_file(bool)` setter plumbs the activation gate; `resolve_modules` in `cli.rs` reads `module.is_test_file` from the walker. The Call-arm in `resolve_block.rs` dispatches bare-identifier unresolved callees inside test files (and outside the existing trait-assoc-fn deferred path) to a new `error_undefined_call_with_stub` helper. 5 resolver tests pin the gate (production no-stub / test-file with-stub), zero-arg render, multi-arg render, and the no-regression case where a test-file call resolves cleanly.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Best-effort literal-argument inference.** `infer_stub_arg_type` walks the call-arg expression: integer literals with a suffix (`1i8`, `200u32`, `999u128`) round-trip the suffix; unsuffixed integers land as `i64` (Kāra's default integer literal type per `typechecker::const_eval::infer_operand_target_ty`). Float literals: suffix → `f32` / `f64`; unsuffixed → `f64`. Bool / char / string / c-string → `bool` / `char` / `String` / `ref CStr`, matching the typechecker's wire forms. Identifiers, struct literals, calls, and other expressions whose types depend on type-checker state stay `_` placeholders — the post-typecheck-refinement layer is where those gain types. 4 additional resolver tests pin suffixed-int / mixed-primitive / identifier-fallback cases plus the multi-arg render-source round-trip.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Lift into `hints[].diff` on the JSON envelope.** `DiagEntry.stub_hint_json: Option<String>` carries the pre-rendered hint JSON; `DiagnosticJson::add` lifts both `suggestion` and `stub_hint_json` into a unified `hints` array. New helpers: `sibling_production_file` (`src/math_test.kara` → `src/math.kara`); `target_append_line` (reads the production file's line count; defensive `1` when the file does not exist yet, so the diff describes file creation under the pure-TDD opener); `render_stub_hint_json` formats `{description, diff{file, line, old, new}}`. Multi-module emitters `resolve_errors_json` / `_jsonl` grow a matching `,"hints":[…]` tail via the shared `stub_hints_tail` helper so the cross-module flow surfaces the diff too. Single-file `Pipeline::resolve` infers `is_test_file` from the source filename (`*_test.kara` heuristic) so `karac check foo_test.kara --output=json` fires the enrichment. Text-mode (`print_resolve_errors_text`) renders the stub as an indented `hint:` block following the existing `did you mean` line for human readers. 2 CLI integration tests pin the test-file-emits-diff and production-file-omits-diff paths end-to-end against `karac check --output=json`.

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the `hints[].diff` contract is stable, the inference depth widens later): (a) **Return-type inference from `assert_eq(call, expected)` / `call == expected` context** — needs parent-context tracking during resolver traversal; stub `return_type` field already exists, the wiring is pure additive. (b) **Identifier-arg inference from explicitly-typed bindings** (`let x: u64 = …; consume(x)` → `consume(x: u64)`) — needs scope lookup of explicit `ty` annotations on bindings; complementary to the literal path. (c) **Post-typecheck refinement layer** for argument expressions whose types depend on type-checker state — the bigger pipeline change called out in deferred.md as an optional second milestone; depends on (a) + (b) landing first to show real-LLM-loop usage justifies the cost. (d) **Single-file text-mode** stub rendering in `print_text_diagnostics` — multi-module text mode already surfaces the hint; single-file text mode currently emits the bare error line (matches the existing pattern for `did you mean` suggestions in that emitter, which are also JSON-only today). Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Signature-from-Call-Site Stub Diagnostic](deferred.md#signature-from-call-site-stub-diagnostic).

- [x] **`karac catalog` — public API surface index.** Shipped 2026-05-18. New subcommand emits one JSONL record per exported item (`fn`, `struct`, `enum`, `trait`, `const`, `type_alias`, `distinct_type`, `effect_resource`, `extern_fn`, plus `impl_method` rows for `pub` methods inside `impl` blocks). Each record carries the item's signature shape — generics with bounds, parameters with classified modes (`own` / `ref` / `mut ref` / `mut slice`) and types, return type, declared effect row (one object per verb with its resources), refinement constraints (`requires` / `ensures` / `where`), and source span (`file` / `line` / `col` / `offset` / `length`). Public surface only — items whose visibility is `Default` or `Private` are skipped. Catalog runs against the parse-only AST (no resolve gate) so external tooling can index a file mid-edit; the `name` field absorbs future multi-module path prefixing without a schema break. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Catalog collector + JSONL renderer (functions).** New `src/catalog.rs` walks `Program.items`, filters to `Visibility::Pub`, and emits one JSON line per `pub fn` (including `impl_method` rows qualified as `TargetType.method`). Param-mode classification reads off the `TypeExpr` head: bare → `own`, `Ref(T)` → `ref`, `MutRef(T)` → `mut ref`, `MutSlice(T)` → `mut slice`. Effects render as `[{verb, resources}]` so consumers query by verb without re-parsing the surface string. `src/formatter.rs` grows four `pub` helpers — `render_type_expr`, `render_effect_list`, `render_expr`, `render_trait_bound` — to share the canonical printer with the catalog without duplicating the type-expr surface. 7 unit tests pin function-record shape (private omitted; sig fields; ref/mut-ref modes; unit return; generic bounds; declared effects; span line/file).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Extend collector to all public item kinds.** `render_struct` / `render_enum` / `render_trait` / `render_const` / `render_type_alias` / `render_distinct` / `render_effect_resource` / `render_union` / `render_extern_function` / `render_opaque_type` cover the remaining catalog surface. Per-kind payloads: struct fields (with `pub` / `mut` flags), enum variants (with `unit` / `tuple` / `struct` shape discriminator), trait methods (full sub-signatures + `has_default` boolean) + assoc types, distinct-type / type-alias `refinement` expressions surfaced as source strings. Generics carry effect-param entries (`{name, effect: true}`) alongside type params with bounds. 7 additional unit tests pin struct, enum, trait, const + type alias, impl-method qualification, effect resource, and distinct-type refinement.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Wire `karac catalog <file>` subcommand.** `Command::Catalog { file }` + `parse_catalog_command` parser (positional file arg only; flags rejected). `cmd_catalog` gates on parse errors only — name-resolution failures (unknown types in a half-written file, undeclared effect resources) leave the per-item AST shape intact, so the catalog still emits, matching the same "AST-walk on parsed program" posture that `karac query attributes` already takes. Top-level help + per-subcommand help text. 8 CLI integration tests pin one-record-per-public-item shape, JSONL terminator + envelope validity, impl-method qualification + private-method omission, empty file → empty output, unknown-flag + missing-file rejection.

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the JSONL schema is stable; the indexing depth widens later): (a) **Multi-module path prefixing** — single-file mode keys items by their bare name today; multi-module mode (post-v1, alongside `module::ProgramTree`) will prepend the module path. The JSON field is already named `name` (not `path`), so the schema absorbs the change without breaking consumers. (b) **`pub` discriminator for `effect resource` declarations** — the AST today has no visibility marker on `EffectResourceDecl`, so the catalog surfaces every declaration. Adding `is_pub` to the AST + filtering on it is mechanical once the broader visibility-on-effect-decls slice lands. (c) **Trait alias / marker trait records** — `TraitAlias` / `MarkerTrait` items currently skip catalog rendering; the per-kind payload is uncontroversial (bounds + supertraits respectively) but no consumer needs them yet. (d) **Project-mode `karac catalog` over the whole crate** — the subcommand takes a single file today; once the project-mode walker matures the cross-file flow (`cli::resolve_modules`-style), `karac catalog` learns to emit the whole-project surface in a single JSONL stream. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Signature Catalog](deferred.md#signature-catalog-karac-catalog).

- [x] **`karac query affected-by` — call-graph reach query.** Shipped 2026-05-18. New `karac query affected-by <target>` subcommand surfaces the call graph as a public JSONL view. Target forms: bare `<file.kara>` (seed = every fn in file), `<file.kara>:<line>` / `<file.kara>:<lo>-<hi>` (seed = fns inside the inclusive range), `<file.kara>:<fn>` / `<file.kara>:Type.method` (seed = single fn). Output is a single JSON record per invocation: `{type:"affected_by", input, callers, callees, tests}`. `--tests-only` flag suppresses callers/callees and emits just the test set; `--direction=callers|callees|all` (default `all`) further trims the envelope. Multi-seed targets union per-seed reach into one envelope. Test-fn discovery follows the same rule the test runner uses (`*_test.kara` filename + `test_*` prefix). Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `CallGraph` plain-data builder + node info.** New `src/call_graph.rs` with `CallGraph { nodes, forward, reverse }` and `NodeInfo { key, file, line, col, offset, length, is_test }`. Built by walking the parsed [`Program`] — every `Item::Function` becomes a node keyed by bare name; `Item::ImplBlock` methods become `TargetType.method`; `Item::TraitDef` methods with default bodies become `Trait.method`. Body walk collects callees through a comprehensive `ExprKind` match: `Call { Identifier(name) }` resolves to `name`; `Call { Path { segments } }` with one or two segments resolves to the joined key; `MethodCall { method }` resolves conservatively to *every* known node ending in `.method` (per design.md affected-by spec — false positives on trait-object dispatch acceptable, false negatives would break test selection). Composite expressions (block/if/match/while/for/loop/closure/par/seq/try/lock/providers/unsafe/optional-chain/range/cast/tuple/struct-lit/repeat-lit/map-lit/binary/unary/pipe/question/interpolated-string) recurse correctly. 12 unit tests pin free-fn nodes, impl-method nodes, direct edges, multi-hop transitive reach (callees + callers), recursion safety (SCC nodes terminate), trait-object method linkage, `Type.assoc()` resolution, test-fn classification gated by file kind, and three target-resolver shapes.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Query API on `CallGraph`.** `transitive_callees(start)` / `transitive_callers(start)` are BFS over `forward` / `reverse` with a `BTreeSet` visited set (SCC-safe — every node visited at most once). `reaching_tests(start)` filters `transitive_callers` by `is_test`. `resolve_target(&TargetSpec)` returns the seed-node key set for the three target shapes (`File` / `FileRange` / `Function`). All traversals return nodes in sorted order so the JSONL output is deterministic. Slice 2 ships together with slice 1's 12 unit tests — the API shape was the design target from the start.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Wire `karac query affected-by <target>` subcommand.** `QueryKind::AffectedBy { target, tests_only, direction }` enum variant + `AffectedByDirection { Callers, Callees, All }` enum. `parse_query_command` learns the `affected-by` kind and routes through a dedicated branch that accepts flags interspersed with the positional target (so `--tests-only foo:bar` and `foo:bar --tests-only` are equivalent). `parse_affected_by_target` splits the target on `:` into `(file_path, TargetSpec)` — numeric forms become `FileRange`, anything else (with `::` → `.` normalization) becomes `Function`. `cmd_query`'s new arm builds the call graph via `crate::call_graph::build` over the parsed AST (no resolve / typecheck required — the graph is a pure AST walk, and surface stays usable on half-written files), then unions per-seed reach sets via `BTreeMap` de-dup before rendering. The `tests_only` and `direction` flags branch into `render_affected_by_envelope_tests_only` / `render_affected_by_envelope` respectively. Top-level help + per-subcommand help text list the kind, its target grammar, and both flags. 7 CLI integration tests pin envelope shape (callers + callees + tests), `--direction=callees` suppresses callers + tests, `--tests-only` filters to test fns, whole-file target unions per-seed reach, file-range target filters by line, `--direction=sideways` rejected, and the subcommand-help advertises `affected-by` + flag names.

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the JSONL contract is stable; precision widens later): (a) **Multi-module project mode** — the v1 surface takes a single file path; the multi-module flow lands alongside `module::ProgramTree` so cross-file affected-by can answer "what tests in `crate/tests/` reach `src/sort.kara:42`?". The JSONL envelope schema absorbs the change unchanged. (b) **Per-monomorphization call graphs** — generic functions today summarize across all instantiations (union of every monomorph's reach). A future `--monomorph=T1,T2,...` flag could parameterize the query by type-arg tuple when a concrete use case emerges. (c) **Method-call precision via typechecker reuse** — `MethodCall` resolution today links to every impl method with a matching name (conservative-by-design). Once the call graph can read `TypeCheckResult.method_callee_types`, the precision tightens for typed call sites while staying conservative for untyped ones (e.g. inside generic fn bodies). (d) **`extern fn` leaf nodes** — `extern` boundaries are currently absent from the graph (leaf nodes per design.md). Surfacing them as terminal nodes with a `kind: "extern"` discriminator is a contained extension; consumers that want to follow effect-propagation through extern-boundary edges can opt in. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § karac query affected-by](deferred.md#karac-query-affected-by--call-graph-reach-query).

### 5.4: Interactive REPL and Jupyter Kernel

First-class interactive surface. **v0 → v1 transition:** the MVP REPL shipped 2026-04-28 on top of the tree-walk interpreter; the v62 lock (2026-05-06) moved the runtime backend to **always-JIT via LLJIT** for v1, with tree-walk retained only as a dev/debug tool. See `design.md § Execution Model and Compilation Targets` and the LLJIT integration entry in `phase-7-codegen.md` for the migration work; the user-facing surface (meta-commands, session model, cross-cell semantics) is unchanged by the backend swap. **Delivery split:** the REPL binary and the browser playground are P0 delivery — both optimize the frictionless first-try path that drives adoption. The Jupyter kernel is P0 priority (committed, designed, scoped) but P1 delivery — timed to ship once the stdlib is stable enough that a first-time notebook user does not hit "function not found" on common types. Semantics (cell scope, ownership across cells, effect display) are now specified in `docs/design.md § Interactive Evaluation Model`.

**P0 delivery — ships in v1.**

- [x] **`karac repl` binary.** MVP shipped 2026-04-28; lifted to `[x]` on 2026-05-19 once the last open follow-up (persistent-let value-snapshot semantics — line 671) closed. Line-based REPL over the tree-walk interpreter with meta-commands `:help`, `:quit` (`/`:q`/`:exit`), `:type <expr>`, `:effects`, `:save <path>`, `:reset`, `:dep`. Items accumulate in `Session.items_source`; statement-style cells run inside a synthetic `fn main()` wrapper. `Session::evaluate_cell_captured` test API surfaces the interpreter's `captured_output` so tests don't need to wrestle with the process's stdout fd. The full closed-out follow-up chain: (a) persistent `let` bindings — source-replay + value-snapshot ([x] line 671); (b) cross-cell item re-declaration shadowing — AST-driven `prune_shadowed_items` ([x] line 673); (c) notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic — cross-cell `consumed by cell N` tail ([x] line 675); (d) `--auto-clone` opt-in mode — consume-site rewrites with `perf[auto-clone-in-repl]` note ([x] line 677); (e) session export `.kara` fidelity — `:save` writes a `karac build`-compatible file with declared effects on main, auto-clone insertions preserved verbatim ([x] line 679). 62 integration tests + 7 unit tests cover the full surface. Stretch items (session-aware Jupyter `%magic`, cross-cell `:provide` / `:end-provide` providers, browser playground) remain tracked as separate P1 entries below — they extend the surface rather than complete the MVP.

- [x] **`karac repl` follow-up: persistent statement-level bindings across cells.** Initial option-(a) source-replay model shipped 2026-05-01; option-(b) value-snapshot semantics shipped 2026-05-19, closing the side-effect caveat the `[~]` marker tracked. `Session.persistent_lets` continues to accumulate verbatim `let` source slices for parse / resolve / typecheck — the source-replay form is what the static phases see, so a later cell's reference to `x` still resolves with a recorded type. **What slice 5 (value-snapshot) added**: the interpreter grew three plain-data fields — `let_value_overrides: HashMap<String, Value>`, `let_snapshot_watch: HashSet<String>`, and `captured_let_values: HashMap<String, Value>` — wired into the `StmtKind::Let { pattern: PatternKind::Binding(name), .. }` arm of `eval_stmt_cf`. When the binding name is in `let_value_overrides`, the RHS is **not** evaluated and the binding is created from the pre-loaded value; when the binding name is in `let_snapshot_watch`, the bound value is recorded into `captured_let_values` for the REPL to drain. **Session bookkeeping**: `Session.let_snapshots: HashMap<String, Value>` accumulates the captured values across cells; `run_with_wrapper_inner` pre-populates `let_value_overrides` from snapshot entries that match every persistent-let binding name (via `parse_let_binding_names`), seeds `let_snapshot_watch` with the union of every top-level `let` binding name in the synthesized source (replayed + current cell), runs the interpreter, then drains `captured_let_values` back into `let_snapshots`. **Stale-entry guard**: `prune_shadowed_lets` clears the snapshot entry for every binding name the new cell is about to re-bind so the override does not splice in a stale typed value when the user changes the RHS shape between cells (`let x = 5;` → `let x = "hello";` correctly stores the String snapshot after the rebind). `:reset` clears both the source-replay buffer **and** the snapshot cache so the two stores stay in lockstep. **Pattern-let fallthrough**: `let (a, b) = …` / `let-else` / `let Some(x) = …` patterns fall through the normal RHS-eval path because keying the override on a single name does not cover them; the source-replay model retains the original semantics for those forms (RHS re-runs each cell, matching the pre-snapshot behavior). **Test surface**: 6 new integration tests in `tests/repl.rs` pin the contract — snapshot store records the bound value after the first cell, a side-effecting RHS (`compute()` with a println) fires exactly once across two cells, three-hop chained snapshots stay consistent without re-firing the seed RHS, re-binding to a different type drops the stale entry so the new type lands in the snapshot, `:reset` clears the snapshot cache alongside the source-replay buffer, and unused bindings still snapshot for future-cell visibility. The full `tests/repl.rs` suite (62 tests, was 56) passes on both `cargo test --test repl` and `cargo test --features llvm --test repl`. Files: `src/interpreter.rs`, `src/interpreter/eval_stmt.rs`, `src/repl.rs`, `tests/repl.rs`.

- [x] **`karac repl` follow-up: cross-cell item re-declaration shadowing.** Closed 2026-05-01 with `prune_shadowed_items` — see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. The implementation took the AST-driven path (re-parse the buffer, identify each item's byte range via `item_span`, splice out names re-declared by the new cell) rather than the originally-suggested generalized `strip_main` brace-balance walk. AST-driven is more robust against attribute/visibility/doc-comment placement and handles every named item kind (`fn` / `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `const` / `extern fn` / `type` alias / `distinct type` / `layout` / `effect resource` / `effect group` / `effect verb`) uniformly; anonymous items (`impl` blocks, `use` / `import`, `independent`, `alias`) have no shadowable name and are never pruned. The previously `#[ignore]`d `redeclaring_item_across_cells_shadows` test is now active.

- [x] **Notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic.** Closed 2026-05-08. When the REPL detects a use-after-move spanning cells, the diagnostic renders a hint naming the consuming cell and suggesting `.clone()` at the call site — not an auto-clone insertion. Strictness identical to `.kara` files; only the diagnostic presentation differs. See `design.md § Interactive Evaluation Model > Ownership Across Cells`.

- [x] **`--auto-clone` opt-in mode.** Closed 2026-05-08. `karac repl --auto-clone` flag enables 2B-style ergonomics: `.clone()` inserted at the consume site when the binding is referenced in a later cell; emits `perf[auto-clone-in-repl]` note. Never silent. Inserted clones appear verbatim in session export.

- [x] **Session export — `.kara` fidelity.** Shipped 2026-05-18. `:save <path>` writes the session as a single `.kara` file that `karac build` accepts and that reproduces the session's observable behavior. Items hoist to file scope (sourced from `Session.items_source`, which is already shadow-pruned so a re-declared item lands as a single up-to-date definition). Statement-style cells (everything `classify_input` does not flag as `PureItems`) are concatenated into the body of a synthetic `fn main()` in submission order, four-space indented, with blank-line separators between cells preserved. The wrapper carries declared effects rendered from `main`'s inferred effect set on the synthesized program — verbs are emitted in design.md order (resource verbs first, then execution verbs) with sorted, deduplicated resources, so the export is byte-deterministic. Auto-clone insertions ride through unchanged because `apply_auto_clone_rewrites` writes them into `cell_history` at insertion time; the exported header announces the bake-in when `--auto-clone` is on so a reader of the file knows to expect them. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Export renderer.** New `Session::render_exported_session` (`src/repl.rs`) walks `cell_history`, classifies each cell via `classify_input`, splits into items section (from `items_source`) + statement-cell body, and renders the canonical wrapper form. Public surface so integration tests can inspect the rendered string without a file write. `fn save` becomes a thin shim that calls `render_exported_session` and routes the write through `std::fs::write`. Header comment names the export source ("Saved Kāra REPL session") and the compile/behavior guarantee ("Re-runs via `karac build` for identical observable behavior"), plus a third line when `--auto-clone` is on noting the bake-in.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Effect annotation rendering.** New `Session::compute_main_effect_decls` (`src/repl.rs`) synthesizes a parse-only program from the items section + main body, runs `effectcheck`, and looks up `main` in `inferred_effects`. The render helper `render_effect_decls` (`src/repl/util.rs`) groups traced effects by verb into a `BTreeMap` keyed by `verb_emit_order` (matches design.md verb listing — reads, writes, sends, receives, allocates, panics, blocks, suspends, user-defined), resources sorted lexicographically, and emits `<verb>(R1, R2)` for resource verbs / bare `<verb>` for execution verbs. Empty effect sets emit the bare `fn main()` form so pure sessions stay minimal. Over-declaration is harmless — the body must respect the declared upper bound, not match it exactly — so the seeded stdlib effect propagation (e.g. `env.set` → `writes(Env)`, `Vec.new` → `allocates(Heap)`) flows through naturally without per-call instrumentation.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Round-trip fidelity tests.** 7 new tests in `tests/repl.rs` covering the spec's two guarantees end-to-end. `export_wraps_statements_in_synthetic_main`: items appear at file scope before `fn main()`, statement cells inside main's body. `export_compiles_with_karac_build`: the exported source parses + resolves + typechecks cleanly (the "compiles with karac build" guarantee). `export_reproduces_observable_behavior`: runs the exported source through the same interpreter pipeline the REPL uses (`parse` → `resolve` → `typecheck` → `lower` → `Interpreter::run` with captured output) and asserts byte-equality against the session's accumulated stdout. `export_declares_effect_set_on_main`: a session calling `env.set` (seeded as `writes(Env)`) emits `writes(Env)` on the exported main, AND the exported file still compiles under that declaration. `export_omits_item_cells_from_main_body`: items appear exactly once (at file scope), never duplicated inside main. `export_no_statement_cells_emits_empty_main`: item-only sessions still produce a valid empty-body `fn main() {}` wrapper that compiles. `export_preserves_auto_clone_insertions_in_main_body`: when `--auto-clone` rewrites `consume(s)` → `consume(s.clone())`, the rewrite rides into the exported main body unchanged AND the header carries the `--auto-clone` bake-in note. The existing `auto_clone_export_preserves_inserted_clones` test (which only verified `cell_history` was rewritten) stays in place as a separate regression pin for the upstream rewrite path.

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the compile + identical-behavior guarantees are met; the wrapper shape widens later): (a) **`Result[(), E]`-shape wrapper** — design.md and the entry spec describe wrapping in `fn main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` so cells can use `?` against fallible calls. The v1 implementation emits plain `fn main()` because (i) there is no builtin `Error` type in Kāra (errors are per-domain like `IoError`, `VarError`), and (ii) the unbound-`E` problem in `Ok(())` inference today means even the canonical `examples/word_count.kara` shape (`Result[(), IoError]` + `Ok(())`) hits a type-inference gap (see `tests/cli.rs` for the canonical `karac check examples/word_count.kara` regression). Once typechecker `Ok` inference and a generic `Error` type land, the wrapper widens to the Result form; cells using `?` today still work in the REPL because the REPL's own wrapper is also plain `fn main()`. (b) **Re-binding across cells across export** — sessions that re-bind the same name across cells (e.g. cell 1: `let x = 1;` then cell 3: `let x = 2;`) export both `let` statements into one `fn main()` body; Kāra rejects same-scope re-declaration with an `'x' is already defined in this scope` error. The REPL's `prune_shadowed_lets` resolves this at submission time, but the cell-history-faithful export walk does not. A future slice could (i) emit each statement cell in its own `{ … }` block scope, (ii) rewrite later re-bindings to a fresh name (`x__1`, `x__2`) per the use-site count, or (iii) collapse the source to the REPL's current shape (persistent_lets + non-let statements). Documented limitation; the workaround is `:reset` between re-binding cells. (c) **Mid-session item shadowing across export** — when cell 3 redefines `fn greet` after cell 2 used the cell-1 version, the export uses the cell-3 version only (`items_source` is shadow-pruned). The exported file's behavior diverges from the session for the cell-2 call site. Acceptable v1 trade — matches the REPL's "current view" semantics; a richer slice could thread per-cell item-version snapshots if a real use case emerges. (d) **`Provider`-scope replay in `:save`** — cross-cell `:provide R = expr` / `:end-provide R` (the next entry in this section) would need to wrap the in-scope cells inside `with_provider[R](expr, || { … })` on export. Attaches naturally to the export renderer once the provider stack lands; the entry already specifies the wrapping form. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P0 § Session Export](deferred.md#session-export--kara-fidelity).

- [x] **Cross-cell providers — `:provide R = expr` / `:end-provide R` meta-commands.** Shipped 2026-05-19 across five slices. The two meta-commands open and close long-lived `with_provider[R]` scopes that span subsequent cells, with `%provide` / `%end-provide` magics forwarding to the same handlers (closes line 689 v1 follow-up (a)). Implementation lives in `src/repl.rs`:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — Scope audit.** Confirmed `with_provider[R](expr, || body)` is an existing builtin registered in `src/prelude.rs:571` and implemented by `Interpreter::match_with_provider`, so per-cell wrapping is pure source synthesis — no new compiler machinery needed. `dispatch_meta` lives at `src/repl.rs:662`; new arms slot in beside `:save` / `:reset` / `:dep`.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Parser + `Session.provider_stack` + LIFO close + panic guard.** New `pub struct ProviderFrame { resource, expr_src, opened_cell }` and `Session.provider_stack: Vec<ProviderFrame>` field. `parse_provide_form` (in `src/repl/util.rs`) splits on the first `=` so expression operators like `==` survive. `add_provider` constructs the expression eagerly via `try_construct_provider` — runs the full parse → resolve → typecheck → ownership → interpreter pipeline against a synthetic program built from items + persistent lets + the expression wrapped in any active outer providers; if any stage errors or `interp.runtime_errors` records a runtime panic, the frame is NOT pushed (design.md "if construction panics, the scope is not opened"). `end_provider` enforces LIFO close — out-of-order surfaces a structured error using the design-spec wording. Construction is non-mutating (no `persistent_lets` / `cell_byte_ranges` side effects).

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Per-cell wrap during run + saved-session export wrap.** `Session.provider_history: Vec<ProviderHistoryEntry>` records every successful open / close at `cells_seen = cell_history.len()`; `build_synthetic_cell` wraps the cell body via the shared `wrap_in_active_providers` helper (innermost-first nesting per the saved-session form) before splicing it into the synthetic main. UAM byte-range mapping still recovers the cell because `cell_byte_ranges` spans the entire wrap, not just the user-typed text. The export-side renderer `render_exported_main_body_with_providers` interleaves cell history with provider history into a linear event timeline, folds it into an `ExportNode` tree (Statement / Block), and emits nested `with_provider[R](expr, || { … })` blocks with one level of indentation per nesting depth — empty scopes collapse to nothing, unbalanced opens close implicitly so the file is always well-formed. Sessions that never opened a scope fall back to the flat `render_main_body` path so existing 679-style export tests stay valid byte-for-byte.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Notebook-aware closed-scope diagnostic.** Two parallel fields on `Session`: `persistent_let_provider_scope: Vec<Vec<String>>` records the active provider stack (resource names, outermost first) at capture time; `pruned_provider_lets: Vec<PrunedProviderLet>` accumulates entries for bindings dropped by `end_provider`'s prune step. `end_provider` snapshots `active_at_close` BEFORE popping, then evicts every `persistent_let` whose capture-scope equals it (lets captured under a strict prefix — i.e. before the closing scope opened — stay because they belong to an outer block). Cleared `let_snapshots` entries for each evicted binding name. New `render_resolve_errors_repl` parallel to `render_ownership_errors_repl` intercepts `undefined name 'X'` resolver errors, looks up X in `pruned_provider_lets`, and appends the design-spec tail: `note: \`X\` was declared inside \`:provide R\` (cell M) and went out of scope when \`:end-provide R\` ran in cell N` plus a remediation hint pointing at the extract-before-`:provide` workflow. `extract_undefined_name` helper in `repl/util.rs` parses the resolver's exact `format!("undefined name '{}'", name)` shape. Re-binding the same name in a later cell clears the prune entry via `capture_new_lets` so unrelated future errors don't carry stale tails; `reset_persistent_lets` clears both fields. Closure-capture-and-escape collapses into the binding-scope rule with no separate handling (design.md § Cross-Cell Providers's "closure capture is the same case" guarantee).

  - [x] **Slice 5 — Tests + `%provide` / `%end-provide` magic forward-wiring + tracker flip.** Refactored `add_provider` / `end_provider` to return `Result<String, String>`; `dispatch_meta` routes Ok to stdout / Err to stderr, `dispatch_magic` wraps Ok in `MagicOutput::ok` / Err in `MagicOutput::error`. Magic surface and REPL meta-command surface now share the same handler and the same `Session.provider_stack` — opening via `:provide` then closing via `%end-provide` is a load-bearing test pin. Closes line 689 v1 follow-up (a). 25 new tests in `tests/repl.rs` cover: parser usage-error paths (5), push/pop semantics (3), LIFO mismatch keeps stack (1), no-active-scope error (1), nested push (1), run-time wrap propagates through `FakeClock.now() = 42` (1), export form (5 — flat fallback, empty-scope collapse, scope wrapping, nested outer-then-inner, header), notebook-aware diagnostic (5 — headline shape, outer-scope binding survives, re-bind clears stale prune, :reset clears pruned bindings, nested close only prunes inner scope), magic forward-wiring (3 — error path, ok path, magic-meta shared stack).

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the meta-command surface, run-time wrap, export form, and diagnostic chain are all in place; refinements widen the surface without changing the contract): (a) **Captured stdout from construction** — `try_construct_provider` lets the interpreter print directly to the process stdout; the magic surface (Jupyter context) would prefer to capture and route into `MagicOutput.text`. Wiring lands alongside the kernel binary (this section's "Jupyter kernel MVP" entry, slice 4); the dispatcher is the contract. (b) **Eager construction with outer-provider wrap testing** — the wrap is in place but exercised only indirectly (the nested-scope test relies on real resource definitions like `Clock` / `RandomSource`). A future test slice could synthesize a user-declared `effect resource` from items_source and exercise the full nested-validation path end-to-end. (c) **Saved-session export of `persistent_lets` declared inside a scope** — slice 3's export emits cells inside the scope, but cells that *introduced* persistent lets while the scope was open are exported by their verbatim cell source (which lives in cell_history) — the let appears inside the right `with_provider` wrap by virtue of timeline placement. The edge case is when a cell mixes a let with statements outside that let's scope; for v1 the verbatim form is exported unchanged. A future slice could rewrite the cell source to keep the let scoped exactly to its own provider wrap if a mixed-mode use case emerges.

- [~] **Browser playground (`play.kara-lang.org` or equivalent) — in-tree artifact shipped 2026-05-19; hosting/DNS deployment remains a v1.x operational task.** Zero-install entry point hosting the interpreter behind a web frontend. **Architecture decision — WASM-in-browser over server-backed.** Zero infrastructure cost (static hosting only — no per-session compute), inherently sandboxed by the browser engine (no rate-limiting / abuse-mitigation surface to build), and matches the "zero-install" framing more honestly than a server that the playground implicitly trusts to be up. The interpreter is the right target — codegen/LLVM are out of scope for a playground. **Pipeline contract**: `karac::run_playground(source: &str) -> PlaygroundResult { stdout, diagnostics, ok }`; diagnostics carry `{ phase, message, line, column, offset, length }` with `phase` ∈ {`parse`, `resolve`, `typecheck`, `effect`, `ownership`, `runtime`}. Posture mirrors `run_program_full` for post-resolve phases (typecheck / effect / ownership errors are collected but the interpreter still runs — the tree-walk interpreter is dynamically typed and does not enforce effects or ownership). Parse and resolve errors are hard stops. **`ok`** is true iff every phase ran cleanly AND no runtime errors fired. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `run_playground` entrypoint + native tests.** Mints `pub fn run_playground` in `src/lib.rs` with the `PlaygroundResult` / `PlaygroundDiagnostic` envelope; 9 native unit tests in `lib::playground_tests` pin the contract independent of any wasm machinery (pure expression, captured println output, parse error early-stop, resolve error early-stop, typecheck-warning execution path, runtime error recorded as diagnostic, span carries line/column/offset, multiple resolve errors in one pass, ok=false when typecheck error even if stdout present).

  - [x] **Slice 2 — wasm32 compile target + `karac-playground` wasm-bindgen wrapper.** Two-part: (a) cfg-gate karac's OS-touching surface so the crate compiles for `wasm32-unknown-unknown` — `ureq` and `rustyline` become `[target.'cfg(not(target_arch = "wasm32"))'.dependencies]`; `cli` / `repl` / `doc` / `scaffold` cfg-gated at lib.rs on `not(target_arch = "wasm32")`; `module` / `walker` / `manifest` stay always-on since `resolver` and `typechecker` consume their data types (the fs entry points inside them are reached only from `cli`/`repl` and thus dead on wasm32); `interpreter/helpers.rs`'s three http functions cfg-split (`eval_http_get` / `eval_http_post` stub to `make_http_error` on wasm32, `wrap_ok_response` and `make_response` go native-only); `src/main.rs` gets an empty `fn main()` for wasm32. (b) New `playground/` workspace member with `crate-type = ["cdylib"]`, depends on `karac` + `wasm-bindgen` + `serde-wasm-bindgen` + `console_error_panic_hook`; exposes `#[wasm_bindgen] pub fn run(source: &str) -> Result<JsValue, JsValue>` that calls `karac::run_playground` and serializes the envelope via `serde_wasm_bindgen`. `wasm-pack build --target web --out-dir web/pkg` produces a 2.0 MB `.wasm` (post-`wasm-opt`) + JS glue. Regression sweep: 1168 integration tests still pass on native after the un-gating of `module` / `walker` / `manifest`.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Static HTML/JS shell (editor + run + output + diagnostics).** Three files under `playground/web/`: `index.html` (top bar with title + Run/Share buttons; two-pane grid for Source editor + Output / Diagnostics), `playground.css` (VSCode-style dark palette; per-phase diagnostic color tokens — parse / resolve = error red, typecheck / effect / ownership = warning amber, runtime = magenta), `playground.js` (ESM module loading the wasm-pack output as `import init, { run } from './pkg/karac_playground.js'`; on Run uses `requestAnimationFrame` to paint "Running…" before the synchronous wasm call; diagnostics rendered as clickable list items that call `editor.setSelectionRange(offset, offset + length)`; status line summarizes the run as "OK." / "N parse, M ownership, …" / a neutral early-exit message; keyboard: Cmd/Ctrl+Enter triggers Run, Tab inserts `\t`). **Editor choice — textarea, not CodeMirror/Monaco.** Zero dependencies, zero build step beyond `wasm-pack`, one network round-trip after the wasm fetch. CodeMirror integration is a v1 follow-up. Smoke-tested via `python3 -m http.server`: all three files + the pkg/ glue + the `.wasm` serve 200 OK; wasm magic header confirmed; the JS glue exports `function run(source)` and `__wbg_init as default` (matches the `import init, { run }` shape in `playground.js`).

  - [x] **Slice 4 — URL share via compressed fragment.** Share button compresses `editor.value` via `CompressionStream("deflate-raw")` (drops the 2-byte zlib header for shorter URLs), base64url-encodes the bytes (`+/` → `-_`, strip `=` padding so the payload survives URL parsers without percent-escaping), writes `history.replaceState(null, "", "#code=...")` (replace, not push, so rapid re-shares don't pollute back-button history), and `navigator.clipboard.writeText(url)` (with a graceful "URL in address bar" fallback when the clipboard API is unavailable on insecure contexts or older browsers). Inverse `hydrateFromUrl` runs *before* wasm init so a shared link lands in the exact state the sender saw; the hash is parsed via `URLSearchParams` (so future params like `#code=…&theme=…` slot in without refactoring); malformed payloads fall back to DEFAULT_SOURCE with the decode error surfaced via the status line (silent reset would lose the sender's intent). Cmd/Ctrl+S triggers Share and suppresses the browser save-page dialog. **Fragment, not query string** — the URL hash never reaches the server; user source stays in the browser, no log-line exposure, no incidental telemetry surface. Encoder chunks the byte stream at 0x8000 bytes per `String.fromCharCode.apply` call to avoid stack-overflow on long inputs. Round-trip verified in Node 25 (same `CompressionStream` / `DecompressionStream` / `btoa` / `atob` API as the browser): a 69-byte sample compresses to an 86-char base64url payload; round-trip equality holds; payload is `/^[A-Za-z0-9_-]+$/`-safe.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — Build script + tracker flip + entrypoint contract polish.** `playground/build.sh` wraps `wasm-pack build --target web --out-dir web/pkg "$@"` so contributors don't need to remember the flags; `chmod +x` and self-locating via `BASH_SOURCE` so it works from any cwd. Native test surface widened from 7 to 9 in `lib::playground_tests`: `run_playground_reports_multiple_resolve_errors_in_one_pass` (pins that the early-return copies every error, not just `errors[0]`); `run_playground_ok_false_when_typecheck_error_even_if_stdout_present` (pins that the `pre_interp_diag_count` bookkeeping flows into `ok` correctly — typecheck errors flip `ok` even when the interpreter completes and captures output).

  **v1 follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (not load-bearing — the architecture, entrypoint contract, wasm build pipeline, web shell, and URL-share form are all in place; refinements widen the surface without changing the contract): (a) **Hosting / DNS deployment** — the in-tree artifact is shippable; pointing `play.kara-lang.org` at a static-hosted `playground/web/` (CloudFront / Cloudflare Pages / Vercel — operational choice) is the remaining task to actually launch. (b) **CodeMirror integration** — the v1 MVP uses a plain `<textarea>` to keep the page dependency-free; swapping in CodeMirror 6 (or Monaco) for syntax highlighting + gutter line numbers + clickable underline decorations on diagnostic spans is a non-load-bearing UX upgrade. (c) **Mobile-responsive CSS** — the two-pane grid is desktop-first; a stacked layout (editor on top, output below) would land via a `@media (max-width: 768px)` block. (d) **Stdlib showcase examples / template gallery** — a dropdown of canonical Kāra programs (binary search, FizzBuzz, the elevator example, etc.) that populate the editor with one click. Examples already live in `examples/*.kara` so the data source is in tree; only the dropdown UI is missing. (e) **Captured stderr** — the interpreter's `write_stderr` path doesn't yet flow into a capture buffer; user-code `eprintln` goes to actual stderr (which on wasm32 routes to the browser's `console.error`). Adding a `captured_stderr: Option<Vec<String>>` field on `Interpreter` (parallel to `captured_output`) plus a `stderr: Vec<String>` field on `PlaygroundResult` would close this. (f) **Embed mode (`?embed=true`)** — a slimmed-down read-only render (editor + Run only, no Share / no diagnostics list) suitable for embedding in docs / book pages via `<iframe>`. (g) **Wasm bundle size** — the 2.0 MB `.wasm` is functional but heavier than ideal for cold-load; future passes could explore `wee_alloc`, panic = "abort" in the playground crate, or selective pruning of interpreter resource backends that the playground can't reach anyway.

**P0 priority, P1 delivery — ships with v1.1 alongside stable stdlib.**

- [x] **Jupyter kernel MVP — shipped 2026-05-19.** Kāra kernel implementing the `jupyter_client` ZMQ protocol: shell/iopub/stdin/control channels, cell execution returning `text/plain` for the last expression, stderr routing for diagnostics with **clickable source spans in JupyterLab** (diagnostic machinery already produces spans; protocol-level wiring exposes them). `interrupt_request` (control channel) flips a `Kernel::interrupt_flag` cooperative-cancel hook (interpreter-side polling is a v1.1.x follow-up — the existing `par {}` token is per-block, not per-process). Tab completion over current-session identifiers + prelude. Packaging: `pip install karac-kernel` with a Python shim that locates the `karac-kernel` binary and registers the kernelspec (precedent disambiguation: `evcxr_jupyter` is actually `cargo install` + self-installing binary, not pip; we went with the pip-shim route for v1.1 launch since the Kāra-native installer rewrite is a documented v1.1.x follow-up — see below). Kernel process itself is Rust; the Python package is only launcher + installer. Lives in a new `kernel/` workspace member (mirrors `playground/`'s layout) so libzmq + HMAC deps don't pollute the karac compiler crate's dep tree or its wasm32 build surface (relevant to the playground's `wasm32-unknown-unknown` target). Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `kernel/` workspace member + `--connection-file` parser + binary skeleton.** New `kernel/` crate with a `karac-kernel` binary depending on `karac` as a library. `connection.rs` defines the typed `ConnectionFile` view (transport / ip / key / signature_scheme + the five port fields — `shell_port`, `iopub_port`, `stdin_port`, `control_port`, `hb_port` — with serde `rename = "hb_port"` matching the spec's snake_case shape), `ConnectionFileError` (`Io` / `Parse` / `UnsupportedSignatureScheme`), and an `endpoint(port)` helper that builds `tcp://<ip>:<port>` or `ipc://<ip>-<port>` strings. The parser rejects any `signature_scheme` other than `"hmac-sha256"` at startup (we sign only with HMAC-SHA-256; silently accepting other schemes would mean accepting messages we cannot verify). `main.rs` wires a minimal argument parser supporting both `--connection-file=<path>` and `--connection-file <path>` forms (Jupyter writes the equals form but matching `jupyter_client`'s tolerance avoids surprises), `--help` / `-h`, and `--version`. The binary loads + validates the connection file and exits cleanly with a "slice 1 — message loop not yet wired" stderr notice so it's usable as a kernelspec-wiring smoke test (slice 6) before the protocol surface lands. 17 native unit tests in `kernel/src/connection.rs::tests` and `kernel/src/main.rs::tests` pin: canonical-file parse, `hb_port` rename, signature-scheme rejection, missing-required-field rejection, malformed-JSON rejection, empty-key permitted (spec allows it to mean "skip signing"), `endpoint` for both `tcp` and `ipc` shapes, real-file round-trip via `std::env::temp_dir`, missing-file → `Io` error, plus the seven CLI-parser variants (separate / equals / missing-arg / missing-value / unexpected-arg / help short+long / version). Clippy + fmt clean across the full workspace.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — HMAC SHA-256 + Jupyter wire-protocol message envelope.** New `kernel/src/wire.rs` module shipping the pure-types / pure-codec layer of the [Jupyter Messaging Protocol](https://jupyter-client.readthedocs.io/en/stable/messaging.html#wire-protocol). `Header { msg_id, username, session, msg_type, version, date }` is `Serialize` / `Deserialize` (field order preserved via `serde_json`'s `preserve_order` feature, already enabled at the workspace root for `std.json`'s sake). `Message { identities, header, parent_header, metadata, content, buffers }` is the round-trip-ready container — identities are the opaque ZMQ-ROUTER routing frames preceding `<IDS|MSG>` and are passthrough; buffers are post-payload raw bytes preserved for the Widget protocol's forward compatibility. `Signer` wraps the connection file's `key`; `sign_parts([h, p, m, c])` hex-encodes `HmacSha256(key, h‖p‖m‖c)` per the spec, and **the verify path matches against the bytes the sender actually sent — never against re-serialized JSON**, since canonicalization differences would otherwise break signatures (test `signature_uses_received_bytes_not_reserialized` pins this contract). Empty signing key is a documented spec escape hatch: outgoing signature is `""`, incoming signatures accepted unconditionally (tests `empty_key_disables_signing`, `empty_key_accepts_any_signature`). Constant-time hex-string comparison via a local `constant_time_eq` helper so equality cost doesn't depend on the byte position of the first mismatch. `DecodeError` variants — `MissingDelimiter`, `TruncatedAfterDelimiter { found }`, `BadSignature`, `InvalidSignatureEncoding`, `InvalidHeader`, `InvalidJson { field }` — give slice 3's message pump precise reject reasons. **Deps**: `hmac 0.12`, `sha2 0.10`, `hex 0.4` — RustCrypto's pure-Rust trio, no native libs. **Slice-3 wiring deferred via `#![allow(dead_code)]` at the module level** with an in-comment "remove when ZMQ sockets land" pointer; clearer than peppering every item with `#[allow]`. **14 new unit tests** in `kernel/src/wire.rs::tests`: signed round-trip; identity + buffer preservation; empty-key disables signing both ways; wrong-key rejection; content-tamper rejection; header-tamper rejection; missing-delimiter / truncated-after-delimiter / invalid-header-JSON / invalid-parent-header-JSON decode errors; the byte-fidelity contract test; an externally-cross-checked HMAC vector (`HMAC-SHA256(key, "abcd") = 2a31ec0e…1121f8`, verified independently against `openssl dgst -sha256 -hmac` and Python's `hmac` module so future RustCrypto upgrades catch any silent algorithm change); and a constant-time-eq smoke test. Full kernel suite: 31 tests passing (17 from slice 1 + 14 new). `cargo fmt --all -- --check` and `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — ZMQ sockets + heartbeat + `kernel_info_request`.** Three new modules in the `kernel/` crate. **`transport.rs`** introduces the `Transport` trait + `Channel` enum (`Shell` / `IoPub` / `Stdin` / `Control` / `Heartbeat`) abstracting the five Jupyter sockets so the message pump is testable without binding real sockets; `TransportError` flattens bind / I/O / timeout / closed into a single error type; `InMemoryTransport` (cfg(test)) backs each channel with `Mutex<VecDeque>` + `Condvar` queues so unit tests drive the kernel through the same trait the real ZMQ binding implements. **`runtime.rs`** ships the `Kernel` struct + `KernelInfo` identity block + the shell/control message pump (`pump_once` does timeout-bounded recv → decode → dispatch; `run()` alternates shell+control so neither starves the other and shutdown is observed within the 250 ms poll budget). `kernel_info_request` handler emits the `kernel_info_reply` (with `protocol_version` / `implementation: "karac"` / `language_info.name: "kara"` / `file_extension: ".kara"` / `pygments_lexer: "rust"`) plus the canonical busy → reply → idle iopub broadcast triad so JupyterLab flips its "ready" indicator. `shutdown_request` handler echoes the `restart` flag and closes the transport so the run loop exits cleanly. Header construction uses a process-wide monotonic counter + a `<session-prefix>-<counter>` `msg_id` so we don't pull in `uuid` for one field. Heartbeat runs on its own thread (REP echo with a 100 ms recv timeout so shutdown is observed promptly; the dedicated thread is load-bearing — sharing the pump's thread would mean a long `execute_request` starves heartbeat liveness checks and the frontend marks the kernel dead). ISO 8601 timestamps for header `date` are computed via a local civil-from-days helper (Howard Hinnant's algorithm) — no `chrono` / `time` dep just for one timestamp. **`zmq_transport.rs`** (cfg-gated on `feature = "real-zmq"`) wraps the `zmq` 0.10 crate: ROUTER / PUB / REP socket bind per the connection file, `Mutex<zmq::Socket>` for `Sync` (sockets are referenced single-threaded in practice; the mutex is just to satisfy the trait's `Sync` bound). **Feature design — `real-zmq` is opt-in**: the default workspace build compiles only the in-memory transport so `cargo test -p karac-kernel` stays self-contained on hosts without libzmq; the Python shim (slice 6) builds with `--features real-zmq`. The `zmq` crate's transitive `zeromq-src` bundles libzmq from source, so opting in still needs no system package. Without the feature, the binary parses the connection file then exits non-zero with an actionable "rebuild with `--features real-zmq`" hint. **16 new unit tests** in `runtime::tests` and `transport::testing::tests`: `kernel_info_request` round-trip (verifies reply shape + parent-header correlation + identity-frame passthrough); busy/idle iopub broadcast pair (with parent-header pointing at the triggering request and no identity frames since PUB sockets don't route); shutdown reply + transport close + restart-flag echo; unhandled msg_type doesn't crash the pump (slice 4 will add `execute_request`); malformed message is logged and skipped; heartbeat thread echoes its payload; ISO 8601 shape pin; civil-date conversion against four known dates (Unix epoch, 2000-01-01, 2024-02-29 leap day, 2026-05-19); `KernelInfo::default` pulls version from `CARGO_PKG_VERSION`; in-memory transport's six self-tests (push/recv round trip, recv timeout, send/drain, close-makes-recv-fail, close-unblocks-pending-recv, channels-isolated). **Module-level `#![allow(dead_code)]`** on `transport.rs` + `runtime.rs` covering items reachable only from cfg-gated code paths (`InMemoryTransport` under cfg(test), `ZmqTransport` under `real-zmq`); cleaner than per-item `#[allow]` annotations. Full kernel suite: 47 tests passing (17 + 14 + 16). Both `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo clippy -p karac-kernel --all-targets --features real-zmq -- -D warnings` clean; fmt clean. End-to-end real-ZMQ verification deferred to a follow-up — would need either a `pyzmq` client or a `cfg(feature = "real-zmq")`-gated integration test binding a loopback DEALER and sending a kernel_info_request through it; `ZmqTransport` is an intentionally thin (~120-line) adapter so the architectural risk lives in the `Transport` trait + pump, both of which the in-memory tests cover end-to-end.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — `execute_request` → `Session` integration.** `Kernel` now owns a `Mutex<karac::repl::Session>` + `AtomicU64` execution counter. `Session` is `Send`-safe because its `Value` graph already uses `Arc<RwLock<...>>` (committed by phase-4 parallel evaluator work). `Kernel::with_repl_options` forwards `ReplOptions` from the kernelspec — slice 6's Python shim will use it to honor `--auto-clone` and future flag-style kernel arguments. **Execute pipeline**: cells whose first non-whitespace character is `%` route through `Session::dispatch_magic`; everything else goes through `Session::evaluate_cell_captured`. The two paths fold into a uniform internal `CellOutcome` enum (`Ok { stdout, stderr, effect_footer }` / `Error { stdout, stderr, ename, evalue, traceback }`) so the broadcast logic doesn't branch on cell flavor. **IOPub broadcast order** matches the Jupyter spec: `status: busy` → `execute_input { code, execution_count }` (skipped when `silent`) → `stream(stdout)` for captured `println` output (skipped when empty) → `stream(stderr)` for diagnostic strings + auto-clone `perf[…]` notes (skipped when empty) → `stream(stdout)` for the effect footer (skipped when empty; kept on stdout — not stderr — so the footer appears under the cell rather than as a warning) → `error { ename, evalue, traceback }` on diagnostic failure (mirrors the shell `execute_reply` so other frontends connected to the same kernel see the failure without polling shell) → `status: idle`. Effect footer emission relies on the field populated by line 721 slice 3's `Session::compute_cell_effect_footer`; for `println` cells that footer reflects the inferred effect set on `main` (typically `writes(Console)`-equivalent), suppressed when empty. **Shell `execute_reply`**: `status: ok` with `execution_count` + empty `payload` / `user_expressions` on success; `status: error` with `ename` / `evalue` / `traceback` on failure. The shell reply preserves the request's identity frames so a ROUTER socket routes it back to the originating DEALER. **Silent execute semantics** match Jupyter: `silent: true` skips the iopub `execute_input` and the cell-output broadcasts (only the busy/idle status pair fires), doesn't bump `execution_count`, and never appears in the cell history. **`ename` taxonomy**: `"CompileError"` for diagnostic failures from `evaluate_cell_captured` (parse / resolve / typecheck / effect / ownership errors all collapse into this single name; `traceback` carries the per-error breakdown), `"MagicError"` for `dispatch_magic` errors. **8 new unit tests** in `runtime::tests`: simple `println("hello kara")` round-trip pinning shell reply + iopub broadcast sequence + identity-frame preservation; execution-count increment across three cells; silent execute pins counter-stays-frozen + only-status-broadcast; compile-error path pins `CompileError` ename + iopub error broadcast mirroring shell + stream-is-stderr-not-stdout; successful-cell stream-only-stdout pin (effect footer never lands on stderr); magic-cell error path through `dispatch_magic` pins `MagicError` ename; session-state persistence across cells (`let x = 7;` in cell 1, `println(x);` in cell 2 sees x=7); empty-code-is-clean-noop. Existing `unhandled_msg_type_does_not_crash` test re-targeted from `execute_request` (now handled) to `complete_request` (slice 5). `broadcast_status` consolidated into a new `broadcast_iopub` helper so all iopub sends route through one error-logging path. Full kernel suite: 55 tests passing (47 from earlier slices + 8 new). `cargo fmt --all -- --check` and `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean both with and without `--features real-zmq`.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — `complete_request` + `is_complete_request` + `interrupt_request`.** Three new handlers in `runtime.rs` close out the MVP request surface. **`complete_request`** returns `(matches, cursor_start, cursor_end)` per the Jupyter spec; candidates pull from three sources unified into one prefix-filtered list: a hardcoded `PRELUDE_IDENTIFIERS` array (output / stdio: `println` / `print` / `eprintln` / `eprint`; values: `true` / `false` / `Some` / `None` / `Ok` / `Err`; common types: `Vec` / `Map` / `Set` / `String` / `i32` / `i64` / `u32` / `u64` / `f32` / `f64` / `bool` / `char`; the eight effect verbs from the design spec; stdlib aggregators `sum` / `len` / `min` / `max` / `first`), top-level names extracted from `Session::items_source()` via a line-prefix scan for `fn` / `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `const` / `let` / `let mut` / `type` / `shared struct` / `shared enum` / `distinct`, and `Session::persistent_lets()` names. **Rationale for the regex-style scan rather than a real parse**: tab completion is best-effort, never load-bearing — running a full parse + resolve pass on every keystroke would add latency without changing UX outcomes (a missed candidate hurts the user mildly; the next character usually disambiguates). `identifier_prefix_at(code, cursor_pos)` walks back from the cursor to find the token's start (ASCII alphanumeric + `_`), returns `(cursor_start, prefix)`. **`is_complete_request`** uses a delimiter-balance heuristic with full literal awareness: string + char literals (with `\\` escape handling), line comments (`//` to newline), block comments (`/* ... */` non-nesting per Kāra's lexer), and the four bracket kinds (`{` `[` `(` open; `}` `]` `)` close). Returns `complete` for balanced cells, `incomplete` (with 4-space-per-depth indent) for unclosed opens, `invalid` for extra closes (cell will hard-error at parse time; submit immediately so the diagnostic surfaces), `unknown` for unclosed strings/chars (frontend's own heuristic handles multi-line literals better than ours), `complete` for empty cells (matches Jupyter's "blank Enter" UX). **`interrupt_request`** flips a new `AtomicBool` `Kernel::interrupt_flag`; exposed via `Kernel::interrupt_requested()` for tests and future polling. `execute_request` clears the flag at the start of every new cell so a stale interrupt doesn't bleed into the next execution. **Interpreter-side cooperative polling is a slice follow-up** — the existing `par {}` cancellation token in `src/interpreter/exec.rs` is per-block, not per-process, so wiring it through to a kernel-level interrupt requires a separate pass through the interpreter's main eval loops. The kernel-side wire is in place; the interpreter-side hook lands when needed. **13 new tests** in `runtime::tests`: `complete_request` returns prelude identifiers for `"prin"`; includes session-declared `fn my_helper` after an `execute_request` lands; cursor-in-middle-of-token computes `cursor_start` correctly for `"let x = prin"`. `is_complete_request` classifies balanced cells as `complete`, unclosed `fn` as `incomplete` (with 4-space indent), extra `}` as `invalid`, empty cells as `complete`, unclosed strings as `unknown`. `interrupt_request` sets the flag + replies `ok`; `execute_request` clears a stale flag. Unit tests for `extract_top_level_names` (covers fn/struct/enum/const/let/let-mut/type/shared-struct), `identifier_prefix_at` (five variants including cursor-past-end clamp), and `classify_completeness` (eight cell shapes including braces inside string + block comment). Re-targeted the existing `unhandled_msg_type_does_not_crash` test from `complete_request` (now handled) to `comm_open` (forward-compat noise the kernel still ignores). Full kernel suite: 68 tests passing (55 from earlier slices + 13 new). `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean both with and without `--features real-zmq`.

  - [x] **Slice 6 — Python shim (`karac-kernel` PyPI launcher + kernelspec installer).** New `kernel/python/` directory shipping a stdlib-only Python distribution (zero runtime deps — `jupyter_client` would pull in `pyzmq` + `tornado` just to read its data-dir path, so we shell out to `jupyter --paths --json` instead). **`pyproject.toml`** declares `karac-kernel` 0.1.0, requires Python ≥3.9, registers `karac-kernel-install` as a console script + bundles `kernel.json` as package data. **`karac_kernel/launcher.py`** — `find_binary()` does first-hit-wins lookup against `$KARAC_KERNEL_BIN` env override → `shutil.which("karac-kernel")` (PATH) → `$KARAC_KERNEL_FALLBACK_PATHS` (colon-separated directories for advanced setups). `exec_kernel(argv)` uses `os.execvp` on POSIX so signals + exit codes flow through naturally; falls back to `subprocess.run` + propagated returncode on Windows where `execvp` doesn't propagate Ctrl+C cleanly. Missing-binary path exits 127 (POSIX "command not found") with an actionable install hint pointing at `cargo install karac-kernel --features real-zmq`. **`karac_kernel/install.py`** — `kernel_json_payload()` builds the kernelspec body with `argv: [sys.executable, "-m", "karac_kernel", "--connection-file={connection_file}"]` (uses `sys.executable` so a venv-installed `karac-kernel` runs under the same Python it was installed into — avoids the system-Python-can't-import-karac_kernel surprise), `interrupt_mode: "message"` (load-bearing — slice 5's `handle_interrupt_request` only fires when Jupyter sends a control-channel message rather than SIGINT'ing), plus language metadata mirroring the Rust kernel's `kernel_info_reply`. `jupyter_data_dir(scope)` delegates to `jupyter --paths --json` when the CLI is on PATH (authoritative — honors venv / conda / custom-prefix installs); falls back to hardcoded platform defaults matching `jupyter_core.paths.jupyter_data_dir()` verbatim (`~/Library/Jupyter` on macOS, `$XDG_DATA_HOME/jupyter` on Linux, `%APPDATA%/jupyter` on Windows; `/usr/local/share/jupyter` for system scope). CLI accepts `--user` (default), `--system`, `--prefix PATH` (mutually exclusive), plus `--dry-run` for previewing without writing. Idempotent — re-running overwrites. **`karac_kernel/__main__.py`** dispatches between `python -m karac_kernel install …` (installer) and `python -m karac_kernel --connection-file=…` (launcher, the form Jupyter invokes); the dispatcher inspects argv for the `install` subcommand keyword. **`kernel.json`** template lives alongside the package as well (bundled via `package-data` for future tooling that wants the file directly without invoking the installer). **21 new tests** in `kernel/python/tests/` using stdlib `unittest` (no pytest dep so the test surface stays self-contained on any Python ≥3.9): `test_launcher.py` pins all four lookup paths (env override wins over PATH, missing-env-file raises, PATH lookup, fallback dirs scanned last, helpful error message, `main` returns 127 on not-found); `test_install.py` pins the payload schema (required keys, `argv[0] == sys.executable`, `{connection_file}` template present, `interrupt_mode == "message"`, language metadata matches Rust kernel), prefix install + idempotent re-run, `--dry-run` doesn't write, mutually-exclusive flag rejection, fallback-dir shape per platform. End-to-end smoke: `python -m karac_kernel install --prefix=$TMP` writes a valid kernel.json; `KARAC_KERNEL_BIN=$PWD/target/debug/karac-kernel python -m karac_kernel --connection-file=/tmp/nope.json` correctly forwards to the binary which surfaces its own "could not read connection file" error (proves the exec chain). **README** in `kernel/python/` documents the install flow + the v1.1.x follow-up note. Total kernel surface: 68 Rust tests + 21 Python tests, all passing; clippy + fmt clean across the Rust workspace on both default features and `--features real-zmq`.

  **v1.1.x follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (kernel MVP is complete — the wire protocol surface is closed; refinements widen UX without changing the contract):

  (a) **Kāra-native installer rewrite** — replace `kernel/python/` with `install.kara` shipped alongside the Rust binary, once Kāra's stable stdlib lands `std.fs` + `std.env` + `std.process`. The kernel binary itself stays Rust (ZMQ + HMAC + threading is Rust's wheelhouse; rewriting that in hand-rolled FFI would be a robustness regression for marginal architectural purity); only the *installer* moves. Either embed an `install.kara` source string in the Rust binary that runs through the interpreter on `karac-kernel install`, or ship `install-kernel.kara` next to the binary and run via `karac install-kernel.kara`. Small but real eat-your-own-dogfood milestone — first non-trivial Kāra program shipped with the toolchain.

  (b) **Interpreter-side cooperative interrupt polling** — slice 5 wired the kernel-side `Kernel::interrupt_flag` and `execute_request` clears it at cell start, but the interpreter's main eval loops don't yet poll the flag. The existing `par {}` cancellation token in `src/interpreter/exec.rs` is per-block, not per-process, so wiring it through requires a separate pass — likely a thread-local interrupt-token check at loop / call boundaries. Until that lands, `interrupt_request` is observable via `Kernel::interrupt_requested()` for tests but doesn't actually halt a runaway cell.

  (c) **Captured stdout from `:provide` construction** (from line 689 v1 follow-up, originally tracked at this entry) — `try_construct_provider` lets the interpreter print directly to the process stdout; the magic surface would prefer to capture and route into `MagicOutput.text`. The execute_request handler is in place (slice 4) and can be extended once the interpreter exposes a capture hook around provider construction.

  (d) **End-to-end real-ZMQ integration test** — slice 3's `ZmqTransport` is a thin ~120-line adapter covered indirectly through the in-memory transport tests, but no test exercises the actual libzmq path. A `cfg(feature = "real-zmq")` integration test binding a loopback DEALER + sending a kernel_info_request through it would close the gap; deferred since the architectural risk is in the trait + pump (both covered) rather than the adapter.

  (e) **Rich display widening** — `kernel_info_reply` already declares `"text/x-kara"` mimetype + `"rust"` pygments lexer for syntax highlighting in the cell editor. Slice 7+ (line 735, "Rich display for structs and collections") is the v1.1+ track that would emit `text/html` for `Vec[Struct]` and friends — see the post-MVP kernel stretch goals below.

  (f) **`%explain --format=json`** (from line 731 v1 follow-up) — kernel currently routes the magic text through `display_data`; a future widening accepts `%explain <name> --format=json` for IDE consumers that want the structured envelope. `render_to_string` helper already supports both formats; only the magic-side argument grammar needs to grow.

- [x] **Jupyter `%magic` surface — shipped 2026-05-19.** Dispatcher + five magics (`%effects`, `%ownership`, `%explain`, `%set auto-clone`, `%provide`/`%end-provide`) all in place; `%rc` is explicitly carved out as a v1.1.x follow-up (gated on RC fallback's introspection surface settling — see follow-up (e) below). Forward-wired into the kernel via line 719 slice 4's `execute_request` handler. Surface lives in `Session::dispatch_magic(line: &str) -> MagicOutput` (`src/repl.rs`); the Jupyter kernel (this section's "Jupyter kernel MVP" entry, `[x]` shipped 2026-05-19) routes every cell whose first token begins with `%` through this entry point and maps `MagicOutput { text, ok }` onto the protocol's `display_data` / `error` channels. The dispatcher is exercised by the test suite so the surface is observable without a kernel binary. **Shipped magics**: (a) `%effects` walks `items_source` through `effectcheck` and renders one row per inferred function with non-empty effects via the same `render_effect_decls` helper that drives `:save`'s declared-effects on `fn main()` — the kernel reuses the rendered string for its `display_data` reply. (b) `%ownership` builds the session's synthetic `fn main()` view (items + persistent_lets), runs the full parse → resolve → typecheck → ownershipcheck pipeline, filters `OwnershipCheckResult.representations` to `main.*` rows, and overlays a baseline `owned (stack)` label for every persistent-let binding (covering the common `let x = 5;` case that the representations map does not record). RC promotions from the ownership pass win over the baseline. (c) `%explain <name>` wraps the existing `karac explain` subcommand by way of a new `pub fn render_to_string(target, format) -> Result<String, String>` in `src/cli/explain.rs` (the existing `pub fn render` was `process::exit`-shaped and not kernel-friendly). The magic tries concept lookup first, then class lookup, so both `closures` (concept) and `TYPE_MISMATCH` (class) resolve through one entry point. (d) `%set auto-clone on|off` toggles `Session.auto_clone` — the same flag the constructor reads from `ReplOptions.auto_clone` — accepting `on`/`true`/`1` and `off`/`false`/`0`, rejecting other values with a focused error message. **Per-cell effect footer**: `EvaluatedCell` grew an `effect_footer: String` field populated by `Session::compute_cell_effect_footer` after every successful statement-style run. The footer string is built via the same `render_effect_decls` helper so the format matches `%effects` and `:save`. Pure cells (no tracked effects) emit `""` so the kernel can suppress the annotation rather than render an empty footer. **Shipped via forward-wiring**: (e) `%provide R = expr` / `%end-provide R` forward to the same `add_provider` / `end_provider` handlers the `:provide` / `:end-provide` REPL meta-commands use (closed once tracker line 681 landed). Magic surface and meta-command surface share the same `Session.provider_stack`; both return `Result<String, String>` which the magic dispatcher wraps in `MagicOutput::ok` / `MagicOutput::error`. **Deferred forms**: (f) `%rc` is deferred to post-MVP per the spec — RC fallback's introspection surface is still settling — and returns a structured deferral reply. **Test surface**: 15 new integration tests in `tests/repl.rs` covering each magic (success path, empty-state hint, error path, no-argument usage hint), the `MagicOutput` construction helpers, the `%provide` / `%end-provide` deferral pointers, and the `%rc` post-MVP deferral. 3 additional tests pin the per-cell `effect_footer` field — populated for a `writes(Env)` cell, empty for a pure cell, empty for an item-only cell. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `Session::dispatch_magic` dispatcher + `MagicOutput` envelope.** New `pub struct MagicOutput { text: String, ok: bool }` with `ok()` / `error()` constructors. `dispatch_magic` strips the leading `%`, splits on first whitespace, and routes to per-magic handlers via an exhaustive `match`. Unknown magics return a structured error listing the supported set; empty argument lists surface a usage hint.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `%effects`, `%ownership`, `%explain`, `%set auto-clone` handlers.** `magic_effects` reuses the `:effects` meta-command's accumulation loop but returns the rendered string instead of printing. `magic_ownership` runs the synthetic-source pipeline and pairs `OwnershipCheckResult.representations` with a `persistent_lets`-derived baseline. `magic_explain` calls the new `cli::explain::render_to_string` with both `Concept` and `Class` targets. `magic_set` accepts an extensible `<key> <value>` grammar (only `auto-clone` is supported in v1).

  - [x] **Slice 3 — `%provide` / `%end-provide` / `%rc` deferral pointers + per-cell `effect_footer`.** The two `%provide` forms emit structured `not yet wired` errors pointing to tracker line 681; `%rc` returns its post-MVP deferral reason. `EvaluatedCell.effect_footer` populates from `compute_cell_effect_footer` on the successful statement-cell path; falls back to `""` on parse failure or empty-effect main so the kernel can suppress the line.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — Test surface + tracker flip.** 15 + 3 new tests in `tests/repl.rs` pin every magic plus the footer field. Full 80-test repl suite passes on both `cargo test --test repl` and `cargo test --features llvm --test repl`. Tracker flipped to `[~]` with the four-handler / two-deferred breakdown plus v1 follow-ups below.

  **v1.1.x follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (MVP surface is closed — refinements widen UX without changing the dispatcher contract): (a) ~~**`%provide` / `%end-provide` wiring**~~ — shipped 2026-05-19 alongside line 681; the magic handlers forward to `add_provider` / `end_provider` and the magic / meta surfaces share `Session.provider_stack`. (b) **`%explain --format=json` flag-style argument parsing** — the kernel currently routes the text body through `display_data`; a future widening would accept `%explain <name> --format=json` for IDE consumers that want the structured envelope.
