The `render_to_string` helper already supports both formats — only the magic-side argument grammar needs to grow. (c) **`%ownership` enrichment with closure-capture rows** — the `representations` map covers parameters and RC promotions; future enrichment can surface `closure_captures` and `closure_capture_paths` entries when the session's persistent-let bindings include closure-bearing values. (d) ~~**Kernel-side wiring**~~ — shipped 2026-05-19 in the "Jupyter kernel MVP" entry slice 4; `execute_request` routes `%`-prefixed cells through `dispatch_magic` and maps `MagicOutput { ok: true }` onto `display_data` / `stream(stdout)` (with `effect_footer` appended as a trailing stream line) and `ok: false` onto a shell `execute_reply { status: "error", ename: "MagicError" }` + iopub `error` broadcast. (e) **`%rc` magic** — explicitly carved out of the MVP surface; reopens once RC fallback's introspection surface (`rc_values` / `arc_values` rendering posture) settles. Reason for the deferral: RC promotion decisions made by the ownership pass are observable through the existing `%ownership` magic's representations table, so users aren't fully blind in the interim — `%rc` would widen the UX to a dedicated audit view with trigger reasoning, which is genuinely useful but not a v1 gating contract.

**Stretch (P1+) — post-MVP kernel.**

- [x] **Rich display for structs and collections — shipped 2026-05-19.** Spec sentence honoured for the first two bullets: `text/html` table rendering for `Vec[Struct]` (one row per element, one column per field) and `text/plain` pretty-printing for nested data both ship via the `%show <expr>` magic + the kernel's `display_data` IOPub broadcast. `image/png` for plotting is carved out to v1.1.x — gated on stdlib plotting primitive(s) landing first. **Reflection model**: the renderer walks the live runtime `Value` at display time rather than consulting the typechecker's type registry — same observable surface (field names, nesting depth) with weaker coupling, and works on the tree-walk interpreter today without further pipeline integration. **Surface**: new `src/repl/display.rs` exposes `pub struct DisplayBundle { pub mimes: Vec<(String, String)> }` carrying ordered mime/body pairs (`text/plain` is always the first entry) plus `pub fn render_display(value: &Value) -> DisplayBundle`. Always emits `text/plain` (multi-line indent for `Array` / `Map` / `Struct` / `Tuple` that contains further structure; atoms and bare-collections-of-atoms stay inline). Emits `text/html` **only** for arrays of homogeneously-shaped structs — every element must be `Value::Struct` with the same `name` and the same field set; mixed-shape arrays / single structs / atom arrays bail to text-plain only. Columns are sorted alphabetically for stable output (HashMap iteration order is not). HTML escapes `& < > " '` in cells so untrusted string fields don't break the table. `Slice[Struct]` also emits `text/html` (same shape requirements; only the start/len window is rendered). **`%show <expr>` magic**: extends `Session::dispatch_magic` with a sixth verb. Evaluates the expression against the current session state via a private `eval_expr_for_display(&self, expr)` that synthesizes `fn main() { <persistent_lets>; let __k_show = <expr>; }`, runs the full pipeline (parse → resolve → typecheck → ownership → lower → interpret) with persistent-let value snapshots replayed through `let_value_overrides`, reads back the captured `__k_show` Value, and returns it. Side-effect-free against session state — `cell_history`, `persistent_lets`, and `let_snapshots` are read-only on this path; the `__k_show` binding never leaks out. **`MagicOutput.rich` field**: new `Option<DisplayBundle>` carrying the mime bundle alongside the existing `text` (plain-text mirror for non-rich consumers) and `ok` fields; new `ok_rich(text, bundle)` constructor. The existing `ok(text)` / `error(text)` constructors leave `rich = None` so the existing five magics (`%effects`, `%ownership`, `%explain`, `%set`, `%provide`/`%end-provide`) keep their stream(stdout) routing. **Kernel wiring**: `CellOutcome::Ok` grew a `display_bundle: Option<DisplayBundle>` field; `run_cell`'s magic branch stashes `out.rich` there and zeroes `stdout` (so the bundle's text/plain doesn't render twice); `emit_cell_output` broadcasts `display_data` on IOPub with the full mime map (data + empty metadata + empty transient) when the bundle is present, otherwise falls through to the existing stream(stdout) path. **Test surface**: 20 unit tests in `src/repl/display.rs::tests` cover atoms, empty arrays, Vec[Struct] HTML emission + sorted columns + escaping, mixed-shape arrays (no HTML), single struct (no HTML), nested struct multi-line, Map/Tuple inline + multi-line branches, Slice[Struct], and DisplayBundle accessor surface; 9 integration tests in `tests/repl.rs` cover the `%show` magic (atom → text-plain only, Vec[Struct] → text-html table, string value, undefined name, empty argument usage hint, session-state non-mutation, unknown-magic help advertises %show, session items visible, nested struct multi-line); 3 kernel tests in `kernel/src/runtime.rs::tests` pin the IOPub broadcast (`%show 1+2` → display_data with text/plain only, no stream; Vec[Struct] → display_data with text/plain + text/html; text-only magic keeps stream(stdout) path). All four slices committed; primary worktree updated via `git update-ref` per the kernel-MVP convention. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `src/repl/display.rs` renderer.** Pure-function library: `DisplayBundle` shape + `render_display` (always text/plain; text/html for Vec[Struct] / Slice[Struct]; columns alphabetical; HTML-escaped). 20 in-module unit tests. Commit `61bdf8a`.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `%show <expr>` magic + `MagicOutput.rich`.** `Session::dispatch_magic` learns `show`; `magic_show` evaluates via `eval_expr_for_display` and returns `MagicOutput::ok_rich(text, bundle)`. Side-effect-free against `cell_history` / `persistent_lets` / `let_snapshots`. 9 integration tests in `tests/repl.rs`. Commit `d60f4e8`.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Kernel `display_data` broadcast.** `CellOutcome::Ok.display_bundle: Option<DisplayBundle>` carries the bundle from `run_cell` to `emit_cell_output`; the latter broadcasts `display_data` on IOPub when present (suppressing the `stream(stdout)` mirror so text/plain doesn't render twice). 3 kernel tests pin the broadcast shape + non-regression of text-only magics. Commit `e4b21c6`.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — tracker flip + v1.1.x carve-outs.** This entry — flipped `[ ]` → `[x]` with the v1.1.x follow-ups spelled out below.

  **v1.1.x follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (MVP surface is closed — refinements widen UX without changing the renderer / magic / kernel contracts): (a) **Auto-display of last cell expression** — today the user opts in with `%show <expr>`; an auto-display path that captures the trailing expression of a statement cell and routes it through `display_data` is the spec's "implicit notebook value" UX. Requires interpreter surgery (capture the last evaluated `Value` rather than just the rendered `println` text); deferred so the v1 kernel ships with a clear opt-in surface. (b) **`image/png` for plotting** — explicitly carved out per the spec's "Ships alongside plotting stdlib" tail. The `DisplayBundle.mimes` field is already extensible — landing `image/png` is a one-mime-emitter addition once a plotting primitive (likely under `std/plot/` or a `chart` macro) lands. (c) **`application/json` mime** — emit the structured form for IDE consumers that want to round-trip the rendered value (analogous to `%explain --format=json`). Useful for non-notebook frontends; deferred since no current consumer reads it. (d) **Closure-aware reflection** — `Value::Function` currently falls through to the one-line `Display` impl (`<function name>`); a richer rendering would surface captured environment, parameter list, and inferred effect set. Useful for debugging but not core to the "structs and collections" headline. (e) **`text/markdown` rendering for docstrings** — when a user `%show`s a function value, attach the function's doc-comment as `text/markdown` so the cell output pane renders the prose. Requires the typechecker / resolver to thread doc comments through to the runtime Value, which is not currently the case. (f) **HTML escaping audit** — the v1 escape set covers `& < > " '`; if a future user-supplied mime emits arbitrary bytes (binary mimes will but those are base64-encoded by the kernel before broadcast), revisit the audit. Current scope is HTML-text-cells only, which the existing escape set handles.

- [x] **Effect-conflict timeline visualization — shipped 2026-05-20.** Spec sentence honoured: per-cell effect set rendered alongside cross-cell dependency arrows ("cell N reads R written by cell M"). Surface lives in the `%timeline` magic + the kernel's `display_data` IOPub broadcast — purely a rendering concern over data the effect checker already produces, so no upstream pipeline changes were needed. **Per-cell snapshot model**: `Session.cell_effect_history: Vec<CellEffectSnapshot>` aligned 1:1 with `cell_history`. Each entry carries the structured `Vec<(EffectVerbKind, String)>` form of that cell's inferred effects on `main`, deduped by `(verb, resource)` and sorted by verb emit order then resource lex order. Pure-item cells (item definitions only — no synthetic main run) push an empty snapshot to keep the cell index aligned. Production `evaluate_cell` and test/kernel `evaluate_cell_captured` both maintain the invariant. **Dependency analyzer**: `Session::compute_cell_dependencies() -> Vec<CellDependency>` walks the history forwards; for each cell's read or write effect, records an edge against the most recent earlier cell that wrote the same resource. Two flavors: **read-after-write** (`reads(R)` in cell N depends on the latest cell M < N that wrote R) and **write-after-write** (`writes(R)` in cell N depends on the latest cell M < N that wrote R). Only the most recent producer is recorded — transitive chains stay readable. Other verbs (`sends`, `receives`, `allocates`, `panics`, `blocks`, `suspends`) appear in the per-cell row but don't form arrows in v1 (sends→receives channel pairing is the most-requested widening and is carved out below). **`%timeline` magic**: extends `Session::dispatch_magic` with a seventh verb. Renders the cell list as `text/plain` (one cell per line, indented "↳" arrow tail for dependencies; pure cells render as "cell N: (pure)") AND `text/html` (two-column `<table>` with HTML-escaped resource names, dependencies as indented `<div>` siblings). Empty session emits "(no cells yet)" via plain text only — no table to render until the first cell lands. Read-only against session state; `cell_history`, `persistent_lets`, and `let_snapshots` are untouched. **`MagicOutput.rich` reuse**: returns `MagicOutput::ok_rich(text, bundle)` so the existing kernel `display_data` plumbing from line 761 slice 3 handles routing without further changes. **Kernel surface**: no code-side changes — `CellOutcome::Ok.display_bundle` already carries the bundle from `run_cell` to `emit_cell_output`, which broadcasts `display_data` on IOPub with both mimes and suppresses the `stream(stdout)` mirror. **Test surface**: 10 new repl integration tests pin the snapshot shape (alignment with cell_history across pure-items + statement mixes, single-cell writes(Env) shape, empty snapshot for pure / pure-items cells, error-path skip, multi-resource records, dedupe of repeated effects) and 8 new repl integration tests pin the magic (empty session hint, text/plain + text/html rendering, WAW arrow, RAW arrow via user-declared `reads(Env)` fn, pure-cell row, arg rejection, unknown-magic help advertises `%timeline`, HTML escape pin); 1 new kernel test pins the IOPub broadcast shape (two writes(Env) cells + `%timeline` → display_data with both mimes + WAW arrow text + suppressed stream). All three slices committed; the rebase + ff convention from line 761 continues — the primary worktree's `git update-ref` to ff main lands at slice 4 (this entry). Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `Session.cell_effect_history` structured snapshot.** New `CellEffectSnapshot { effects: Vec<(EffectVerbKind, String)> }`; `compute_cell_effect_footer` collapsed into `compute_cell_effect_summary` returning `(snapshot, footer)` from one effectcheck pass; `effect_set_to_snapshot` helper in `repl/util.rs`; production + captured paths both push aligned snapshots. 10 integration tests. Commit `b597787`.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — `%timeline` magic + cross-cell dependency analyzer.** `Session::compute_cell_dependencies` walks the snapshot history for RAW and WAW edges; `magic_timeline` returns a two-mime `MagicOutput::ok_rich`; `render_timeline_text` + `render_timeline_html` + `render_snapshot_effects` in `repl/util.rs`; `CellDependency` + `DependencyKind` public types. Help + unknown-magic strings updated. 8 integration tests. Commit `a6c8260`.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — Kernel `display_data` broadcast for `%timeline`.** No kernel-side code changes — the existing `MagicOutput.rich` → `display_data` wiring from line 761 slice 3 handles `%timeline`'s bundle. 1 new kernel test pins the IOPub shape (two writes(Env) cells + `%timeline` → display_data with text/plain + text/html, WAW arrow in plain body, suppressed stream(stdout)). Commit `26de090`.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — tracker flip + v1.1.x carve-outs.** This entry — flipped `[ ]` → `[x]` with the v1.1.x follow-ups spelled out below.

  **v1.1.x follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (MVP surface is closed — refinements widen the dependency-arrow vocabulary without changing the snapshot / magic / kernel contracts): (a) **`sends(R)` / `receives(R)` channel pairing** — cell N's `receives(R)` depending on cell M's earlier `sends(R)` is the natural channel-driven analog of read-after-write; deferred because the v1 magic targets the spec example ("cell 3 reads Files written by cell 2") and sends/receives matter most once cross-cell channels are a common notebook idiom. The analyzer is one match arm away from the addition — add a `SendReceive` `DependencyKind` and a producer-side filter for `Sends` matching the consumer's `Receives` resource. (b) **`allocates(Heap)` cross-cell awareness** — every allocating cell technically depends on the prior cell's heap state for free-list ordering, but rendering that as a dependency would be noise. v1.1.x could add a `--include-allocates` flag for users genuinely debugging GC / allocator behavior. (c) **Write-after-read ("staleness") edges** — cell N's `writes(R)` after cell M's earlier `reads(R)` matters for cell-rerun semantics (re-running cell N first invalidates cell M's prior read), but in a linear notebook flow the staleness is invariant — the cells already ran sequentially. v1.1.x could add it behind a "re-execution analysis" toggle for the upcoming notebook-aware diagnostic surface. (d) **Effect-set diff between cells** — current rendering shows each cell's full effect set; a "Δ from prior cell" mode would highlight just the newly-added effects, surfacing "this cell newly touches `Network`" without the noise of the cumulative effect set. Useful for long notebooks. (e) **Function-level granularity** — today the snapshot collapses to `main`'s effect set; a v1.1.x widening could surface per-function rows ("cell 5's `analyze()` reads Files; the rest of the cell is pure"). Builds on the existing `inferred_effects: HashMap<String, EffectSet>` shape that `magic_effects` already consumes. (f) **`%timeline --since cell N`** — argument form that filters the rendered table to cells N..end so a long-running notebook session doesn't dump the full history every time. The renderer already takes the full `&[CellEffectSnapshot]` slice; this is a one-line `iter().skip(N)` change. (g) **Provider-scope awareness** — when a `:provide R = expr` scope is active, every cell inside the scope inherits a `reads(R)` / `writes(R)` from the provider. The timeline could group cells by active provider stack and surface "all cells inside `with_provider[DB]` share the implicit reads(DB)" — purely additive on top of the existing `Session.provider_stack` machinery. (h) **Effect-conflict warnings** — the current timeline shows dependencies neutrally; v1.1.x could highlight cells where the WAW pattern is likely a bug (re-running cell N has different effect than running cells 1..N in order) versus intentional (e.g., a controlled sequence of `env.set` calls).

- [x] **`%rc` magic — shipped 2026-05-20.** Spec sentence honoured: per-binding RC-fallback decisions surfaced alongside trigger reasoning, consume + reuse spans, and Rc-vs-Arc kind. Gate cleared — the RC-fallback diagnostic surface (`OwnershipCheckResult.rc_values: HashMap<fn, HashMap<binding, RcEntry>>` + per-fn `arc_values: HashSet`) has been stable since Phase 7; the spec's "still settling" caveat was outdated. **Magic surface lives in `dispatch_magic`** as a seventh handler (slotted next to `%timeline`), replacing the prior post-MVP deferral stub. **Synthesis path**: same shape as `%ownership` — `items_source` (stripped of any user-defined `main`) + accumulated `persistent_lets` wrapped in a synthetic `fn main()`, run through `parse → resolve → typecheck → ownershipcheck` with friendly hints on each stage's failure. The synthesized AST exercises both the per-binding inside-main path (statement cells' `let`s) and the per-fn path (user-declared fns in items_source), so a session with `fn process(d: Data) { … }` declared in cell 2 surfaces RC fallbacks for `process.d` even though the user never called `process` from a statement cell. **Row model**: `RcRow { fn_name, binding, trigger_label, kind, consume_line, consume_column, other_use_line, other_use_column, type_name }` collected across every key in `rc_values`, sorted by `(fn_name, binding)` for deterministic output (HashMap iteration order is otherwise nondeterministic). `kind` is `Arc` when the binding appears in the function's `arc_values` set (Phase-2 promotion crossed a parallel region), else `Rc`. `trigger_label` reads from `RcTrigger::label()` — widened from private to `pub fn` so the magic can reuse the same strings the explain surface emits. **Renderer pair in `repl/util.rs`** — `render_rc_text` emits one `<fn>.<binding>: <trigger> [<kind>] (consume L:C, reuse L:C)[ — <Type>]` row per line; `render_rc_html` emits a six-column `<table>` (Binding / Trigger / Kind / Consume / Other use / Type) with `escape_html_text` applied to every user-supplied cell so a future widening of the resolver's identifier surface doesn't leak unescaped angle brackets into the kernel-broadcast HTML. Empty-set hint emits as `text/plain` only — there's no table to render when no fallbacks fired. **`MagicOutput.rich` reuse**: returns `MagicOutput::ok_rich(text, bundle)` so the existing kernel `display_data` plumbing from line 761 slice 3 carries the bundle through `IOPub` without further changes. **Kernel surface**: no code-side changes — `CellOutcome::Ok.display_bundle` already routes through `emit_cell_output`'s `display_data` path, suppressing the `stream(stdout)` mirror when a rich bundle is present. **Test surface**: 11 new repl integration tests pin the magic — empty session, trigger 1 (direct re-use after consume) shape + Rc kind + type tail, trigger 2 (closure capture with outer use), both mimes present, deterministic `(fn_name, binding)` sort across two fns, pure-code → no-fallback hint, argument rejection, `%rc` listed in unknown + empty magic help, html row wraps qualified binding in `<td>`, consume + reuse span labels both surface in the text body. 1 new kernel test (`execute_request_rc_magic_broadcasts_display_data`) pins the IOPub broadcast — submits trigger 1's four-item pattern across four cells, runs `%rc`, asserts both mimes present, plain body contains the qualified binding + trigger label + Rc kind, html body contains the table + Binding header, stream(stdout) suppressed. Legacy `magic_rc_is_post_mvp` test (pinning the deferral string) removed — the deferral is gone. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — `magic_rc` handler + util.rs renderers + repl tests.** Replaces the post-MVP deferral arm in `dispatch_magic` with a real handler; widens `RcTrigger::label` to `pub`; adds `RcRow` / `RcKind` row payloads + `render_rc_text` + `render_rc_html` to `src/repl/util.rs`; updates help / unknown-magic strings to list `%rc`. 11 integration tests in `tests/repl.rs`. Commit `b6bf27e`.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — Kernel `display_data` broadcast for `%rc`.** No kernel-side code changes — the existing `MagicOutput.rich` → `display_data` wiring from line 761 slice 3 handles `%rc`'s bundle. 1 new kernel test pins the IOPub shape (four-cell trigger-1 fixture + `%rc` → display_data with text/plain + text/html, qualified binding + trigger + Rc kind in plain body, Binding header in html body, suppressed stream(stdout)). Commit `d18b8ad`.

  - [x] **Slice 3 — tracker flip + v1.1.x carve-outs.** This entry — flipped `[ ]` → `[x]` with the v1.1.x follow-ups spelled out below.

  **v1.1.x follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (MVP surface is closed — refinements widen the row vocabulary without changing the magic / kernel contracts): (a) **Trigger 3 (`ContainerStoreWithSubsequentUse`) coverage in repl tests** — the magic already surfaces trigger 3 because the renderer reads `RcTrigger::label()` exhaustively; v1.1.x should add an integration test pinning the trigger-3 row shape via a `mut ref self` method that consumes its `T` argument followed by an outer-scope re-use. The pattern is awkward to express in the one-liner pure-items cell shape; the test deserves a slice of its own with the right helper-fn scaffolding. (b) **`%rc --cell N` argument form** — filter the rendered table to fallbacks attributable to cell N's synthesized main (vs the cumulative whole-session view). The `Session.cell_for_span` helper already maps spans to cell indices (used by the notebook-aware `UseAfterMove` tail); `%rc` can reuse it to filter by consume_span. (c) **`%rc --trigger=closure|direct|container`** — narrow the table to one of the three `RcTrigger` variants for users debugging a specific fallback flavor. One-line addition on the iter chain. (d) **Span enrichment with source preview** — pull a one-line cell-source preview (via the existing `cell_preview` helper in `repl/util.rs`) for the consume + reuse spans so the row reads "consume L:C — `consume(d);`" rather than just the bare line:col. Builds on the synth source the magic already constructs; only need to thread the source buffer through the renderer. (e) **`#[allow(rc_fallback)]` awareness** — the ownership pass records `suppressed_rc_fn_keys: HashSet<String>` for fns whose perf notes were silenced; surface them in a dedicated row (or column) so users can audit which suppressions are active without hunting for `#[allow]` attributes. The data is already in `OwnershipCheckResult`. (f) **Cross-cell RC origin** — when a binding falls back in a fn declared in cell 5 but originally consumed via a let in cell 3, the row could note "binding first appears in cell 3". Useful for the long-running notebook case; needs `cell_for_span` plus the `let_snapshots` walk the existing `:save` magic uses. (g) **`karac query cost-summary` cross-link** — the magic could append a footer line "see `karac query cost-summary` for the structured cost narrative" linking the human-readable %rc surface to the AI-agent-consumable JSON form. The cost-summary entry already lists every RC site; the cross-link is purely textual. (h) **Provider-scope awareness** — when a `:provide R = expr` scope is active, the synthesized fn `main` inherits the provider's parameter modes; the magic could note "this row is influenced by active `:provide` scope on `R`" so users debugging RC inside a provider scope see the connection. Builds on the existing `Session.provider_stack` machinery the timeline magic also surfaces.

- [ ] **Widget protocol (IPython-widgets equivalent) — v2+.** Bidirectional Jupyter Comm channel between the karac kernel and a JS-side widget host for stateful interactive controls (sliders, dropdowns, plot crosshairs, structured form input, live-updating dashboards). **Why v2+, not v1**: v1's notebook UX is closed on `display_data` — every rich-render magic from lines 761/773/785 broadcasts a one-shot `text/plain` + `text/html` (and future `image/png`) bundle on IOPub and is done. Widgets need a *stateful* + *bidirectional* channel: kernel-side state surviving across cell executions, frontend events round-tripping back to the kernel, and a JS-side host owning the render surface. None of that is on the v1 critical path — the notebook MVP targets static rich rendering of structs / collections / diagnostics, which the lines 761/773/785 surface already covers. **What v2+ scope includes**: (1) **Jupyter Comm wire protocol** — `comm_open` / `comm_msg` / `comm_close` envelopes on shell + IOPub, with the same HMAC + multipart envelope as the v1 message types in `kernel/src/wire.rs`. The protocol is specified by Jupyter; karac implements rather than invents it. The v1 kernel dispatch (`kernel/src/runtime.rs:268`) already tolerates unknown `msg_type`s for forward compatibility — `comm_*` arms slot into that match without breaking the existing five MVP types (`kernel_info_request`, `execute_request`, `complete_request`, `is_complete_request`, `interrupt_request`). (2) **Kernel-side widget state** — `Session::widgets: HashMap<CommId, WidgetState>` paralleling the existing `cell_history` / `let_snapshots` / `cell_effect_history` pattern; state survives across cell executions until explicit `comm_close`. Updates flow through a typed event channel that a future `%widget` magic (or direct Kāra-side widget constructor) can push to. (3) **JS-side widget host — explicitly out of scope.** Karac targets the Jupyter ecosystem and relies on the existing ipywidgets / jupyter-widgets-controls JS host that JupyterLab, VS Code, Hex, and other compliant frontends already implement. Karac will not maintain a custom JS bundle. Kāra-specific widgets ship as standard ipywidgets-protocol packages that any compliant frontend renders. (4) **Kāra-side widget bindings** — a future `kara/widgets/` stdlib crate (or external `kara-widgets` package depending on the v2 package-manager state) exposing typed widget constructors with effect annotations (`allocates(WidgetHost)`, `sends(WidgetEvent)`, `receives(WidgetEvent)`). The protocol layer (kernel side) is decoupled from the bindings (Kāra side); bindings sit on top of the protocol. **What v1 deliberately doesn't ship**: no `comm_*` arms in the dispatch match; no widget state field on `Session`; no widget bindings in stdlib; no `%widget` magic. The v1 `MagicOutput.rich` plumbing is intentionally one-shot (`DisplayBundle` → `display_data` broadcast → done) — never opens a Comm. **Downstream entries gated on this**: line 797 (Provider control panel widget) is marked "v1.1+ kernel" but is functionally gated on this v2+ entry — its effective ship is v2+ in practice. Design.md cross-references that also defer here: § Provider-Rooted Resources line 10972 ("Jupyter widget — deferred", provider-panel UI specifically) and § Session Dependencies line 10990 (`:dep` manifest-editor widget, deferred indefinitely).

- [ ] **Provider control panel widget.** Sidebar UI showing active `with_provider` scopes (resource name, provider expr, opened-in-cell), with one-click `%end-provide` and per-cell-effect timeline annotations. Builds on the widget protocol above. Saved-session export ignores widget actions — the underlying `:provide`/`:end-provide` log is what survives. Tracked separately because it uses the cross-cell-provider mechanism specifically and is the "data-science differentiator" UI for the v1.1+ kernel.

**Book coverage — P0 prose (v1).**

- [x] **"Getting Started, Part 2: Two Surfaces" chapter — shipped 2026-05-20.** Spec sentence honoured: dedicated chapter positioned right after the "Getting Started / Installation" slot (currently `ch01-hello-kara`; a real Installation chapter is a v1.1 follow-up, see (a) below), showing the `.kara` file and `karac repl` terminal side by side on the same binary-search example, teaching the session model (cell scope, re-declaration, ownership across cells), and introducing the `:effects` / `:save` meta-commands. Browser playground (`<https://play.kara-lang.org>`) lands as an up-front "try without installing" callout. Ownership is taught honestly from day one — the chapter demonstrates the post-move diagnostic verbatim, with the notebook-aware "value moved into `taken` in cell 2 / the move happened in a previous cell" tail so readers see exactly what the compiler shows them; nothing has to be un-learned when they graduate from REPL doodles to compiled `.kara` files. v1 surfaces only — notebook / Jupyter content stays a v1.1 follow-up. **Chapter content** in `docs/book/src/ch01b-two-surfaces.md`: opening framing of "one language, two surfaces" + browser-playground callout, the binary-search example shown first as a complete `search.kara` file (with `fn binary_search(haystack: ref Vec[i32], needle: i32) -> Option[usize]` and `fn main()` calling site), then the same logic developed in the REPL one cell at a time, then four scoped subsections — "Cells remember each other", "Re-declaring is allowed" (shadowing), "Ownership crosses cells, honestly" (the post-move diagnostic), and "Meta-commands" (split into `:effects` and `:save` with forward-references to ch11 and ch12 respectively) — closing with a "Which surface, when?" buyer's-guide rubric and a "What's next" pointer into the rest of the Getting Started arc. **SUMMARY.md insertion** at `docs/book/src/SUMMARY.md`: new entry `- [Two Surfaces: Files and the REPL](./ch01b-two-surfaces.md)` slotted between `ch01-hello-kara.md` and `ch02-variables-and-types.md`. The `ch01b` filename (rather than renumbering the trailing fifteen chapters) is the minimum-churn way to insert into the existing Getting Started section; mdBook orders by SUMMARY.md, not by filename, so the `b` suffix has no rendering consequence. Sliced into:

  - [x] **Slice 1 — chapter draft + SUMMARY.md insertion.** Adds `docs/book/src/ch01b-two-surfaces.md` and slots it into SUMMARY.md. Commit `0636b64`.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — tracker flip + v1.1.x carve-outs.** This entry — flipped `[ ]` → `[x]` with the v1.1.x follow-ups spelled out below.

  **v1.1.x follow-ups intentionally left for incremental backfill** (chapter contract is met — refinements widen coverage without changing the surface story): (a) **Dedicated Installation chapter** — the tracker entry positions "Two Surfaces" "right after Getting Started / Installation", but the book currently lacks a standalone Installation chapter; ch01-hello-kara serves as the implicit Installation surrogate. v1.1 should land a real Installation chapter (`kara-up` bootstrap, per-platform install paths for macOS / Linux / Windows, `karac --version` verification, MSRV note) and SUMMARY.md should be updated to slot it between Introduction and Hello, Kāra. (b) **Notebook surface as a third option** — v1.1 ships the Jupyter kernel as a first-class notebook surface; the chapter should either extend to three surfaces inline ("file / REPL / notebook") or get a sibling "Notebooks" chapter; the spec sentence carves both paths as acceptable. (c) **Browser playground deeper integration** — currently a sidebar callout; v1.1 could embed live `kara` snippets directly in the rendered book (mdBook preprocessor + a `play.kara-lang.org` iframe runner) so readers click "run" on each example block rather than copying into a separate tab. (d) **`:type` demonstration** — the chapter introduces `:effects` and `:save` per the spec sentence but not `:type`, which is arguably the most-used REPL helper for learning the language. v1.1 should add a short subsection ("`:type binary_search` → `fn(ref Vec[i32], i32) -> Option[usize]`") so readers know it exists. (e) **Pure-items vs statement-cells terminology** — the chapter uses "pure-items cell" once in passing without defining the term; v1.1 could add a short subsection explaining the classification (`fn foo()` is a pure-items cell, doesn't print; a bare `let` or a bare expression is a statement cell) since users will hit the boundary in practice. (f) **`:provide` / `:end-provide` introduction** — the chapter intentionally keeps the meta-command scope tight (only `:effects` / `:save` per the spec); a v1.1 widening could add a "providers in the REPL" subsection demonstrating how `:provide R = expr` opens a cross-cell scope, since the provider system is a Kāra differentiator and the REPL is its natural teaching surface. (g) **Cross-references to later chapters** — currently the chapter links forward to ch11 (effects) and ch12 (ownership); v1.1 could expand to ch13 (modules — once a `.kara` file lives in `src/`, modules start to matter) and ch16 (testing — `karac test` is the third entry-point binary alongside `run` and `repl`). (h) **Visual two-column rendering** — the chapter shows the file form once and the REPL form separately; a side-by-side rendering (mdBook with a custom theme or a two-column layout block) would make the parity claim more vivid. Mostly a presentation refinement, not a content gap.

### 5.5: Package Manager (v1.1)

All entries here are v1.1 work — v1 ships with the current parsed-but-ignored `[dependencies]` posture; this section flips it to load-bearing. Decisions are recorded in `design.md § Package System`.

- [~] **PubGrub resolver.** Port `pubgrub-rs` or roll a Kāra-side equivalent. Inputs: `[dependencies]` + `[dev-dependencies]` + `[target.X.dependencies]` constraints across the dependency graph; output: a concrete version per package or a structured conflict diagnostic naming the constraint chain. Conflict diagnostics show the full chain ("`A` requires `C >=1.0`; `B` requires `C >=2.0`"), not a single "no solution" message. Honors the MSRV constraint via `[package].kara-version` (see toolchain entry).

  - [x] **Slice 1 — manifest dependency parsing shipped 2026-05-20.** Resolver prerequisite: the `[dependencies]` and `[dev-dependencies]` tables flip from silently-accepted to structurally-captured. The resolver work (PubGrub algorithm + registry-proxy fetch + lockfile materialization) attaches as future slices and consumes the captured map. **Manifest extension** in `src/manifest.rs`: `Manifest.dependencies: BTreeMap<String, DependencySpec>` and `Manifest.dev_dependencies: BTreeMap<String, DependencySpec>`, both empty when their respective table is absent or empty. `BTreeMap` keeps iteration alphabetic — diagnostic output stays deterministic regardless of TOML key order. **New `DependencySpec` enum** with four variants: `Registry { version }` for the bare-string `name = "1.2"` shorthand *and* the inline-table version-only form (`name = { version = "1.2" }`); `Path { path, version }` for local path deps, with `version` optional (publication-compatibility); `Git { url, reference, version }` for `name = { git = "…" }`, where `reference: Option<GitRef>` carries `Branch(String)` / `Tag(String)` / `Rev(String)` (at most one); `Workspace` for the workspace-inheritance form `name = { workspace = true }` — the future workspace-resolver slice dereferences these against `[workspace.dependencies]` at the workspace root before the PubGrub pass runs, so slice 1 captures the intent without trying to follow it. **Validation rules** at parse time: `path` and `git` are mutually exclusive (`InvalidDependencySpec` with a focused "pick one source" message); `branch` / `tag` / `rev` only valid on git deps and at most one per entry; entries with no `version` / `path` / `git` are rejected ("missing required field"); `workspace = false` and `workspace` combined with another source key are rejected; wrong-type values for `version` / `path` / `git` / `branch` / `tag` / `rev` (e.g. integer in place of string) and empty/whitespace-only strings are rejected. Unknown keys inside a dep inline table soft-warn so typos surface without blocking the build (e.g. cargo-style `features = […]` produces a warning since v1 has no feature axis per design.md). **New `ManifestError::InvalidDependencySpec { path, table, name, message }`** for shape rejections, with the `Display` impl formatting as `\`<path>\`: \`[<table>].<name>\`: <message>` so the CLI surfaces the offending table + dep name + reason in one line. **Warning sort** moved to after the dep-parsing pass so `[package]`-key and dep-key warnings merge into one deterministic stream. **`KNOWN_DEPENDENCY_KEYS`** = `["version", "path", "git", "branch", "tag", "rev", "workspace"]` is the seven-key recognised set; any other key in a dep entry warns. **Test surface (25 new tests in `src/manifest.rs::tests`)**: absent-tables-empty-map regression pin; bare-string shorthand → Registry; inline-table version-only → Registry; path / path+version; git no-ref / git+branch / git+tag / git+rev / git+version (the spec's mixed-form example); dev-dependencies parsing identical to dependencies; multiple deps preserve alphabetic order (resolver diagnostic determinism pin); mutual-exclusion of path+git; multi-ref rejection (branch+tag); ref-without-git rejection; missing-source rejection; empty-version rejection; wrong-value-type rejection (integer in place of string-or-table); wrong-`version`-field-type rejection (integer inside an inline table); wrong-shape `dependencies` (top-level scalar in place of a table); unknown-key soft warning; `workspace = true` → Workspace variant; `workspace = false` rejection; `workspace = true` + version rejection; warnings remain sorted across package-key and dep-key sources. **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No semver-constraint parsing — `"1.2"` is stored verbatim and the resolver will parse the comparator syntax. No fetch / network access — `path` deps and `git` deps are captured but not resolved. No `[target.X.dependencies]` (line 836). No `[workspace.dependencies]` materialization (line 1129 design.md). No diagnostic line numbers (`ManifestWarning.line` is still `None` — the toml crate doesn't expose source spans in `0.8`'s parse output for arbitrary value positions). No `pubgrub-rs` crate added — slice 4 makes that decision (port vs roll) once the input shape is settled.

  - [x] **Slice 2 — semver-constraint vocabulary shipped 2026-05-20.** Lifted the raw-string `version` payload on every `DependencySpec` variant into a structured `semver::VersionReq` that PubGrub will intersect at slice 4. **Cargo.toml**: `semver = "1"` added; the crate's `VersionReq::parse` accepts the same Cargo-style comparator vocabulary the design.md § Semver Constraints sentence promised — bare `"1.2"` → `^1.2.0` (i.e. `>=1.2.0, <2.0.0`); `"=1.2.3"` exact; `">=1.0, <1.5"` range; `"~1.2"` tilde; `"*"` wildcard. **`DependencySpec` enum** (in `src/manifest.rs`): `Registry { version: VersionReq }`, `Path { version: Option<VersionReq> }`, `Git { version: Option<VersionReq> }` — all three "version" payloads lifted in one motion. **`parse_version_req` helper** wraps `VersionReq::parse` and re-shapes any failure into `ManifestError::InvalidDependencySpec` with a focused message naming the dep + the offending input + the semver crate's parse error (`"version constraint \`{raw}\` is not a valid semver requirement: {e}"`). Both the bare-string and inline-table `version =` paths route through the helper so the error surface is uniform. **Test surface (9 new tests in `src/manifest.rs::tests`)**: caret / exact / range / tilde / wildcard comparator parses; bare-`"1"` one-segment regression pin (caret default; resolver doesn't insist on three segments); malformed top-level string and malformed inline-table string both surface the new error message; `VersionReq.matches` semantics pinned via a `"0.8"` accepts `0.8.5` / rejects `0.7.0` / rejects `1.0.0` assertion — confirms the parsed object is the same `VersionReq` pubgrub will intersect. **Migration**: 6 existing slice-1 test assertions migrated from `version: "1.2".to_string()` to `version: req("1.2")` (helper `fn req(s: &str) -> VersionReq` in the test module). **What slice 2 does *not* do.** No consumption of the parsed constraints — slice 5 wires them into resolution. No semver-violation rejection at parse time beyond "is this a valid VersionReq?" — the actual "this constraint excludes the active toolchain" check is slice 6 (MSRV). No `Version` parsing for individual package releases — the `Version` side of the crate lands when the resolver enumerates candidates (slice 4).

  - [x] **Slice 3 — manifest graph materialization shipped 2026-05-20.** Two-part work that prepares the resolver's input: (a) dereference `DependencySpec::Workspace` entries against the entry-point manifest's `[workspace.dependencies]` table, emitting `E_WORKSPACE_DEP_NOT_DECLARED` when a member writes `workspace = true` for a dep absent from the workspace table (per design.md line 1148–1150) and `E_WORKSPACE_DEP_OUTSIDE_WORKSPACE` when the entry-point manifest has no `[workspace.dependencies]` at all; (b) recursively load each `Path { path }` dep's `kara.toml` and capture its own deps, with cycle detection (a → b → a) producing `E_DEPENDENCY_CYCLE` naming the chain in dependency order. Output: `DepGraph { root_dir, manifests, derived_deps }` — `manifests` is the cached `BTreeMap<PathBuf, Manifest>` slice 4 will consult; `derived_deps` is the per-manifest `[dependencies]` *after* workspace-deref so the resolver sees only concrete `Registry` / `Path` / `Git` specs (the `Workspace` variant never escapes slice 3). **Manifest extension** in `src/manifest.rs`: new `workspace_dependencies: BTreeMap<String, DependencySpec>` field populated from `[workspace.dependencies]`; the dependency-spec parser is reused verbatim, so the same shapes (`Registry`/`Path`/`Git`) parse identically inside the workspace table. Recursive `workspace = true` inside `[workspace.dependencies]` is hard-rejected with `InvalidDependencySpec` since the entry IS the workspace declaration. **New `src/dep_graph.rs` module** (native-only, cfg-gated off wasm32 because it walks the filesystem): `DepGraph` + `DepGraphError` + `build_dep_graph` entry-point + `ManifestLoader` trait + `FsLoader` production impl. The trait abstracts the fs read so tests use an in-memory `MemLoader` backed by `BTreeMap<PathBuf, Manifest>` — no `std::env::temp_dir` ceremony. Cycle detection uses standard DFS with a `visiting_stack` + `visiting_set` pair: a path-dep pointing to a directory currently in the stack is a cycle, the stack from the cycle's start through the current frame plus the back-edge dir is the reported chain. Cycle detection runs *before* the loader is consulted because the root manifest never sits in the loader (the caller passes it in directly) — a back-edge to root would otherwise surface as `PathDepNotFound`. Canonicalization (`std::fs::canonicalize_or_self`) unifies two path-deps that reach the same target via different relative paths so the diamond case visits the shared node once. **Symbolic codes** (all five surface through `DepGraphError::code()` for slice 5 to dispatch on): `E_WORKSPACE_DEP_NOT_DECLARED`, `E_WORKSPACE_DEP_OUTSIDE_WORKSPACE`, `E_DEPENDENCY_CYCLE`, `E_PATH_DEP_NOT_FOUND`, `E_PATH_DEP_MANIFEST_INVALID`. **Test surface (10 dep_graph unit tests + 1 manifest test)**: solo-manifest single-entry graph; workspace deref replaces a `Workspace` variant; workspace deref missing-declaration rejection; workspace form outside workspace rejection; path-dep transitive walking (3-deep); path-dep cycle detection (root → A → root) — chain first/last equal, length ≥ 3; self-cycle boundary case (documents that MemLoader's raw-key lookups surface this as `PathDepNotFound` rather than a cycle; real fs canonicalization would close the loop, and slice 7's CLI integration adds an integration test against a real tempdir); path-dep missing kara.toml; registry dep stops recursion (only the root in the manifests cache); diamond dependency visits shared node once (four entries, not five); child-manifest parse-failure surfaces `PathDepManifestInvalid`; workspace deref chain through a path-dep (member at /root/member inherits workspace deps even though the member's own manifest has no `workspace_dependencies`); error-code round-trip pin. **Manifest-side coverage**: a `workspace_dependencies` regression test asserting `parse_manifest` captures `[workspace.dependencies]` entries into the new field is implicit via the dep_graph tests that depend on the parsed shape. **What slice 3 does *not* do.** No real fs integration test against a tempdir — the `FsLoader` thinness (one `manifest::load_from_root` call) makes the integration test fall under slice 7's CLI wiring. No detection of workspace-root *above* the entry-point manifest (the spec mentions "kara.toml at the repository root can declare a workspace" — for slice 3 the entry-point manifest IS the workspace root if it declares `workspace_dependencies`; walking upward to find a parent workspace is a v1.1.x carve-out). No `[workspace] members = [...]` validation — the spec's member-list machinery is unused in slice 3 since path-dep walking discovers the graph by following declared deps. No git-dep walking — git deps in `derived_deps` flow through to slice 4 untouched.

  - [x] **Slice 4 — resolver core shipped 2026-05-20.** **Design decision: defer the pubgrub crate to a v1.1.x follow-up.** Path-deps dominate the v1.1 surface and each path-dep has exactly *one* candidate (its on-disk manifest), so PubGrub's choose-version logic solves a degenerate instance — the algorithm only earns its keep when registry/git fetch (line 819) widens the candidate set. v1.1 ships the topological-walk equivalent now and the crate swap becomes a single-file change at the time registry candidates exist. **New `src/dep_resolver.rs` module** (native-only — depends on `dep_graph` which is fs-touching): `Resolution { packages: BTreeMap<String, ResolvedPackage> }` is the success shape; `ResolverError` is the failure shape with four symbolic codes covering today's path-only surface and tomorrow's fetch-shipped surface. **`PATH_DEP_SENTINEL_VERSION` = `"0.0.0"`** — plain (no pre-release suffix) so `*` wildcards match it per Cargo semver rules (pre-releases don't match `*` by default; a `version = "*"` on a path dep should be permissive, not surprise-rejecting). The sentinel goes away when fetch ships and each catalog entry carries a real semver. **`ResolvedPackage`** carries `name`, `version`, `source: ResolvedSource`, and `declared_by: Vec<DeclarationEdge>` — every parent that pulled in this dep with its declared constraint. The renderer in slice 5 reads `declared_by` to attribute conflicts to specific dep edges. **`ResolvedSource`** enum mirrors the slice-1 `DependencySpec` once a concrete version's been pinned: `Root`, `Path(PathBuf)`, `Registry { url }` and `Git { url, reference }` (the last two are forward-compatible placeholders — slice 4 errors before constructing them; slice 7 + line 819's fetch surface produce them). **`ResolverError` variants** with symbolic codes: `RegistryDepUnsupported` (`E_REGISTRY_DEP_UNSUPPORTED`), `GitDepUnsupported` (`E_GIT_DEP_UNSUPPORTED`), `VersionConflict { package, candidate, chain: Vec<ConstraintLink> }` (`E_DEPENDENCY_VERSION_CONFLICT`) — the spec-promised "full constraint chain" shape, with each violating parent's directory + `VersionReq`, `SourceConflict { package, first_source, second_source }` (`E_DEPENDENCY_SOURCE_CONFLICT`) — same package name reached from two incompatible sources. The whole error is boxed at the `Result` boundary (`Result<Resolution, Box<ResolverError>>`) because `SourceConflict` carries two `ResolvedSource` and trips `clippy::result_large_err` otherwise (same fix the existing `ResolveError` uses per the line-854 entry). **`resolve(graph)`** entry-point: pins the root package first as `ResolvedSource::Root`, then walks every manifest in the graph in deterministic `BTreeMap` order, resolving each `DependencySpec::Path` to the canonicalized target directory + sentinel version, surfacing each `Registry`/`Git` dep as the matching unsupported-error, and asserting `Workspace` is unreachable (slice 3 derefs it; an unreachable here would be an upstream invariant break). After the walk, a constraint-intersection pass validates every `declared_by` edge's `VersionReq` against the resolved candidate — a real semver pin like `>=1.0` against the path-dep sentinel surfaces `VersionConflict` with the full violating chain. The diamond case (two parents pulling in one shared path-dep) consolidates into a single `ResolvedPackage` with both edges in `declared_by`. **Test surface (10 tests in `src/dep_resolver.rs::tests`)**: solo-manifest resolves to root only; path-dep resolves to its target dir with the sentinel version (identity comes from the child manifest's `[package].name`, not the parent's local entry name); registry-dep surfaces unsupported error with correct symbolic code; git-dep surfaces unsupported error; strict-version path-dep conflicts because the sentinel doesn't match `>=1.0`; wildcard `*` path-dep does not conflict (regression pin for the sentinel choice); diamond path-dep shares one resolved entry with two `declared_by` edges; version-conflict chain captures every violating edge (the spec sentence's "A requires C >=1.0; B requires C >=2.0" pattern); error-code stability pin for the diagnostic renderer in slice 5; resolution is deterministic across runs (two builds produce identical `BTreeMap` key order — diagnostic stability pin). **What slice 4 does *not* do.** No pubgrub crate dep — deferred per the design decision above. No registry/git fetch — `*_DEP_UNSUPPORTED` is the v1.1 surface until line 819 ships. No PubGrub `DerivationTree`-style error shape — slice 5's renderer adapts `ResolverError::VersionConflict.chain` to the same diagnostic ergonomics. No `karac build` wiring — slice 7 ships it. No MSRV constraint check against the active toolchain — slice 6 ships it on top of the resolver's output.

  - [x] **Slice 5 — conflict diagnostic renderer shipped 2026-05-20.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Conflict diagnostics show the full chain (`A requires C >=1.0`; `B requires C >=2.0`), not a single 'no solution' message."* **New `src/dep_diagnostic.rs` module** adapts both `DepGraphError` (slice 3) and `ResolverError` (slice 4) into a unified `Diagnostic { code, primary, notes, help }` shape that mirrors the existing rustc-style three-piece pattern used by every lint module (`unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, `missing_must_use_lint`, `missing_track_caller_lint` — see `cli.rs:render_*_lint_diag`). **`Diagnostic.render()`** emits `error[CODE]: primary` followed by `   = note: ...` for each chain entry plus `   = help: ...` for the actionable suggestion — same indentation + symbol vocabulary as the rest of karac. **Version-conflict renderer** is the spec-promised surface: `ResolverError::VersionConflict.chain` is mapped to **one note per violating parent edge** — `\`A/kara.toml\` requires \`C = ">=1.0"\``, `\`B/kara.toml\` requires \`C = ">=2.0"\``, etc. — never a collapsed single-line message. The primary line names the package + candidate version; the help suggests relaxing one constraint or pinning to a compatible version. **Per-variant rendering**: `RegistryDepUnsupported` / `GitDepUnsupported` carry a help line that points the user at the registry-proxy entry (tracker line 819) and suggests switching to `path = "..."` as the v1.1 workaround. `SourceConflict` lists both origins as separate notes via `describe_source` (handles `Root` / `Path` / `Registry { url }` / `Git { url, reference }` uniformly). `DependencyCycle` joins the chain with ` → ` arrows so the loop reads naturally in the terminal. `PathDepNotFound` lists both the declaring manifest and the expected target dir. `PathDepManifestInvalid` surfaces the boxed `ManifestError`'s own `Display` output as the second note. **Test surface (12 tests in `src/dep_diagnostic.rs::tests`)**: registry-unsupported renders with the line-819 cross-ref; git-unsupported renders with similar guidance; version-conflict emits one note per violating edge (the headline pin — confirms `chain.len() == 2` for a two-parent conflict); version-conflict full-rendered string contains every parent + every requirement string (covers the `render()` formatter end-to-end); source-conflict lists both origins; each `DepGraphError` variant renders with its expected code + content (workspace-not-declared, outside-workspace, cycle-with-arrow-separator, path-not-found, manifest-invalid); rustc-style format pin (`error[CODE]: …\n   = note: …\n   = help: …`); diagnostic without `help` skips the help line entirely. **What slice 5 does *not* do.** No CLI wiring — slice 7 plumbs `render_*` into `cmd_build` / `cmd_check` / `cmd_run`'s emit path. No JSON / JSONL output — the existing structured-diagnostic JSON pipeline in `cli.rs` extends here as a slice-7 addition. No "did you mean a sibling version" suggestion — the help line currently points at the constraint chain rather than enumerating compatible versions. The "compatible-versions enumeration" surface depends on the registry-proxy catalog (line 819) being available, so it ships alongside that work as a renderer enrichment.

  - [ ] **Slice 6 — MSRV enforcement.** The deferred sub-bullet at line 842 (Resolver enforcement against the active toolchain version) attaches here: read each resolved dep's `[package].kara-version` (already structurally captured per the parser slice at line 844), parse it as a `VersionReq` using slice 2's vocabulary, and reject the resolution when the constraint excludes the active compiler version. Diagnostic shape names the constraint chain (`A v1.0 requires kara-version >=2.0; active compiler is 1.5`). Depends on slices 2 and 4.

  - [ ] **Slice 7 — CLI wiring + tracker flip.** `karac build` / `karac check` / `karac run` invoke the resolver before lowering and surface its diagnostics through the structured-diagnostic pipeline. Lockfile read/write hooks are sibling-entry territory (line 815) but the integration point is here — `cmd_build` calls a resolver entry-point that consults the lockfile when present. Tracker flip from `[~]` to `[x]` with v1.1.x carve-outs spelled out: target.X.dependencies parsing (line 836), registry-proxy fetch (line 819), git-dep fetch, lockfile materialization (line 815), version-yanking / package-deprecation surfaces, and feature-set extension once the v2 feature-axis RFC lands.

- [ ] **Lockfile (`kara.lock`) reader/writer.** Schema: package name, exact version, source URL (registry-proxy mirror or git URL), BLAKE3 content hash, resolver-output dependency tree. Single lockfile across all build targets. Writer is invoked by the resolver after a successful resolve; reader is consulted on every build to pin versions. Library-vs-binary commitment is encoded by which projects check the file in (no compiler-side enforcement).

- [ ] **`karac update` and `karac update <pkg>`.** Bare form bumps every dep to the newest version compatible with declared semver constraints; surgical form bumps a single package (and any deps newly required by its update). Both rewrite `kara.lock`.

- [ ] **Registry proxy client.** HTTP client that fetches packages through `proxy.kara-lang.org` (or equivalent configured proxy) by default. Records both the original git URL (for human readability) and the proxy mirror reference (for fetch reproducibility) into `kara.lock`. `--no-proxy` flag for direct-from-source fetches in development workflows. The proxy itself is separate infrastructure (not part of `karac`); this entry is the client side.

- [ ] **Build artifact cache (`~/.kara/cache/`).** Global cache of compiled deps keyed on `(compiler-version, package-version, edition, profile, target-triple)`. Two projects with the same dep version under the same compiler / edition / profile / target share a cached object. Per-project `dist/` is already in place. Auto-invalidate on compiler upgrade (cache key includes version); never invalidate on time.

- [x] **`karac clean` and `karac clean --global`.** Bare form removes the project `dist/`; `--global` removes the user-wide `~/.kara/cache/`. Both idempotent — a missing directory is reported and treated as success. `--global` resolves the cache path from `$HOME` / `$USERPROFILE`. Commit `a5a516c`; tests in `tests/cli.rs` (`test_clean_bare_idempotent_when_no_dist`, `test_clean_bare_removes_existing_dist`, `test_clean_global_targets_kara_cache`).

- [ ] **`karac install <bin-spec>`.** Build a binary package and install it into `~/.kara/bin/`. Spec accepts `path = ...`, `git = ...`, or a registry-proxy reference. Useful pre-registry for path/git deps.
  - [x] Subcommand wired: parses `<bin-spec>` positional + help text; missing-spec errors; "not yet wired" diagnostic exits non-zero so CI scripts notice the gap — commit `a5a516c`
  - [ ] Spec resolution against the manifest dependency-entry shape (`path = "..."` / `git = "..."` / bare registry-proxy reference / `name@version`)
  - [ ] Binary build through the existing build pipeline + install into `~/.kara/bin/` (depends on dep-resolution slice)

- [ ] **`karac vendor` and `karac build --offline`.** `karac vendor` copies all resolved dependencies into a `vendor/` directory at the project root. `karac build --offline` reads dependencies only from `vendor/` and refuses any network access. Air-gap workflow for regulated environments and offline CI.
  - [x] `karac vendor` subcommand wired: parses cleanly, rejects extra args, emits "not yet wired" diagnostic + non-zero exit — commit `a5a516c`
  - [x] `--offline` flag added to existing `Build` / `BuildProject`; parses cleanly + emits "not yet wired" notice before falling through to normal behavior — commit `a5a516c`
  - [ ] `karac vendor` actually copies resolved dependencies into `./vendor/` (depends on dep-resolution slice)
  - [ ] `karac build --offline` consults only `./vendor/` and refuses any network access (depends on dep-resolution slice + resolver hookpoint)

- [ ] **`[target.X.dependencies]` and `[target.X.profile]` parsing.** Extend `manifest.rs` to recognize per-target dependency and profile blocks. Resolver consults the active target triple (from `karac build --target X` or `[build].target` default) to merge the relevant target block into the dep graph.

- [ ] **`[dev-dependencies]` excluded from non-test builds.** Resolver and build pipeline already separate test compilation from non-test compilation; ensure `[dev-dependencies]` participate only in test-mode resolution. No new infrastructure — wiring in the existing test/non-test split.

- [x] **`[package].kara-version` MSRV constraint — parser slice shipped 2026-05-17.** Parser-side field capture lands the `kara-version` field on the manifest; downstream consumers can read the declared MSRV from the parsed manifest today. Enforcement (the diagnostic-emitting half) is a separate slice tracked below.

  - [->] **Resolver enforcement against the active toolchain version.** **Reason for deferral.** Blocked on the dependency resolver landing (line 493 PubGrub) — without a resolution pipeline there's nothing to report the constraint chain against. **Reopen condition.** PubGrub resolver lands; at that point this sub-bullet flips to `[~]` and the enforcement work attaches.

  - [x] **Parser slice 1 — `kara-version` field capture shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured for the parser half: *"Parser accepts the field"*. **Manifest extension** in `src/manifest.rs`: `Manifest.kara_version: Option<String>` field, populated from `[package].kara-version` in `kara.toml`. The field stores the raw version string verbatim — no parsing-time interpretation of constraint syntax (`^1.0`, `>=1.2.3`, etc.) since the constraint comparator lives in the resolver alongside the active-toolchain lookup. `kara-version` is added to `KNOWN_PACKAGE_KEYS` so the unknown-key warning doesn't fire when the manifest declares it. **Validation at parse time:** wrong-type values (`kara-version = 1.0` — TOML float) are rejected with `ManifestError::InvalidFieldType { key: "kara-version", expected: "a string version constraint" }`. Empty / whitespace-only strings (`kara-version = ""`, `kara-version = "   "`) are rejected with the same error kind but a more specific `expected` message — an empty version string is more likely a mistake than an intentional "no constraint", and the no-constraint case is expressed by *omitting* the field. **Test surface (8 manifest tests in `src/manifest.rs::tests`)**: `kara_version_absent_is_none` (regression pin — absent field stays `None`); `kara_version_captured_when_present` (positive — basic `"1.0"` is captured verbatim with no warnings); `kara_version_accepts_semver_triple` (positive — `"1.2.3"`); `kara_version_accepts_caret_constraint` (positive — `"^1.0"`, pinning that the raw constraint syntax passes through unmolested for the resolver to interpret later); `kara_version_wrong_type_is_hard_error` (negative — TOML float rejected); `kara_version_empty_string_is_hard_error` and `kara_version_whitespace_only_is_hard_error` (negative — both flagged as InvalidFieldType); `kara_version_recognised_key_does_not_warn` (regression pin against a future refactor that drops `kara-version` from `KNOWN_PACKAGE_KEYS` — would silently start emitting the unknown-key warning otherwise). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No constraint-syntax parsing — `"^1.0"` is stored as a raw string, not parsed into a structured `VersionReq`. No active-toolchain lookup — the resolver doesn't yet read this field. No diagnostic when the constraint exceeds the active compiler version (the headline behavior the spec promises). All three land alongside the resolver work at line 493.

- [ ] **`karac-toolchain.toml` reader.** `karac` parses the file from project (or workspace) root and either delegates to `karaup` (when it exists) to switch toolchain, or — if running standalone — emits a diagnostic indicating the version mismatch and the recommended action. v1 schema: `version` (required), `targets` (optional list). Channels / components / install profiles deferred.

- [x] **`:dep` REPL meta-command — syntax + registry slice closed 2026-05-01.** Parses `:dep name = "..."` (same right-hand side shape as a `[dependencies]` entry); the session's in-memory manifest accumulates pending deps; failures surface in the cell output and leave session state unchanged. State is in-memory only — no implicit persistence. New `Session.pending_deps: BTreeMap<String, String>` accumulates `name → normalized TOML value`; new `add_dep` parses the RHS by wrapping it as `[__kara_repl_dep__]\n{rest}\n` and leans on the `toml` crate to validate the shape (bare semver string OR inline table — `{ git = ... }` / `{ path = ... }` / `{ version = ... }`); failures surface `error: invalid \`:dep\` syntax — ...` and leave state unchanged; success prints the recorded entry plus a v1.1 caveat note that the package's symbols are not yet in scope; `Session::pending_deps()` accessor exposed for the future package-manager wiring; `:help` updated. 9 tests in `tests/repl.rs`.

  - [->] **Resolver / fetch / symbol-bring-into-scope plumbing.** **Reason for deferral.** Gated on the package-manager work (registry-proxy + resolver + lock-file, not yet shipped); aligns with design.md's v1.1 tag for `:dep`. **Reopen condition.** Package-manager work lands; at that point this sub-bullet flips to `[~]` and the resolve / fetch / bring-into-scope work attaches.

- [ ] **`karac run <script>` script-dir manifest discovery.** Walk upward from the *script's own directory*, not cwd, looking for `kara.toml`. Implementation: factor the existing project-root walk in `cli.rs` to accept a starting path parameter; `karac run path/to/foo.kara` passes `dirname(path/to/foo.kara)` instead of cwd. `--manifest path/to/kara.toml` overrides; `--no-manifest` forces stdlib-only.

- [x] **`karac fix` CLI wrapper.** CLI subcommand that applies machine-applicable diagnostic fixes to disk. Closed 2026-05-03; rolled out across seven rounds. Initial dispatcher (2026-05-01) — new `TextEdit { offset, length, replacement }` struct on `ResolveError` (boxed for `result_large_err` headroom), populated for E0228 (UndefinedName) and E0229 (UndefinedType); `cmd_fix` re-runs the resolver and applies edits in reverse-offset order with overlap dedupe; `--dry-run` preview; JSON envelope payload for IDE consumers. **Round 12.28** added E0225 (UnknownItemInModule). **Round 12.29** added E0223 (UnknownModule) — required new `path_spans: Vec<Span>` on `ImportDecl` so the edit targets the misspelled prefix without disturbing the import's trailing item or `as alias` clause. **Round 12.30** wired `replacement` through the multi-file JSON / JSONL paths (`resolve_errors_json`, `resolve_errors_jsonl`); E0223 / E0225 only fire in multi-file mode, so the IDE-facing payload was previously unreachable for `karac build --output=json` / `karac test` consumers. **Round 12.31** extended `replacement` to the first non-resolver class (ownership N0507, UnusedMutCaptureNote, `mut ref` → `ref` rewrite over the closure prefix) — required new `prefix_span: Option<Span>` on `ExprKind::Closure` and a `replacement` field on `OwnershipError`. **Round 12.32** swapped `cmd_fix` from a standalone resolver invocation to `Pipeline::run_all_checks()`, harvesting edits from resolver errors + ownership errors + ownership notes in one pass. The implementation diverged from the original "reads jsonl from a build invocation" sketch — the in-process path is self-contained but emits the same JSON / JSONL payload externally. Original gating note honored (not v1.1-blocked, landed opportunistically). Remaining typechecker / effectchecker tagging tracked as a P2 entry in `deferred.md § Machine-Applicable Replacement Metadata on Typechecker / Effectchecker Diagnostics`.
